Loomis Jr. and Emory Burke with violations of the Code, § 26-4902, under which "Acting as peace officer without authority" is made a misdemeanor; the terms of this section being as follows: "Any person who shall, without authority, exercise or attempt to exercise the functions of, or hold himself out to anyone as, a deputy sheriff, marshal, policeman, constable, or other peace officer or detective shall be guilty of a misdemeanor: Provided, that nothing in this Chapter shall be construed to interfere with the police powers granted to conductors of passenger trains, nor shall this and the preceding section apply in times of riot or unusual disturbance, or in other instances provided for by law." Loomis demurred to the indictment, his demurrer was overruled, and he excepted pendente lite. He also filed what he designated a "plea of double jeopardy," which the judge dismissed on an oral motion and demurrer of the State, and to this ruling Loomis again excepted pendente lite. On the trial,  [***2] the jury returned a verdict finding Loomis guilty on three of the five counts, to wit, counts 2, 4, and 5, and not guilty on counts 1 and 3. Sentences were imposed in accordance with the findings on counts 2, 4, and 5. His motion for a new trial, based on the usual general grounds, and numerous special grounds added by amendment, was overruled, and he excepted, assigning error on his exceptions pendente lite, as mentioned above, and on the refusal of a new trial.

In the bill of exceptions, which was returned to this court, it is stated: "The Supreme Court, and not the Court of Appeals, has jurisdiction hereof because questions are raised herein under the Georgia and United States Constitutions and as to the constitutionality of Georgia statutes (grounds of amended motion, 1, 4, 13, 15, 16a, 16b, 16d, 19, 31)." The following statement will indicate the general nature of these grounds, although they are mentioned here in a somewhat different order from the enumeration in the bill of exceptions.

Special ground 1 of the motion for new trial assigned error on the admission of certain testimony as to the defendant's belief in the Bible, over stated objections of the defendant.

Special [***3] ground 13 assigned as error the oath administered to the jurors trying the defendant, whereby they swore to be guided by the evidence, instead of an oath whereby they would have been sworn to be guided by the evidence and the movant's statement.

Special ground 15 assigned error on the propounding of the first of the three voir dire questions. "Have you from having seen the crime committed or having heard any of the testimony delivered on oath, formed and expressed any opinion in regard to the guilt or innocence of the prisoner at the bar?" The assignment of error was that the phrase, "alleged crime," should have been used instead of the word "crime."

Special ground 16b assigned error on the judge's charge on the subject of conspiracy.

Special ground 16d assigned error, "because the court erred in enforcing seating arrangements for counsel at counsel table, that constituted an unfair advantage for State's counsel and an unfair disadvantage for movant and his counsel and a denial of due process for movant in violation of his said constitutional right of due process."

Special ground 31 assigned error on the court's failure to grant a mistrial for allegedly improper remarks made by [***4] counsel for the State.

In each of the above six grounds, movant alleged the error therein complained of violated stated provisions of the State and Federal Constitutions; the only constitutional provisions referred to in any of these grounds being those relating to due process, freedom of conscience, and religious opinions. See Code, §§ 1-801, 1-815; Code (Ann. Supp.), §§ 2-103, 2-112, 2-113.

Special ground 4 complained because the judge, upon his own initiative, denied to movant his constitutional right actively to participate with his counsel in the conduct of his own defense by himself conducting the cross-examination of witnesses against him for the State, and particularly the witness, H. C. Newton, a detective of the City of Atlanta; the ruling of the court being that in order to avail himself of such right of cross-examination the movant would have first to dismiss his then counsel definitely from the case and forfeit any and all right to reinstall him as such counsel at any later stage of the case, although he made timely announcement of his intention to cross-examine the said witness and of his request and desire to do so immediately on the conclusion of the said witnesses's [***5] direct examination by counsel for the State, before any cross-examination of said witness had been undertaken and while said witness remained upon the stand for the purpose of cross-examination. The movant's request and attempt to exercise his said asserted right to cross-examine the said witness and other witnesses for the State, as supported and urged by himself and his counsel, who consented thereto, and the court's said ruling thereon, were as follows:

The attorney specifically invoked the provision of the Constitution, that "No person shall be deprived of the right to prosecute or defend his own cause in any of the courts of this State, in person, by attorney, or both." See Code (Ann. Supp.), § 2-104.

This ground of the motion then sets forth a lengthy colloquy, in which the judge, the defendant, and the defendant's attorney, all participated, parts of the colloquy being as follows:

The court: "I am going to rule this: Just as long as your father is your counsel and attorney representing you, only he can ask the questions. If you reach the state you have no counsel and don't desire a counsel appointed for you, I will permit you to conduct your own defense. If you reach [***6] that state I am going to give you an opportunity to select counsel."

The defendant: "I was the only one present when most of the things that have been related to the jury and the court for the last couple of days occurred, and I am the only one able to know when the truth is being told and when the truth is not being told."

The defendant: "I am the only one in position to know when the witnesses get on or off the truth or when certain points are left out in their cross-examination, in their direct examination, and it is not that I am dissatisfied with counsel, but I have to talk with him and confer with him and half the time he doesn't know what is right and what is not, and it takes up the court's time when he asks about a thing that is wrong, that is not wrong, when it was the truth, and otherwise I have to direct him --."

The court: "You have the right to confer with him any time you want to. He is your counsel."

The defendant: "Yes, I understand that, but now what I would like to know is this, if I did, it is a tremendous advantage in talking direct to the witness, now if I did take over the case, Your Honor, and cross-examine this witness from here on, then that means that [***7] when the arguments come, I must carry on with the arguments? For instance, if my father does not continue the case for me any longer through the questioning of the witnesses, can I reobtain him?"

The court: "No, sir."

The court: "I have ruled this, Mr. Loomis, and I think you as a lawyer know what the law is. With regard to the defendant representing criminal cases, the defendant has the right to come into court and defend himself. Where he selects counsel to represent him, the case is tried by counsel, he is represented by counsel, and since he has counsel, the court will only permit counsel for him to ask questions and argue the case. Now if he hasn't got counsel and doesn't want the court to appoint him a counsel, then he can conduct his own defense, but I am not going to permit a mix-up, start off by your representing him as counsel and then stop and let him step in and represent himself and then permit you to have anything further to do with the case."

Mr. Loomis: "Doesn't Your Honor in that ruling strike out the words, 'or both,' of paragraph four of section one of the Bill of Rights?"

The court: "No, sir."

Mr. Loomis: "May I ask Your Honor as a matter of information [***8] what those words are supposed to mean?"

The court: "I am not construing the Constitution now. I am simply passing on the request of your son to be permitted to act as his own counsel, and I am ruling as long as he has you as counsel you will have to represent him."

In the motion for a new trial, it is contended that the ruling of the court as above stated deprived the defendant of his right to defend his own case in person, by attorney, or both, as declared in the foregoing constitutional provision; and that the exercise by the defendant of his right of cross-examination was indispensable in this particular case (for reasons stated) for the preservation of his rights and liberties unimpaired and unprejudiced.

The defendant yet recognized his own limitations, in so far as the other phases of the case were concerned, and was, therefore, unwilling -- if there was in fact no alternative -- to pay the price of dispensing with his counsel in respect to these other matters, even in order to gain the much valued and much desired right of personal cross-examination. Still other assignments of error were contained in this ground.

Special ground 16a assigned error on a long excerpt from [***9] the court's charge referring to counts 2, 4, and 5 of the indictment, and as to each count instructing the jury that if they believed beyond a reasonable doubt that the defendant committed the offense as alleged, they would be authorized to convict him. Assignments (f) and (g) were as follows:

(f) "Because, as to each and every one of counts two, four, and five of said indictment, said section 26-4902 of the Georgia Code [is] inapplicable, because the same was unconstitutional in that it violated the due-process guaranties of both the Constitution of the State of Georgia [citing], and the Constitution of the United States of America [citing], which respectively read as follows [quoting said provisions] and which were violated by said section 26-4902 in at least two respects, viz.:

"1. In that the said statute was too vague and indefinite to define the incidence of guilt -- that is, the event or events in which the things therein denounced were prohibited and made punishable -- since it in effect provided that it made the things therein denounced be criminal and forbidden and made the same punishable as therein provided only when they were not otherwise provided for by law.

 [***10] "2. In that said statute was too vague and indefinite in defining the thing therein denounced as criminal and forbidden, and thus failed to provide any reasonable or sufficiently ascertainable standard of guilt."

(g) "Because, as to each and every one of counts two, four, and five of said indictment, said section 29-4902 of the Georgia Code was, as construed by the court, inapplicable, because, as so construed by the court, unconstitutional, since the court construed the statute as making punishable the doing of anything by a private citizen, as such, which happens also to be one of the things done by policemen in the performance of their public duties, and not as making punishable such act only when so done by one not a policeman under the claim and pretense that in so doing he was a policeman, and thus construed the statute in such a way as to make it abridge the privileges and immunities of citizens of the United States, contrary to section I of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States, supra, movant being, according to the uncontradicted proofs, a citizen of the United States and, therefore, entitled to the protection of the said constitutional guaranty."

Special ground [***11] 19 assigned error on two excerpts from the judge's charge to the jury, the first of which was as follows:

"I charge you that the police of a State, in a comprehensive sense, embraces its system of internal regulation by which it is sought not only to preserve the public order, and to prevent offenses against the State, but also to establish, for the intercourse of citizen with citizen, those rules of good manners and good neighborhood which are calculated to prevent a conflict of rights and to insure to each the uninterrupted enjoyment of his own, so far as is reasonably consistent with a like enjoyment of rights by others."

By the second excerpt, the jury were instructed that "The word 'police' is the function of that branch of the administrative machinery of the government which is charged with the preservation of public order and tranquility, promotion of public health, safety and morals, and the prevention and punishment of crimes."

The only assignments of error which undertook to raise any constitutional question in relation to either of these instructions were as follows:

"And, finally, both portions of the court's charge as quoted and complained of in this ground constitutes [***12] such a construction of the said statute, to wit, section 26-4902 of the Code of the State of Georgia, as renders the same unconstitutional, since, as so construed, the said statute violates the principle of due process as secured and guaranteed by" quoted provisions of the Constitutions of Georgia and the United States. "The statute offends against said principle of due process and said constitutional guaranties respectively, because it provides no reasonably or sufficiently ascertainable standard of guilt when construed as the court has here construed it in the charge complained of in this ground. This is the first opportunity movant has had to complain of the court's said erroneous charge and said unconstitutionality of statute as construed therein."



DISPOSITION: Transferred to Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a man alleged to have usurped police power by acting as a peace officer without authority in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 26-4902, sought review of the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which overruled his demurrer to a five-count indictment to which he excepted. He was found guilty and sentenced on three counts, and his motion for a new trial was overruled. He raised constitutional issues on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff claimed that the supreme court and not the court of appeals, had jurisdiction over the action even though a violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 26-4902 was only a misdemeanor. On review, the court found that the court of appeals had jurisdiction of actions involving mere applications of unquestioned and unambiguous provisions of the Georgia and United States Constitutions. The court found that the trial court's denial of his request to cross-examine a named witness because he was better acquainted with the facts than was his attorney was not error because the trial court had inherent power to prescribe the manner in which it conducted business without depriving him of his right to prosecute or defend his own cause. The court ruled that he could not raise for the first time on appeal the constitutionality of § 26-4902 because it formed the basis of the indictment and he should have anticipated the jury charges which he alleged were in error. The court ruled that no constitutional question was properly raised to bring the action within the court's jurisdiction, and the action was transferred.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the man's appeal of his conviction for usurpation of police power to the court of appeals after finding that he did not properly raise any constitutional issues.

 

1423 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Brunswick Peninsular Corp. v. Daugharty


No. 16085


Supreme Court of Georgia


203 Ga. 454; 47 S.E.2d 275; 1948 Ga. LEXIS 347



March 19, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Complaint for land. Before Judge Thomas. Ware Superior Court. November 10, 1947.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error corporation filed exceptions to a judgment of the Ware Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained defendant in error's general demurrer and dismissed the corporation's petition to recover two lots of land.


OVERVIEW: The Georgia General Assembly created a new county from the counties of Ware and Lowndes to be called the Clinch County. Two lots of land that were originally left in Ware County at that time were later, through 1927 Ga. Laws p. 545 (1927 Act), included in Clinch County. On exceptions to the dismissal of its petition to recover the lots, the corporation alleged that the 1927 Act was unconstitutional as being repugnant to constitutional provisions providing that laws of a general nature were to have uniform operation throughout the state. The court noted that no attack on the 1927 Act's validity was made in the trial court, and thus the court was required to assume that it was a valid and constitutional statute, and that, in view of it, the two lots of land were situated in Clinch County instead of Ware. Because cases respecting titles to land were required to be tried in the county where the land lay, the Superior Court of Ware County was without jurisdiction to try any issue respecting title to the lands.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1424 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Ellis v. Hapeville


Nos. 16047, 16049


Supreme Court of Georgia


203 Ga. 364; 47 S.E.2d 265; 1948 Ga. LEXIS 344



March 17, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equitable petitions. Before Judge Almand. Fulton Superior Court. September 20, 1947.

The facts in case 16047 are as follows:

H. D. Ellis filed a suit in equity against the City of Hapeville and named individuals as the Mayor and Council. He alleged that the act of the General Assembly approved March 28, 1947 (Ga. L. 1947, p. 1395), purporting to extend the territorial limits of the City of Hapeville, subject to a referendum, is unconstitutional and void, because notice of intention to apply for such legislation was not published once a week for three weeks during the period of sixty days immediately preceding its introduction into the General Assembly, as required by article 3, section 7, paragraph 15 of the Constitution.

With respect to the publication that was made, the petition alleged that notice was published on November 14, November 21, and November 28, 1946, but was not thereafter again published; and that the bill proposing such legislation was not introduced until March 11, 1947, so that there was no publication at all during the period of sixty days immediately preceding its introduction.

The petition further alleged: By reason of the facts above stated, the City [***2] of Hapeville and the named governing authorities are without authority to exercise any jurisdiction whatever over the additional territory, as described in the act and also in the petition. The petitioner is a resident and citizen of said territory, and he brings this action on behalf of himself and other residents of said territory similarly situated.

After the passage of said act and under the purported authority therein contained, the defendants herein named have sought to assume jurisdiction and assert control over the above described territory, and said defendants are now contending that said territory constitutes a part of the City of Hapeville and is subject to control by said city and subject to all the powers that said city may have the right to exercise over its citizens, and that the citizens of said territory are now citizens of the City of Hapeville and subject to the obligations imposed by law upon the citizens of said city. Said defendants are without legal authority to exercise dominion or control over said territory or any of the citizens thereof, and said territory is not a part of the City of Hapeville.

Unless said defendants are restrained and enjoined from [***3] so doing, they will continue to seek to exercise dominion and control over said territory, and endeavor to collect taxes from the residents thereof, to impose license fees upon the persons engaged in business in said territory, and generally to deal with the citizens of said territory as legal residents of said city.

The petitioner is without adequate remedy at law in the premises, and is entitled to the protection of a court of equity.

Wherefore, the petitioner prays: (1) that said defendants be restrained and permanently enjoined from in any manner exercising or seeking to exercise dominion, control, or supervision of the territory hereinabove described or any of the residents or citizens thereof, and from in any manner dealing with said territory as a part of the City of Hapeville; (2) for general relief; and (3) for process. (There was no allegation that the plaintiff owned property in the proposed additional territory or that he was engaged in any business therein.)

The court sustained a general demurrer and dismissed the petition, and the plaintiff excepted.

In case 16049, the facts were the same, except that in the latter case the petition was brought by a different plaintiff,  [***4] namely, K. B. Irvine.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens excepted to judgments of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) in two cases, which sustained defendant city's general demurrer and dismissed the citizens' identical petitions that sought to enjoin any further attempts by the city to exercise control over the purportedly extended territory of the city.


OVERVIEW: The citizens alleged that an act to extend the territorial limits of the city was unconstitutional and void because notice of intention to apply for such legislation was not published for the required period. The citizens alleged that the city was seeking to assume jurisdiction and assert control over such territory, and unless restrained and enjoined it would continue to seek to exercise dominion and control over the territory. The court determined that these allegations were not sufficient to show impending injury to person or property of either citizen because it was not shown that either owned property in such territory or that his personal or property rights were affected. Even as to a plaintiff who was a taxpayer, a court of equity would not enjoin an ultra vires act of municipal authorities that could not have injured the taxpayer. The petitions did not allege sufficient facts to authorize even an apprehension of injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1425 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Aldridge v. Federal Land Bank


No. 16061


Supreme Court of Georgia


203 Ga. 285; 46 S.E.2d 578; 1948 Ga. LEXIS 311



February 10, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment. Before Judge Thomas. Bacon Superior Court. October 11, 1947.

Federal Land Bank of Columbia filed in the Superior Court of Bacon County, Georgia, a petition against B. H. Aldridge, as tax collector of the said county, and Glenn S. Phillips, as State Revenue Commissioner of the State of Georgia, alleging the following: The petitioner has outstanding a large number of loans in various counties of this State, which are secured by liens on farm lands. In 1934 it made a loan to G. A. Carter on the security of 206 acres, more or less, of lots of land Nos. 81, 104 and 105 in the fifth land district of Bacon County, and took from him a deed to secure the said loan, the deed being duly recorded, and the loan being still outstanding. The said Carter failed to pay the county ad valorem tax on the said land for the year 1945, and an execution for such tax and for ad valorem taxes on personal property owned and returned by him was issued by the defendant, B. H. Aldridge, as tax collector, and is outstanding and unsatisfied, constituting a lien against the petitioner's security, and it may be levied at any time on the said security and the security be offered for sale [***2] to enforce the said execution. The amount of the ad valorem tax assessed against the petitioner's security is $ 9, and the amount of the ad valorem tax assessed against the said personal property of G. A. Carter, included in the execution aforesaid, is $ 43.06. The petitioner has offered to pay the tax on its security with interest to date of payment and a release fee of fifty cents. Such offer was made to B. H. Aldridge, as tax collector of Bacon County, with the understanding that upon payment of the tax it would be his duty to issue a receipt showing such payment and to execute a release of the land from the lien of the execution aforesaid. The said Aldridge, as tax collector, has refused to accept payment of the tax on the land aforesaid, with interest and the release fee, on the ground that no other real estate is returned and assessed by or against G. A. Carter with the land on which the petitioner holds a lien, and that the petitioner is without legal right to pay the tax on said land and have the same released from the execution without also paying the tax on the personal property returned by G. A. Carter and included in the execution; the said Aldridge, as tax collector,  [***3] asserting that he is acting under the authority and direction of the State Revenue Commissioner who, acting through his agent, B. E. Thrasher, Chief Clerk of the Property and License Tax Unit of the Department of Revenue, has advised him, in substance, that he can refuse to issue a release under the offer as made by the petitioner. The petitioner is advised and believes that it has a legal right to pay the tax on its security and have it released from the execution without also paying the tax on the personal property, and its effort to do so and the refusal of B. H. Aldridge, as tax collector, to accept the payment offered and to release the land from the execution constitute an actual controversy as to which the petitioner is entitled to a declaratory judgment by the court. The controversy involves uncertainty and insecurity with respect to the rights of the petitioner arising out of a large number of its loans in various counties of this State. The prayers were: (1) For process; (2) that the court render judgment declaring that the petitioner has a right to pay the tax on the land hereinbefore referred to, without paying the tax on the personal property, and to have the land released [***4] from the lien of the tax execution issued against G. A. Carter, leaving it as a lien only against his personal property.

The defendants each filed demurrers on the following grounds: (1) no cause of action is set forth against the defendant; (2) the petition does not set forth an actual controversy entitling the petitioner to a declaratory judgment; (3) the petition does not set forth a cause of action for equitable relief.

The defendants also filed answers, which as amended denied that the petitioner was entitled to the relief sought, and contending that the Code, § 92-5712, upon which the petitioner relied was unconstitutional, in that it violated article 7, section 1, paragraph 1 of the Constitution (Code, Ann. Supp., § 2-5401), and the provisions of the Constitution as appearing in the Code, § 2-2401, before the 1945 amendment to the Constitution, being the same as the provisions of article 7, section 1, paragraph 1, supra, for the reason that, where a tax execution for ad valorem taxes covers only one piece, parcel, or tract of real estate, and it is shown that a release executed by the tax collector would seriously impair or extinguish the lien for taxes, it restrains the [***5] sovereign right of the State to tax as declared by the Constitution. They prayed that it be declared by the court that the tax collector did not have the right to release the real estate as sought by the petitioner; that the act of 1931 (Ga. L. 1931, p. 122) as amended by the act of 1933 (Ga. L. 1933, p. 50), codified as § 92-5712, has no application when a tax execution covers only one piece, parcel, or tract of real estate; and that the said act of 1931 as amended (Code, § 92-5712) be declared unconstitutional if applied to a release as sought by the petitioner.

When the case came on for a hearing, the defendants, on October 4, 1947, admitted that the allegations of fact in the petition were true; and it was agreed between the parties that the judge of the court hear and determine all issues in vacation without a jury. On October 11, 1947, the court rendered judgment overruling the demurrers, and declaring that the petitioner was entitled to the relief sought, the judgment being based "on the stipulation and finding that G. A. Carter returns no real estate in Bacon County other than the land covered by the plaintiff's deed to secure debt, and that no other land in Bacon County [***6] is assessed as the property of G. A. Carter."

The exception here by the defendants is to that judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant in error taxpayer brought a claim against plaintiffs in error, state and local tax authorities, which denied his request to release property upon which he held a security due to his payment of tax upon the security amount. The Bacon Superior Court (Georgia) overruled demurrers by the tax authorities and found that the taxpayer was entitled to the relief requested. The tax authorities appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tax authorities argued that the interpretation of Ga. Code Ann. § 102-103 under which relief was granted to the taxpayer was violative of Ga. Const. art. 4, § 1, para. 1 (1877) and Ga. Const. art. 7, § 1, para. 1 (1945). In support of this view the authorities urged that where, as here, a tax execution covered only one piece, parcel, or tract of real estate, and it was shown that a release thereof by the tax authorities could seriously impair or extinguish the lien for taxes, the sovereign right of the state to tax as declared by the constitution was restrained. The court found that Ga. Code Ann. § 102-103 did not have the effect claimed since it did not restrict the right to tax and in the present case assessments were made on both the real and the personal property here involved, and execution had been issued with the respective amounts of the taxes shown therein. The court found that the tax on the land on which the taxpayer had a lien was paid as fully, when the proceedings authorized by the statute have been completed, as if collected directly from the tax debtor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting the taxpayer the ability to pay the tax on the security he had in real estate and effecting a release of the property by the tax authorities.

 

1426 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Trust Co. of Georgia v. Mortgage-Bond Co.


No. 15934


Supreme Court of Georgia


203 Ga. 461; 46 S.E.2d 883; 1948 Ga. LEXIS 317



January 17, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Adhered to on Rehearing, March 20, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari; from Court of Appeals. 75 Ga. App. 211.

The present case is before this court on certiorari from the Court of Appeals. For the decision under review, see 75 Ga. App. 211 (42 S. E. 2d, 781). The action in the trial court was a proceeding by a New York corporation to revive a dormant judgment. By an amendment, it appeared that the plaintiff was suing for the use of another corporation, to which the cause of action was assigned pending the original suit in which the judgment was obtained. The amendment further disclosed that the corporation was voluntarily dissolved after institution of the proceeding for revival; whereupon the trial court sustained a demurrer and dismissed the action. The main question in the case is whether the action abated on dissolution of the plaintiff, as a corporate entity, and involves a determination as to whether section 36 of the Corporation Act of 1938, providing for continued existence of "all corporations" for the term of three years after their dissolution and until final disposition of all suits begun within that time, for the purpose of prosecuting and defending suits by or against them,  [***2] and other purposes, applies to foreign corporations. The Court of Appeals held that these provisions apply alike to foreign and domestic corporations, and reversed the judgment of the trial court. The petition as amended did not show whether the corporation had ever been engaged in business in Georgia.

The facts of the case, as stated in detail by the Court of Appeals, were as follows: On May 22, 1945, The Mortgage-Bond Company of New York filed a petition for scire facias to revive a judgment obtained by it on January 7, 1936, in Fulton Superior Court against W. H. Wynne, States Realty Company Inc., and Wynndam Court Apartment Company Inc. It was alleged that said judgment was more than seven years old and was dormant, and that no part of the debt for which said judgment was rendered had been paid except $ 1000, realized from the sale of certain property levied on and sold in February, 1936, under the fi. fa. issued on said judgment, which amount had been credited thereon. It was alleged that W. H. Wynne had died testate after the rendition of the judgment and the issuance of the fi. fa., and under his will, which had been probated, Trust Company of Georgia was named as executor [***3] and trustee and had qualified as such more than 12 months before the filing of the petition. The petition prayed that scire facias issue and be served upon Trust Company of Georgia, as executor and trustee of the said W. H. Wynne; that it be required to show cause why it should not be made a party defendant in the case; that service likewise be made upon the other defendants; and that all of the defendants be required to show cause why said judgment should not be revived.

In amendments to the petition for scire facias, it was alleged that The Mortgage-Bond Company, the original plaintiff, had sold, conveyed, transferred, assigned, and delivered on October 21, 1935, to Mortbon Corporation of New York all of its assets and property (except its corporation franchise and name), with all "privileges and appurtenances whatsoever thereunto belonging," subject to certain conditions not material to this case; that under said assignment the notes evidencing the indebtedness on which said original judgment was issued became the property of Mortbon Corporation; and that after the date of said assignment the latter corporation had exclusive custody and control over said notes, and upon the rendition [***4] of said judgment said corporation assumed exclusive custody and control over said judgment and the execution issued thereon. It was also alleged in the amendments that, notwithstanding said transfer and assignment, which was made after the filing of the original petition in the suit on the notes and before the judgment was obtained therein, Mortbon Corporation allowed and permitted the case to proceed in the name of the assignor, and allowed and permitted the judgment to be taken in the name of said assignor, but that said corporation was the owner and holder for a valuable consideration of the notes on which the judgment was obtained and the indebtedness represented by them, after October 21, 1935 (the date of the assignment), and was the beneficial and equitable owner and holder of the judgment and the execution issued thereon at all times after the judgment was rendered and the execution was issued.

It appears from the petition that it was in fact filed by Mortbon Corporation, although it was filed in the name of The Mortgage-Bond Company; and that on June 30, 1945, after the filing of the petition, the name of Mortbon Corporation was changed to Telfair Stockton & Company Inc.,  [***5] and the petition prayed that the action proceed in the name of the plaintiff for the use of Telfair Stockton & Company Inc. It also appears that on June 4, 1945, while the petition for scire facias to revive said dormant judgment was pending, the charter of the plaintiff, The Mortgage-Bond Company, was dissolved under a voluntary proceeding in the Supreme Court of the State of New York. It was then alleged that, "notwithstanding the dissolution of said charter, the present owner and holder of the beneficial and equitable interest in said dormant judgment, to wit, Telfair Stockton & Company Inc., is under the laws of the State of Georgia and equitable principles, entitled to have said case proceed in the name of The Mortgage-Bond Company of New York, and is, under said laws and equitable principles, entitled to have said dormant judgment revived and to have the same enforced."

Each of the defendants filed demurrers to the petition as amended as follows: (1) Said petition does not as a whole, nor do any of its parts, show a cause of action against this defendant for the revival of the judgment sought to be revived in said petition. (2) Said petition as amended shows on its face that [***6] the party plaintiff has no legal existence. The demurrers were sustained by the trial court, and the plaintiff, The Mortgage-Bond Company of New York, suing for the use of Telfair Stockton & Company Inc., excepted.

The Court of Appeals having reversed the judgment of the trial court sustaining the demurrers and dismissing the petition, the defendants in error in the Court of Appeals, namely, Trust Company of Georgia, as executor and trustee under the will of W. H. Wynne, deceased, States Realty Company Inc., and Wynndam Court Apartment Company Inc., presented to this court an application for the writ of certiorari, which application was granted.

In the motion for rehearing in the Court of Appeals, the movants, now petitioners in certiorari, averred, among other things, that the court "overlooked the fact that it does not appear in the record that at the time of its dissolution, or at any other time, The Mortgage-Bond and Trust Company [?] was engaged in business in the State of Georgia."

The petition for certiorari assigned error on the decision and judgment of the Court of Appeals upon the ground, among others, that they were illegal and contrary to law, because the court incorrectly [***7] held that section 36 applies to foreign as well as Georgia corporations.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff New York corporation sought to revive a dormant judgment that was obtained from a different corporation which had dissolved. The trial court dismissed the action. That dismissal was reversed on plaintiff's appeal to the Court of Appeals (Georgia). Defendants, realty company and apartment company, appealed the dismissal.


OVERVIEW: The corporation brought an action in the trial court to revive a dormant judgment. It was discovered that, in reality, the corporation was not the original corporation which held the judgment that was to be revived. The original corporation had assigned its rights to the corporation and had since dissolved. Defendants, realty company and apartment company, obtained dismissal of the action, the corporation appealed, and that dismissal was reversed. This appeal ensued. The court determined that the main question was whether the action had abated on dissolution of the original corporation as a corporate entity and whether § 36 of the Corporation Act of 1938 applied to foreign corporations. Under § 36, Georgia corporations continued in existence for three years after dissolution in order to prosecute or defend actions. The court found § 36 did not apply to foreign corporations. This meant the original corporation, who was a foreign corporation, did not continue in existence after its dissolution, especially since it did not conduct any business in the state. Moreover, the original action abated because the revival was not brought by the original corporation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court that reversed a dismissal by the trial court of the corporation's action to revive a dormant judgment.

 

1427 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Walker Electrical Co. v. Walton


No. 15967


Supreme Court of Georgia


203 Ga. 246; 46 S.E.2d 184; 1948 Ga. LEXIS 579



January 10, 1948, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for injunction. Before Judge Guess. DeKalb Superior Court. July 2, 1947.

Walker Electrical Company filed its verified petition in DeKalb Superior Court, alleging: H. G. Walton, the defendant, is a resident of DeKalb County. Walton has filed three cases against the plaintiff in the Civil Court of Fulton County. The issues in the three cases should be determined in one action; they constitute a single controversy. Walton divided his demands to prevent the plaintiff from setting forth its defense. (See Walker Electrical Co. v. Walton, 201 Ga. 591, 40 S. E. 2d, 523, for a statement of Walton's three suits.)

The contracts between the plaintiff and Walton involve work for the United States Government. Walton failed and refused to file certain termination claims, and the amounts claimed by Walton in his first suit are proper items of a termination claim. The defendant persisted in his refusal to file a termination claim until a stipulation was made that by so doing the defendant would not waive his right to prosecute his action and would not be bound by the termination claim. An award has been made on the termination claim, in a stated sum, and the plaintiff has offered [***2] to turn this over to the defendant in settlement of the three suits, but it has been refused. Walton's trover action involves certain machinery which is either the property of the United States or of the plaintiff, the cost of the machinery having been paid to the defendant in amounts paid him by the plaintiff.

The three cases filed by Walton involve construction contracts on the premises of the plaintiff, and construction contracts for Owens and Blum, executives of the plaintiff, the amount claimed by the defendant in the third case being the result of an audit made by auditors and the attorney for the defendant. The amount found due by such audit did not take into account counter-claims of the plaintiff which had not been put on the books of the plaintiff because they were unliquidated in amount. The defendant failed to keep records separating the material and labor chargeable to the plaintiff and that chargeable to named executives of the plaintiff, for which the plaintiff would be reimbursed by such executives. Numerous items and demands of the plaintiff against the defendant are set out.

In order to avoid a multiplicity of actions, the issues should be consolidated, and [***3] the plaintiff's petition should be maintained for the purpose of an accounting. It is alleged "on information and belief that the defendant is insolvent." The plaintiff can not obtain full and adequate relief in the Civil Court of Fulton County because it is a court of limited jurisdiction and has no equitable jurisdiction, may not appoint an auditor, and does not have jurisdiction to make an accounting between the parties.

The act approved January 31, 1946 (Ga. L. 1946, pp. 287-294), increasing the jurisdiction of the Civil Court of Fulton County, is void and of no effect for certain stated reasons. (Constitutional attacks made by the petition of the plaintiff in error, and urged by counsel in its behalf, will be discussed in the opinion.)

The prayers of the original petition were that: the bill be filed; process issue; temporary injunction be granted; an order be entered consolidating the issues involved in the three cases pending in the Civil Court of Fulton County; the case be referred to an auditor; and the plaintiff have judgment against the defendant in a stated sum.

The plaintiff filed two amendments to the petition. In the first, a further attack was made on the act [***4] increasing the jurisdiction of the Civil Court of Fulton County. By the second amendment, additional matters were set up to show that the plaintiff is entitled to recover from the defendant, it being alleged that the accounts between the parties are numerous and payrolls on various jobs must be compared, that it is impossible for a jury to pass upon the complicated facts, and that the plaintiff is entitled to discovery from the defendant of the names and addresses of employees to whom he claims he made payment of wages, and the time and place where they were employed. The plaintiff prayed that an order issue directing the defendant to make the records described available to it.

The general demurrer to the petition was sustained and the case dismissed. The exception is to that judgment.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed three cases against plaintiff in civil court. Plaintiff filed a petition for consolidation of the actions in equity. The DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) sustained defendant's demurrer to the petition and dismissed it. Plaintiff sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant brought one action based on termination claims, one in trover, and one to recover under an audit. Plaintiff claimed that the actions should be consolidated because they constituted a single controversy and because it could not obtain adequate relief due to the civil court's limited jurisdiction. The court found that 1946 Ga. Laws 287 gave the civil court concurrent jurisdiction with the superior courts, did not contain any restriction as to cases pending on its effective date, and gave sufficient publication of notice as required by Ga. Const. art. III, § 7, par. 15 (1945). Thus, the court held that the civil court had full jurisdiction to determine all issues between the parties in the pending cases, including any defenses filed or amended by plaintiff. The court also held that under Ga. Code Ann. § 3-113, defendant's claims could not be joined in the same action because two arose ex contractu and one ex delicto. Furthermore, the petition did not make a cause for consolidation of actions in equity because there was no showing that the multiplicity of suits would render a trial difficult, expensive, and unsatisfactory at law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed plaintiff's petition for an injunction to compel consolidation of defendant's civil court claims against it.

Dep't of Human Res. v. W.


A99A2159.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


241 Ga. App. 677; 527 S.E.2d 280; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 1690; 2000 Fulton County D. Rep. 438



December 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Civil rights action. Rockdale Superior Court. Before Judge Nation.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Rockdale County (Georgia), which awarded attorney fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 in respondent's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 civil rights action challenging the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 19-11-9.3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the state human resources agency which mailed notice to plaintiff that it would suspend plaintiff's driver's license if he failed to pay child support arrearages. Defendant later suspended the license. Plaintiff sought declaratory judgment requesting that Ga. Code Ann. § 19-11-9.3, which provided the notice requirements, be declared unconstitutional. Plaintiff brought the action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and requested attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. Defendant appealed an award of attorney fees. The court reversed the award of attorney fees, finding that plaintiff was not the prevailing party. Plaintiff received no relief because the statute had been found to be constitutional and the suspension of plaintiff's license remained pending throughout the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The judgment awarding attorney fees was reversed because plaintiff received no relief and was not the prevailing party in the civil rights action.

 

1429 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Brabham v. State


A99A2059.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


240 Ga. App. 506; 524 S.E.2d 1; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 1391; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3895



October 21, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Armed robbery, etc. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Karpf.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia) finding him guilty on a jury verdict of armed robbery and false imprisonment, and sentencing him as a recidivist.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of armed robbery, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-8-41(a), and false imprisonment, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-41(a), and was sentenced as a recidivist. On appeal, the court affirmed. Entering a pharmacy with a black plastic bag over his hand and telling the victim he had a gun was sufficient to establish the use of an offensive weapon, even though the victim did not see an actual gun and no gun was recovered. The evidence was sufficient to support the false imprisonment conviction where the victim testified that appellant forced him at gunpoint to sit on the floor of the pharmacy and remain there. Application of the recidivist statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7, did not violate the Separation of Powers doctrine, Ga. Const. art. II, § 1, para. 3, because the power to create and prescribe punishment for crimes was legislative in nature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, holding that there was sufficient evidence to establish use of an offensive weapon where appellant had a bag over his hand and claimed he had a gun, that forcing victim to remain on floor at gunpoint established false imprisonment, and that the recidivist statute was not unconstitutional.

 

1430 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Dester v. Dester


A99A0930. A99A0931.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA, THIRD DIVISION


240 Ga. App. 711; 523 S.E.2d 635; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 1476; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3885



October 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsiderations Denied November 8, 1999. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied March 3, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ga. LEXIS 225.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Effingham Superior Court. Before Judge Martin.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. A99A0930. Judgment reversed in Case No. A99A0931.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed a judgment of the Effingham Superior Court (Georgia) granting summary judgment to defendant husband on the ground of interspousal tort immunity. Defendant employer cross-appealed the same court's denial of its summary judgment motion on plaintiff's claims of respondeat superior, negligent entrustment, and negligent hiring and retention of defendant husband.


OVERVIEW: Defendant husband was driving plaintiff wife and the rest of his family home from dinner in a truck owned by defendant employer when the truck was involved in an accident. Defendant husband had consumed several beers earlier in the day and had two margaritas at dinner. Plaintiff was seriously injured. The trial court granted summary judgment to defendant husband and denied summary judgment to defendant employer. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment in part, holding that the interspousal tort immunity doctrine prohibited plaintiff from suing defendant husband for personal injuries. The court reversed the judgment in part, holding that defendant employer was not liable to plaintiff because defendant husband was not acting within the course and scope of his employment at the time of the accident. Defendant husband was not on call, and defendant employer had no actual knowledge that defendant husband was drinking and driving the evening of the collision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to defendant husband. The interspousal tort immunity doctrine precluded plaintiff wife from bringing a personal injury suit against defendant husband. The judgment was reversed as to defendant employer, because defendant husband was not acting within the scope of his employment when he wrecked defendant employer's truck.

Hall v. State


A99A2284.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


240 Ga. App. 356; 523 S.E.2d 409; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 1346; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3756



October 14, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Robbery, etc. Troup Superior Court. Before Judge Keeble.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of robbery and obstruction of an officer in the Troup Superior Court. Defendant appealed to the Supreme Court of Georgia after the denial of his motion for new trial. The Supreme Court later transferred the appeal to this court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of robbery and obstruction of an officer. The court found that evidence was sufficient to authorize the jury's finding of guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. After reviewing the State's reasons for exercising its peremptory strikes, the court found the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding the State's explanations race-neutral. Defendant was in prison nearly 14 months prior to trial, and claimed he was denied his right to speedy trial. Balancing all four factors under the Barker test, the court concluded that the almost 14-month delay in the case sub judice did not violate defendant's constitutional right to a fair and speedy trial.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed because evidence was sufficient, trial court did not abuse its discretion in accepting State's reasons for peremptory strikes, and almost 14-month delay did not violate defendant's right to speedy trial.

 

1432 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Stewart v. State


A00A0183, A00A0184.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


240 Ga. App. 154; 522 S.E.2d 743; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 1249; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3589



September 24, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to dismiss indictments. Bryan Superior Court (case no. A00A0183). Tattnall Superior Court (case no. A00A0184). Before Judge Harvey.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial of his motions to dismiss two separate indictments filed against him in two different Superior Courts for failing to maintain funds from pre-need funeral service contracts unimpaired in an authorized state bank as required under Ga. Code Ann. § 43-18-96.


OVERVIEW: Defendant failed to maintain funds from pre-need funeral service contracts unimpaired in an authorized state bank as required under Ga. Code Ann. § 43-18-96. Accordingly, defendant was charged with unlawful disposition of proceeds received from pre-need funeral service contracts in separate indictments in two different counties. Defendant moved to dismiss the indictments, contending the statute under which he was charged was unconstitutional. Both county Superior Courts denied the motions. Defendant appealed to Georgia's Supreme Court, which transferred the cases to the Court of Appeals, after finding that its subject matter jurisdiction had not been invoked. The appeals court held that it was without jurisdiction to consider the merits of the direct appeals because the denial of the motions were not directly appealable under Ga. Code Ann. § 5-6-34(a)(1), but were only appealable as interlocutory orders or after a conviction. Therefore, although defendant obtained certificates of immediate review from Superior Court, he did not pursue mandatory application procedures of § 5-6-34(b) for interlocutory appeals. Thus, court was without jurisdiction, and appeals were dismissed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's appeal was dismissed because the denial of his motions to dismiss the indictments filed against him were not directly appealable, but, instead, were appealable only as interlocutory orders. Thus, the court lacked jurisdiction to review the direct appeals because defendant did not pursue the mandatory application procedures associated with interlocutory appeals and required for the court to review interlocutory appeals.

 

1433 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Shores v. State


A99A1671.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


240 Ga. App. 189; 522 S.E.2d 515; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 1197; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3465



September 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 29, 1999. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied February 25, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ga. LEXIS 196.


PRIOR HISTORY: Theft of services, etc. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Girardeau.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial of his motion for a new trial, following his convictions in the Hall Superior Court (Georgia) for theft of services and theft by taking.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of theft of services, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-8-5, and theft by taking, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-8-2. The trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial. In affirming, the court concluded that defendant, owner of a race track, was guilty of theft of services in issuing checks to winning drivers despite knowledge that there were insufficient funds in the business account to cover the checks, especially where drivers had voiced concerns about the sufficiency of funds and defendant assured them that the race track was solvent. Such evidence showed intent, and supported the verdict. Further, defendant committed the offense of theft by taking when he accepted race fuel and paid by check, but later stopped payment thereon. Defendant made no attempt to make payment or to return the fuel, which he had sold to drivers for profit.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Defendant's issuance of checks on accounts having insufficient funds, while assuring payees of business solvency, and defendant's stopping of payment on a check for racing fuel received, supported convictions for the offenses of theft of services and theft by taking.

 

1434 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Green v. State


A99A1611.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


239 Ga. App. 617; 521 S.E.2d 441; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 1050; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3142



August 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 16, 1999. Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Drug violation, etc. Bartow Superior Court. Before Judge Davis.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the Bartow Superior Court (Georgia) which found appellant guilty of possession of less than one ounce of marijuana, possession of methamphetamine, trafficking in methamphetamine, unlawful possession of fireworks, giving a false name to a law enforcement officer, making a false statement, and speeding.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped for speeding and consented to the search of his car. The search revealed cash, marijuana, and methamphetamine. Appellant was found guilty of possession of less than one ounce of marijuana, possession of methamphetamine, and related offenses. He sought review of the convictions. Appellant argued that the court erred when it denied his motion to suppress because the state failed to prove that the radar was used in accordance with law, because he was illegally detained and his vehicle was searched without proper consent, and because the evidence obtained from a diaper bag belonged to his passenger. The court affirmed. It found that the denial of the motion to suppress was proper even if the radar was not used correctly because the officer could visually detect that the appellant was speeding and was therefore authorized to make the stop. In addition, the court found that consent to the search was freely given. As to the diaper bag, appellant lacked standing to challenge the admissibility because he never asserted a possessory interest in the bag.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellant's convictions for possession of marijuana and other related offenses because the police officer was authorized to make the traffic stop and because consent to search the vehicle was freely given.

 

1435 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Lyons v. State


A99A1613.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


239 Ga. App. 325; 521 S.E.2d 232; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 1012; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3066



July 26, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DUI, etc. Whitfield Superior Court. Before Judge Boyett.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Whitfield Superior Court (Georgia), affirming a conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391 (a) (1), and weaving over the roadway in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-48. Defendant asserted that Ga. Code Ann. § 40-13-28 unconstitutionally deprived defendant of due process by requiring him to establish that a record was requested in the lower court proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in uniform traffic citations with driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391 (a) (1), and with weaving over the roadway in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-48. Defendant signed a rights and plea form, which omitted any actual guilty plea, but indicated that defendant was aware of his rights in court. The court found defendant guilty on both charges and sentenced defendant. Defendant appealed the conviction, asserting that Ga. Code Ann. § 40-13-28 unconstitutionally deprived defendant of due process by improperly placing on defendant the burden of establishing that a record was in fact requested in the lower court proceeding. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because under Ga. Code Ann. § 40-13-28, the burden remained on defendant to ensure that the record included the issue upon which he sought review, as well as the lower court's ruling on the issue, which satisfied due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol and weaving over the roadway because pursuant to state statute, the burden remained on defendant to ensure that the record included the issue upon which defendant sought review, as well as the lower court's ruling on the issue, which satisfied due process rights.

 

1436 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Burns v. State


A99A1206.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


239 Ga. App. 532; 521 S.E.2d 217; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 1005; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3059



July 23, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 6, 1999. Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Armed robbery, etc. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Bass.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentence by the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia) for armed robbery and possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony. On appeal, defendant argued that the traffic stop of his vehicle was not based on any reasonable, articulable suspicion, that his subsequent arrest was without probable cause, and that the evidence obtained during the search of his vehicle incident to his arrest should have been suppressed. The appellate court rejected defendant's contention and held that the totality of the circumstances created a justifiable suspicion concerning defendant's identity and warranted a limited investigative detention to determine if he roughly fit the description of the perpetrators. It further found that under the totality of the circumstances, the officer had sufficient probable cause to justify defendant's custodial arrest for suspicion of armed robbery and that the trial court properly denied the defendant's motion to suppress. The court also rejected defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-6.1, and it affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence for armed robbery and possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony. The court held that the traffic stop of defendant's vehicle was based on reasonable, articulable suspicion, that his subsequent arrest was with probable cause, and that the trial court properly denied his motion to suppress evidence.

 

1437 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



McBee v. State


A99A1587.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


239 Ga. App. 314; 521 S.E.2d 209; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 999; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3027



July 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Aggravated sodomy. Catoosa Superior Court. Before Judge Hill.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision by the Catoosa Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of rape and aggravated sodomy. The court had merged a sodomy charge into the aggravated sodomy conviction. Defendant moved to vacate the sodomy and aggravated sodomy charges.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of rape, aggravated sodomy, and sodomy. The trial court merged the aggravated sodomy and sodomy counts and entered judgment on the rape and aggravated sodomy counts. Defendant moved to vacate the convictions on the sodomy and aggravated sodomy charges asserting that the convictions were void under a new supreme court ruling. The trial court denied the motion and defendant appealed. The reviewing court stated that a trial court could resentence a defendant at any time if a sentence was void. The court stated the new ruling applied to simple sodomy. Thus, the ruling did not render defendant's conviction for aggravated sodomy void and the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to vacate the conviction. Although the jury had found defendant guilty of simple sodomy, the sodomy charge had been merged with the aggravated sodomy conviction. Thus, the only crimes that defendant was convicted of were rape and aggravated sodomy. Defendant's motion to vacate was denied. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of rape and aggravated sodomy. Defendant's sodomy charge had been merged with the aggravated sodomy charge. Therefore, the new supreme court ruling did not apply to defendant because the ruling only applied to sodomy, not aggravated sodomy.

 

1438 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



World Trade Bus. v. Amit, Inc.


A99A0596.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


239 Ga. App. 383; 521 S.E.2d 40; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 980; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2862



July 15, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 29, 1999. Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Price gouging. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Fryer, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tour operator appealed a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment to defendant hotel, in plaintiff's action to recover for price gouging in violation of the Olympic Anti-Price Gouging Statute, Ga. Code § 43-21-16.


OVERVIEW: Holding that as a person who had contracted to use hotel rooms, plaintiff tour operator had standing to sue defendant hotel under the Olympic Anti-Price Gouging Statute, Ga. Code § 43-21-16. The court reversed the grant of summary judgment for defendant, and vacated the judgment allowing defendant to keep plaintiff's deposit as a liquidated damage. Under the plain language of the statute, plaintiff had standing to sue, because a person who contracted to use a hotel room was not limited to the ultimate consumer or occupier of the room. The court held that the trial court's emphasis on the fact that plaintiff met the statute's definition of a hotel operator, and did not meet the definition of a guest, was misplaced. The court held that nothing in the statute indicated that it protected only guests or excluded operators from protection. The court defined "to use" as to put into service or to have recourse to, or enjoyment of. The court also noted that the contract explicitly provided plaintiff with the right to occupy the rooms. Because the court found that plaintiff had standing, it vacated the trial court's ruling that defendant could keep plaintiff's security deposit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment for defendant hotel, because plaintiff tour operator was a person who had contracted to use hotel rooms, and was entitled to the protection of the Olympic anti-gouging statute. The court held that the statute's protection extended not just to the consumer who occupied the room, but to any person who contracted to use a room, including corporate resellers like plaintiff.

 

1439 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Estep v. State


A99A0445.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


238 Ga. App. 170; 518 S.E.2d 176; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 761; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2203



May 19, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Cruelty to children. Banks Superior Court. Before Judge Adamson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Banks Superior Court (Georgia) denying her motion and amended motion for a new trial following her conviction for cruelty to children. Defendant claimed that her right to be present at trial and to confront witnesses was violated when part of the trial was conducted in her absence and that the court erred in admitting evidence that the county had previously investigated her about bruises on her son.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of cruelty to children following an investigation of her daughter's injury. The trial court denied defendant's motion and amended motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed, claiming that her right to be present at trial and to confront witnesses was violated when portions of the trial were conducted in her absence. She also claimed that the trial court erred in admitting evidence that the county previously had investigated her when bruising was noticed on her son. The court affirmed the conviction, explaining that defendant voluntarily absented herself during trial because she was free on bail, knew the proceedings had begun, and failed to attend. Further, her voluntary absence waived her right to be present when her sentence was imposed. The court further determined that defendant did not challenge the purpose for which the subject evidence was admitted at trial and therefore could not raise the issue on appeal. Finally, although defendant arguably failed to preserve the issue for appeal, the court determined that erroneous admission of a child's hearsay statements did not require reversal because the statements were merely cumulative of other evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for cruelty to children, explaining that defendant voluntarily absented herself during trial because she was free on bail, knew the proceedings had begun, and did not attend. Further, her voluntary absence waived her right to be present at sentencing. Finally, defendant failed to challenge the purpose for which certain evidence was admitted at trial and, thus, could not raise the issue on appeal.

 

1440 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Davis v. State


A99A0186.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


238 Ga. App. 84; 517 S.E.2d 808; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 730; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2127



May 13, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Child molestation, etc. Gilmer Superior Court. Before Judge Milam.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from Gilmer Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of child molestation and related offenses.


OVERVIEW: A child molestation conviction was affirmed because alleged trial errors were caused by defendant's own actions. Shortly before trial was scheduled to begin, defendant attempted suicide by taking an overdose of pills. The trial court found defendant fit to stand trial a day later and denied a continuance. Videotaped testimony from a social worker was admitted because she would be considerably inconvenienced if required to remain another day. Witnesses testified that defendant had engaged in other inappropriate behavior with children. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction because he was not entitled to a continuance where the trial court reasonably determined that he was sufficiently recovered to stand trial. Defendant waived any right under Ga. Code Ann. § 24-10-130(e) to object to the admission of the videotaped testimony because his own conduct in delaying the trial caused the situation. Evidence of similar behavior was admissible in cases involving sexual abuse of children. Denial of a mistrial was not error where a curative instruction was given promptly. Defendant's counsel pursued a reasonable trial strategy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because defendant was not entitled to a continuance after a suicide attempt, defendant's intentional delay of the trial waived defendant's right to confront a witness, evidence of similar acts was admissible, a curative instruction was given after denial of a motion for mistrial, and defendant received effective assistance of counsel.

 

1441 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Wallace v. State


A99A0349.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


238 Ga. App. 69; 517 S.E.2d 801; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 728; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2130



May 12, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Drug violation. Lamar Superior Court. Before Judge McCombs, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed a judgment from the Lamar Superior Court (Georgia) denying his amended motion for new trial following his conviction for two counts of the sale of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was convicted of selling cocaine after an officer twice purchased a substance from defendant. At trial, certificates of drug analysis issued pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 35-3-16 (b), subsequently found to be unconstitutional, were admitted to show that the substance was cocaine. On appeal, the court found that reversal was not required. Since defendant did not object at or before trial to admission of the certificates and did not timely object on constitutional grounds, he waived review. The certificates were properly admitted under the statute in effect at the time, and that evidence, coupled with the officers' testimony, was sufficient to support the conviction. Defendant did not prove that his counsel was ineffective by failing to object to admission of the certificates and failing to tell him that plaintiff state intended to use his prior crimes to aggravate his sentence. The certificates were properly admitted, and plaintiff did not offer a plea to reduce his possible sentence; therefore, defendant could not show a reasonable probability that the outcome of his case would have been different. Finding no error, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Criminal defendant's conviction and sentence for selling cocaine were affirmed. Certificates proving that the substance defendant sold was cocaine were admissible at the time of defendant's trial, and defendant waived any constitutional objections. Defendant did not prove that his counsel was ineffective because he did not show that the trial outcome would have been different but for counsel's conduct.

 

1442 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Worthy v. State


A99A0476.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


237 Ga. App. 565; 515 S.E.2d 869; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 483; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1700



April 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Armed robbery, etc. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Fuller.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), convicting him of armed robbery, and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon on the ground that the trial court erred in failing to grant his motion for a mistrial, in failing to charge jury on the lesser-included offense of robbery, and that the sentencing requirements of Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with armed robbery and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. During opening argument, the prosecutor commented on defendant's decision to present a case and present evidence to the jury. Defendant moved for a mistrial, and the motion was denied. Defendant was convicted of both charges, and he appealed. The appeals court affirmed the convictions because, considering the indirect nature of the prosecutor's comment and that fact that it was given during the opening statement, the court concluded that there was no manifest intent by prosecutor to comment on defendant's failure to testify and that jury would not necessarily understand statement as a comment on defendant's failure to testify; thus, court did not err in refusing to grant a mistrial. Moreover, failure to instruct jury regarding lesser-included offense of robbery was not an error because evidence did not support a charge on robbery just because the gun defendant used when committing the crime was not loaded. Finally, defendant's contention that sentencing requirements of Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7 were unconstitutional had been, in another case, previously settled adversely to him.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed because court properly refused to grant a mistrial; prosecutor's comment regarding defendant's decision to put on a case during opening statement did not involve a manifest intent to comment on defendant's failure to testify. Additionally, court acted properly in refusing to instruct jury regarding lesser-included offense of robbery, and sentencing requirement that court used were not unconstitutional.

 

1443 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Forthe


A98A2457.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


237 Ga. App. 134; 514 S.E.2d 890; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 402; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1521



March 18, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Theft by taking. Lowndes Superior Court. Before Judge Cowart.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State appealed a decision from the Lowndes Superior Court (Georgia) granting defendant's demurrer to the underlying indictment alleging eight counts of theft by taking.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted defendant's demurrer to eight counts of theft because the stated failed to state the specific amount taken with regard to each count. On appeal, the state argued that an allegation of the specific amount of money taken was not required because property value was not an element of the crime charged, but applied only to sentencing. In reversing the decision, the court overruled the decision in Division 2 of State v Stamey, 211 Ga. App. 837, 440 S.E.2nd 725, (1994) and held that an allegation that the amount taken was in excess of $ 500 or under $ 500 was sufficient to apprise the defendant that he was facing either a misdemeanor or a felony charge. Thus the indictment was not subject to either a general or special demurrer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision granting defendant's demurrer as it found that the indictment did not have to allege the specific amount taken and the allegation that the value was more than $ 500, a felony, was sufficient.
