K-Mart Corp. v. Hackett


A98A2420, A98A2421.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


237 Ga. App. 127; 514 S.E.2d 884; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 399; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1470



March 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Floyd Superior Court. Before Judge Salmon.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant retailer appealed a judgment from the Floyd Superior Court (Georgia) in a tort action, in which liability was established by default judgment, following a jury trial as to damages. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying its motion to set aside a default judgment and its request for leave to file an out-of-time answer and in entering judgment against it for punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed separate tort actions against defendant retailer, alleging that as they were exiting one of its stores, a security guard committed an assault and battery upon them and falsely arrested and imprisoned plaintiff male in a malicious manner. A default judgment as to liability was entered in each of those cases. The trial court denied defendant's motion to set aside default judgment and its request for leave to file an out-of-time answer. The jury awarded compensatory damages and punitive damages. Defendant appealed, contending that an adjuster's failure to forward the copies of the complaints to headquarters and retain counsel was excusable because she was not an attorney and should not be held to the same standard as an attorney. The court held that it could not say that the trial court abused its discretion in denying defendant's motion to set aside the default judgment entered against it and to open default. The allegations, which stood admitted as a result of defendant's failure to answer the complaint, clearly supported an award of punitive damages. Therefore, the court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision below denying defendant's motion to set aside a default judgment and its request for leave to file an out-of-time. The court also affirmed the award of punitive damages. Defendant did not meet the statutory requirements and the allegations clearly supported an award of punitive damages.

Rogers v. Barnett


A98A1877.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


237 Ga. App. 301; 514 S.E.2d 443; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 341; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1262



March 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 30, 1999. Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Grandparent visitation rights. Evans Superior Court. Before Judge Harvey.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Evans County (Georgia) that granted appellee grandmother visitation rights to see grandson, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 19-7-3. Appellant asserted that there was insufficient evidence to support the judgment, that § 19-7-3 was unconstitutional, and that the trial court incorrectly denied her application for a court-appointed attorney pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-85.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a judgment that granted appellee grandmother rights to visit her grandson pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 19-7-3. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that granted appellee visitation rights. Hooper v. Harris


A98A1659.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


236 Ga. App. 651; 512 S.E.2d 312; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 188; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 786



February 10, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 25, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Paulding Superior Court. Before Judge Fudger.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed in part, judgment vacated in part and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner contested a judgment entered in the Paulding Superior Court (Georgia), which dismissed his complaint for damages against defendant officials. Plaintiff also contested a ruling entered by the court, which ordered that any further pleadings filed by plaintiff were to be deemed null and void as an operation of law.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff prisoner filed suit against defendant officials claiming that they had taken his personal property when he was arrested and had never returned it. Prior to filing the civil suit, plaintiff asserted the same claim during his criminal case when he filed a motion for the return of his property. The court in the criminal case concluded that defendants were not holding any property belonging to plaintiff. The plaintiff did not appeal; rather, he filed the subsequent civil action. In the civil action, the trial court found that plaintiff's complaint was frivolous and dismissed the suit. Subsequently, the trial court ordered that future pleadings filed by plaintiff were to be deemed null and void by operation of law. Upon plaintiff's appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff's civil action holding that res judicata, under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-12-40, precluded a review of plaintiff's appeal. The court vacated the trial court's order that plaintiff's future pleadings be deemed null and void. The court found that the order was overbroad and unconstitutional because it barred adequate, effective, and meaningful access to the courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff prisoner's suit for damages against defendant officials. The court vacated the trial court's ruling, which deemed future filings by plaintiff null and void, because the order unconstitutionally denied plaintiff meaningful access to the courts.

Kenney v. State


A98A2340.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


236 Ga. App. 359; 511 S.E.2d 923; 1999 Ga. App. LEXIS 175; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 799



February 9, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Armed robbery. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Weeks.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions by the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) for two counts of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of two counts of armed robbery. Appellant challenged the convictions and claimed that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction, that his mandatory sentence was unconstitutional, and that several evidentiary rulings constituted an abuse of discretion by the trial court. The court found that appellant's challenge to the constitutionality of his sentence was raised for the first time on appeal, and it, therefore, refused to address that issue. With regard to the evidentiary rulings, the court held that nothing in the record showed an abuse of discretion on the part of the trial court. Lastly, the court held that the evidence was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to find appellant guilty of the crimes charged beyond a reasonable doubt. Therefore, the convictions were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions because the evidence was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to find appellant guilty of the crimes charged beyond a reasonable doubt. In addition, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion regarding its evidentiary rulings. The court did not address appellant's constitutional claim because it was raised for the first time on appeal.

 

1449 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Zach, Inc. v. Fulton County


A98A2362.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


235 Ga. App. 478; 509 S.E.2d 746; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 1533; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 152



November 25, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Granted May 14, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ga. LEXIS 441.


PRIOR HISTORY: Taxation. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wyatt Cummings Moore.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, 17 non-profit fraternal organizations located within the boundaries of a university, appealed a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which affirmed summary judgment in favor of defendant county and rejected the organizations' equal protection challenge to their motion for summary judgment. The organizations brought suit seeking property tax exemptions and tax refunds under Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-41(a)(6).


OVERVIEW: The organizations contended that § 48-5-41(a)(6) was unconstitutional as applied because some university fraternities and sororities which used their properties in an identical manner received tax exemptions, which resulted in disparate treatment violative of equal protection. The court affirmed and held that the other organizations that received tax exemptions were not similarly situated because they, unlike the 17 organizations in dispute, were located on real property belonging to the university. Because the university was a "college," its property fit squarely within the express language of § 48-5-41(a)(6). On the other hand, the 17 organizations were not operating on "college" property, but on private land located within the boundaries of the university. The organizations' "identical use" argument overlooked the crucial fact that the use had to be by the university or an arm and extension of the university. Because the organizations' buildings were not erected for and used as a college, and because the organizations were not an "arm or extension" of the university, they were foreclosed from claiming otherwise.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of the county and denying the organizations' motion for summary judgment in their taxation challenge.

 

1450 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Nawrocki v. State


A98A1517.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


235 Ga. App. 416; 510 S.E.2d 301; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 1515; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 85



November 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied April 9, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ga. LEXIS 359.


PRIOR HISTORY: D.U.I. Cherokee State Court. Before Judge Gober and Judge Harris, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment, entered in the Cherokee County State Court (Georgia), after a jury's verdict, which found him guilty of driving with an unlawful alcohol concentration (DUI), Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of DUI. On appeal, defendant challenged the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress the results of an intoxilyzer test. The appellate court found that, contrary to defendant's contentions, a DUI suspect may be required to produce a breath sample under Georgia law. However, the appellate court determined defendant should have been permitted to obtain a requested second, state-administered breath test. The appellate court reasoned that under the plain language of Ga. Code Ann. §§ 40-6-392(a)(3), 40-5-67.1(b)(2), a DUI defendant--at his own expense--could affirmatively choose to have the state's qualified testing officer perform an additional breath test. Since, as a practical matter, state law enforcement agencies appeared to be the primary locations at which breath test machines were readily available, a timely second breath test could be conducted on a law enforcement agency's machine. Further, the appellate court advised that the State had the burden of demonstrating compliance with the statutory requirements. Accordingly, the appellate court concluded the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment.

 

1451 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Hindman v. State


A98A1136. A98A1137. A98A1138.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


234 Ga. App. 758; 507 S.E.2d 862; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 1355; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3823



October 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Armed robbery, etc. Whitfield Superior Court. Before Judge Partain.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Whitfield Superior Court, Georgia, convicted three defendants of armed robbery, eight counts of aggravated assault, theft by taking, possession of a firearm during the commission of a crime, and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. Defendants received life sentences on the armed robbery convictions pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7 (b) (2), the recidivist statute. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendants alleged that: (1) the evidence was insufficient to convict defendants on the armed robbery, theft by taking, aggravated assault, and possession of a firearm counts; (2) the superior court improperly admitted evidence of their prior criminal convictions; (3) a fatal variance existed between the armed robbery indictment and the evidence adduced at trial; and (4) Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7(b)(2) was unconstitutional. However, the third defendant did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence as to the theft by taking, armed robbery, and aggravated assault convictions. The court of appeals held that: (1) the evidence was sufficient to support the convictions; (2) the superior court did not err by admitting the prior criminal convictions; (3) no fatal variance existed between the indictment and the evidence adduced at trial; and (4) the issue dealing with the unconstitutionality of § 17-10-7 was not preserved, and even if it was, the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

 

1452 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Veasey v. State


A98A1341.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


234 Ga. App. 795; 507 S.E.2d 799; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 1294; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3724



September 28, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 20, 1998. Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Child molestation. Towns Superior Court. Before Judge Barrett.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Towns Superior Court (Georgia), after he was convicted on one count of child molestation. Defendant had been tried under a two-count indictment for the offenses of child molestation and enticing a child for indecent purposes. The trial court directed a verdict on the enticement count but denied the motion for a directed verdict on the molestation count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant worked at a resort with the victim, a 15-year old boy. The evidence showed that defendant asked the victim about his sexuality, dropped his pants in front of the victim, and asked the victim to do the same. Defendant argued that the State failed to prove his knowledge of the victim's age and erroneously refused to give his requested charge on mistake of fact. The court held that, because a mistaken belief as to the victim's age would not have justified the act, a charge on mistake was not warranted. A directed verdict on the enticement charge did not warrant a directed verdict on the child molestation charge because the two were distinct and separate offenses which were not included within each other as a matter of law. Thus, collateral estoppel, res judicata, and double jeopardy did not apply. The child molestation statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-4(a), was neither impermissibly vague nor violative of due process. The State was not required to prove that defendant knew the victim was under the age of 16.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's child molestation conviction.

 

1453 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Provident Indem. Life Ins. Co. v. James


A98A2040, A98A2041.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


234 Ga. App. 403; 506 S.E.2d 892; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 1258; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3488



September 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Denied January 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ga. LEXIS 72.


PRIOR HISTORY: RICO. Clarke Superior Court. Before Judge Stephens.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurers sought review of the decision of the Clarke Superior Court (Georgia) that denied the insurers' motion to dismiss a claim under the Georgia Racketeer Influenced & Corrupt Organizations Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-14-1 et seq., that had been filed by plaintiff insureds, and determined that there was a lack of subject matter jurisdiction over the insureds' tort claims against the insurers.


OVERVIEW: Defendant insurers appealed the denial of their motion to dismiss a Georgia Racketeer Influenced & Corrupt Organizations Act (RICO), Ga. Code Ann. § 16-14-1 et seq., claim filed by plaintiff insureds, challenging the trial court's determination that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the insureds' tort claims against the insurers and the court's dismissal of the claims. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the tort claims and remanded. The court found that the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction over all of the claims. The court affirmed in part finding that the trial court was correct in not requiring insured to exhaust all administrative remedies prior to asserting their RICO claims. The court held that the tort claims were separate causes of action from an administrative proceeding directed solely at violations of the Insurance Code, and it did not matter whether the insureds were able to prove at trial that the insurers violated the Insurance Code, it was not dispositive of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, finding that the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction over all of the claims. The court reversed in part the trial court's dismissal of the tort claims and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1454 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Nolen


A98A1513.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


234 Ga. App. 291; 508 S.E.2d 733; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 1215; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3440



September 9, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended November 2, 1998.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with driving under the influence. The trial court (Georgia) granted defendant's motion in limine to suppress the results of a chemical sobriety test on the ground that the arresting officer did not read verbatim the implied consent notice as mandated by Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a police officer for failing to maintain his vehicle in its lane of travel. After arresting defendant for driving under the influence, the officer read the implied consent warning found in Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1(b). The officer omitted the word "and" in the phrase "at your own expense and from qualified personnel of your own choosing." The court held that a 1998 amendment to the statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1(b), required the officer to read the implied consent in its entirety but not necessarily in the exact language of the statute, so long as the substance of the notice remained unchanged. The court found that the statute in question governed a rule of evidence, which made it procedural. Under such circumstances, the court found that it was obligated to apply the law as it existed at the time that its opinion was rendered because the amendment did not expressly preclude a retroactive effect. The court affirmed and held that it was prohibited from transferring the case to the Supreme Court of Georgia because the constitutional issue was not raised in or ruled upon by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that suppressed evidence of defendant's field sobriety test.

 

1455 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Burgos v. State


A98A1693.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


233 Ga. App. 897; 505 S.E.2d 543; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 1111; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3051



August 17, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Theft by taking, etc. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Bonner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) judgment of conviction, following a jury trial, for theft by taking (auto) and driving under the influence (DUI). He asserted that the trial court erred in excluding testimony from an expert witness regarding voluntary intoxication in support of defendant's lack of intent defense, in failing to instruct the jury on good character, and in imposing consecutive sentences.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of theft by taking (auto) and DUI, and he was sentenced to consecutive terms of 10 years and 12 months, respectively. The trial court denied his motion for new trial, and he appealed. He asserted that the trial court erred in excluding testimony from an expert witness regarding voluntary intoxication in support of the lack of intent defense, in refusing to instruct the jury as to good character, and in sentencing. The court affirmed. It held that defendant failed to show that an alteration of his brain function caused by intoxication was more than temporary. The clinical signs described by the expert were the same as those of any individual who had consumed alcohol to the point of intoxication and did not have permanent brain damage. The doctor's opinion based on a limited examination would have been speculative and was properly excluded. The trial court's failure to charge on good character was not reversible error, given the overwhelming evidence against defendant. Consecutive sentences were permitted where separate and distinct crimes were charged. Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-10. The sentence was not so overly severe or excessive as to shock the conscience.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction for theft by taking (auto) and driving under the influence and affirmed the sentences imposed.

 

1456 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Radcliffe v. State


A98A1842.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


234 Ga. App. 576; 507 S.E.2d 759; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 1078; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3043



August 12, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 30, 1998. Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Denied February 5, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ga. LEXIS 125.


PRIOR HISTORY: D.U.I. Rockdale State Court. Before Judge Todd.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Rockdale State Court (Georgia), which convicted him of driving with a controlled substance in his blood (DUI), in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(6).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in an automobile accident. After the collision, the elderly driver of the other vehicle went into cardiac arrest and later died. Although defendant did not show signs of being under the influence of alcohol or drugs, the investigating officer read him his implied consent rights, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1(b), and the defendant agreed to submit to chemical tests of his blood and urine. These tests showed the presence of marijuana in defendant's blood. He was later convicted of DUI. Defendant appealed the judgment, contending that the trial court erred in denying his motion to exclude the results of his blood test. The court affirmed the judgment, by holding that the results of defendant's blood test were properly admitted because the implied consent warning properly advised him of the purpose for which his blood was to be tested, and his blood sample was used for the legitimate purpose of determining whether he had committed a violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391, and not for the purpose of determining whether he had committed any other violations of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which convicted the defendant of DUI.

 

1457 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Gibson v. State


A98A1423.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


233 Ga. App. 838; 505 S.E.2d 63; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 1037; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 2965



July 30, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Kidnapping, etc. Brantley Superior Court. Before Judge Loggins, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Brantley Superior Court (Georgia) convicting him of aggravated assault on a peace officer, armed robbery, escape, burglary, theft by taking a motor vehicle, use of a firearm by a convicted felon, and multiple counts of kidnapping and false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his criminal convictions, defendant contended that the trial court erred in refusing to sever the trials of the charges relating to two separate incidents, in refusing to grant a mistrial after his character was improperly placed into evidence, and in failing to grant him a directed verdict as to certain offenses. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's judgment which convicted defendant of aggravated assault on a peace officer, armed robbery, escape, burglary, theft by taking a motor vehicle, use of a firearm by a convicted felon, and multiple counts of kidnapping and false imprisonment. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion for severance because evidence regarding the offenses committed on each date would have been admissible in a separate trial on the offenses committed on the other date. Evidence of defendant's motive was admissible even if it incidentally put his character into evidence. However, the movement of an individual necessitated by defendant's release of that individual from confinement was not the type of movement constituting asportation so as to have supported a kidnapping conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's judgment which convicted defendant of aggravated assault on a peace officer, armed robbery, escape, burglary, theft by taking a motor vehicle, use of a firearm by a convicted felon, and multiple counts of kidnapping and false imprisonment.

 

1458 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Fleming v. State


A98A0636.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


233 Ga. App. 483; 504 S.E.2d 542; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 1014; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 2805



July 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Granted February 24, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ga. LEXIS 217.


PRIOR HISTORY: Armed robbery, etc. Fayette Superior Court. Before Judge Miller.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Fayette Superior Court (Georgia), which denied his motion for directed verdict, failed to charge the jury as he requested, and failed to consider his first offender petition. A jury found defendant guilty of armed robbery and the lesser offense of simple assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and simply assault. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court found that defendant's use of a pellet gun constituted use of an offensive weapon. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support the armed robbery conviction, and the court did not err in denying his motion for directed verdict. The court rejected defendant's argument that the court should have charged the jury on the lesser included offense of theft by taking because there was no evidence that would authorize the court to charge on the lesser included offense of theft by taking. The court found that defendant made a videotaped confession admitting to all elements of armed robbery and admitted at trial that he took the car by using a gun. The court held that the trial court did not err in failing to consider defendant's first offender petition. The court found that defendant, who was convicted of one of the serious violent felonies contained in Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-6.1, was not eligible for first offender treatment under Ga. Code Ann. § 42-8-60.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for armed robbery and sentenced him properly.

 

1459 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Howard v. State


A98A0492.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


233 Ga. App. 724; 505 S.E.2d 768; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 993; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 2814



July 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 31, 1998. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied December 4, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 1237.
Reconsideration denied by, 07/31/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Howard v. State, 1998 Ga. LEXIS 1237 (Ga., Dec. 4, 1998)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Howard v. Brown, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 183335 (M.D. Ga., Dec. 5, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Armed robbery, etc. Clarke Superior Court. Before Judge Stephens.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a conviction in the Clarke Superior Court (Georgia) for armed robbery and his sentence to life without parole as a recidivist offender under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and sentenced to life without parole under the mandatory sentencing provisions for recidivist offenders in § 17-10-7(c). On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentencing, even though the pre-sentencing hearings were conducted without the jury present, because the sentence was mandatory and the judge, therefore, had no discretion as to the length of the sentence or the possibilities of parole or probation. The court held that the mandatory nature of § 17-10-7(c) did not render it unconstitutional and that reading the names of the grand jurors was harmless error because the judge properly instructed the jury that the indictment was not evidence. The court also held that, because the new attorney defendant retained after conviction failed to raise ineffective assistance of counsel claims prior to hearing a motion for a new trial, defendant was not entitled to allege ineffective assistance of counsel for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence and held that the jury's presence was not required at the pre-sentencing hearing under a statute that provided for mandatory recidivist sentencing because the judge had no discretion to decide the length of the sentence or the possibilities of parole or probation.

 

1460 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Chambers of Ga., Inc. v. Dep't of Natural Res.


A98A1190.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


232 Ga. App. 632; 502 S.E.2d 553; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 769; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 2218



May 21, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Declaratory judgment. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hunter.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged an order of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which entered summary judgment in favor of the Georgia Department of Natural Resources (department), in a declaratory judgment action brought by the corporation in its attempt to obtain a solid waste handling permit.


OVERVIEW: The corporation filed an application for a solid waste handling permit and a request for site suitability for a municipal solid waste landfill. The department denied the application, stating that Ga. Code Ann. § 12-8-25.4 prevented issuance of the permit for proposed landfill expansion, because the site would encompass a circular area having a two-mile radius and already containing all or portions of three or more landfills. The corporation did not exhaust its administrative remedies regarding this decision. Instead, the corporation filed a petition for declaratory judgment and injunctive or other relief against the department. The petition averred that § 12-8-25.4 was unconstitutional both facially and as applied, and sought an order declaring the statute unconstitutional and enjoining enforcement of the statute as to the corporation's planned modifications and expansions of the landfill. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the department. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that by electing not to exhaust administrative remedies, the corporation was no longer entitled to petition either for an administrative hearing or for judicial review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the department.

 

1461 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Kirbabas


A98A1020, A98A1021.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


232 Ga. App. 474; 502 S.E.2d 314; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 718; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 2179



May 6, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to suppress. Cherokee State Court. Before Judge Cannon, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. A98A1021. Judgment reversed in Case No. A98A1020.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the judgment of the State Court of Cherokee County (Georgia), which granted defendant's motion to suppress certain field sobriety test results. Defendant also sought review of the judgment of the trial court, which found that a police officer gave proper implied consent warnings required by Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1(b)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed weaving across the center road line and driving slowly in her car by a police officer and was stopped because it raised the officer's articulable suspicion that defendant could have been impaired. The officer requested that defendant undergo field sobriety tests. The officer performed a horizontal gaze nystagmus (HGN) test and noted six positive indications of alcohol impairment. After other tests were performed, the officer arrested defendant and read her the Georgia implied consent notice. Defendant was subsequently unable to perform a test at the police station and then refused to submit to the test. At a motion to suppress hearing, the trial court held that any field sobriety test after the HGN test was inadmissible. The court reversed and held that the trial court was in error in its conclusion that Miranda warnings should have been given before the field sobriety tests were conducted because there was no arrest of defendant during the temporary investigatory stop to conduct the field sobriety tests and defendant was not deemed in custody, seized, or "under arrest" for Miranda purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's determination that certain test results were to be suppressed. The court affirmed the trial court's order that the implied consent warnings were properly given by an officer.

Turner v. State


A98A0072.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


231 Ga. App. 747; 500 S.E.2d 628; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 530; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1674



March 31, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Sodomy, etc. Lumpkin Superior Court. Before Judge Barrett.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed on Count 1; judgment of conviction on Count 2 affirmed; sentence on Count 2 reversed and case remanded in part for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions for sodomy and contributing to the delinquency of a minor by the Lumpkin Superior Court (Georgia).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sodomy and contributing to the delinquency of a minor. Defendant argued the evidence varied from the indictment and that the court improperly increased his punishment by imposing the registration requirements of Ga. Code Ann. § 42-1-12. The court determined defendant was sufficiently informed to defend the sodomy charge proved. The court concluded that proof that defendant submitted to rather than performed the sexual act was sufficient to sustain the conviction. Defendant contended that requiring him to comply with sexual offender registration requirements violated the ex post facto clauses of the Georgia and United States Constitution. The court determined that registration, as a sexual offender was not part of defendant's sentence. The trial court simply informed defendant that upon his probation he might be required to register as a sexual offender. The court stated because it was not part of his sentence there could be no error. The state conceded the trial court erred in sentencing defendant to a 12-month term of imprisonment. The court affirmed the conviction and remanded the case for resentencing on count two of defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both convictions made by the trial court, and remanded the case for resentencing on the second conviction.

 

1463 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Monticello Ltd. v. City of Atlanta


A97A1714.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


231 Ga. App. 382; 499 S.E.2d 157; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 454; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1575



March 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied June 26, 1998, reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 758.


PRIOR HISTORY: Solid waste disposal. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Langham, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a judgment from the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment, finding that appellee was authorized to assess fees for waste disposal services upon appellant's unoccupied and uninhabitable apartment units.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner challenged the lower court judgment that granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment and found that appellee was authorized to assess fees for waste disposal services against appellant on unoccupied and uninhabitable apartment units. The court reversed the judgment of the lower court because it found that an assessment of a fee for refuse collection against a vacant and uninhabitable apartment could not be reconciled with the language of Atlanta, Ga., City Charter § 6-101(g) which allowed fee assessment only against occupied premises for the removal of waste generated by the occupants. The court determined that the charter made no explicit provision for assessment of fees on unoccupied and uninhabitable premises that did not generate solid waste. The court concluded that appellee was not authorized to assess fees for the collection, removal, or disposal of solid wastes against appellant for the individual apartment units that were unoccupied or uninhabitable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court judgment that granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment because it found that appellee's charter did not authorize the assessment of fees against appellant property owner for solid waste disposal on unoccupied or uninhabitable apartment units.

 

1464 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Beugnot v. Coweta County


A97A2286.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


231 Ga. App. 715; 500 S.E.2d 28; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 420; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1299



March 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 31, 1998. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied September 11, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 839.


PRIOR HISTORY: Zoning. Coweta Superior Court. Before Judge Lee.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought review of the decision of the Coweta Superior Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment to defendants, the county and the Board of Commissioners (county), and denied the landowner's motion for partial summary judgment in the landowner's action for a writ of mandamus against the county challenging its denial of the landowner's application for a building permit for the mobile home park.


OVERVIEW: The landowner had 13 mobile homes on his property when the county enacted a zoning ordinance which prohibited mobile home parks. The board of zoning appeals recognized the landowner's property as a nonconforming use. However, the county prohibited the landowner from adding any additional mobile homes. The landowner appealed and the jury held that the landowner should be permitted develop. The landowner continued to add at least one mobile home every two years. Subsequently, he received a letter from the county stating that he had abandoned the nonconforming use status. The county eventually allowed him to continue developing. However, the county denied his application for an additional building permit. The landowner filed his petition for a writ of mandamus. The trial court granted the county's motion for summary judgment. The court reversed and held that he had a vested right in the continued development which he had not abandoned. He had expended substantial time, effort, and money on the development of the property prior to the zoning ordinance and he did not fail to act, nor was there any overt act on his part evidencing his intent to abandon the nonconforming use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and held that the writ of mandamus should have been granted and that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment to the county.

 

1465 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Davidson v. State


A98A0738.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


231 Ga. App. 605; 499 S.E.2d 697; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 376; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1907



March 11, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 25, 1998. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied September 11, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 850.
Reconsideration denied by, 03/25/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Davidson v. State, 1998 Ga. LEXIS 850 (Ga., Sept. 11, 1998)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Transferred by Davidson v. Chatman, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 69093 (S.D. Ga., June 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Child molestation, etc. Banks Superior Court. Before Judge Motes.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Banks Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of several sexual and cruelty crimes committed against children. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in severing the trials, that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-4, defining child molestation, was unconstitutionally vague, that the indictment was defective, and that videotapes should not have been introduced.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual crimes and cruelty to children after the children of defendant's girlfriend reported the abuse. The court affirmed the conviction and held that: (1) the trial court did not abuse its discretion by not severing the trials because some of the acts were conducted simultaneously and the evidence showed that the crimes were a series of connected acts; (2) the state supreme court had ruled that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-4 was not unconstitutionally vague because the phrase "any immoral or indecent act" was definite and certain in its meaning such that people of common intelligence would not have differed as to the application of its provisions; (3) the indictment was not defective for failing to specify exact dates of the illegal acts because, as long as dates were not a material allegation of the offense and the offenses were proven to have been committed within the statute of limitations, defendant's assertion that the period encompassed too many offenses over too long of a time did not establish prejudice or surprise; and (4) videotapes confiscated from defendant's home were admissible to show defendant's lustful disposition and bent of mind.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for sexual crimes and cruelty to children.

 

1466 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Fincher v. State


A97A1850.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


231 Ga. App. 49; 497 S.E.2d 632; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 326; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1077



March 10, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Public Records Act. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hancock.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a former state employee, filed an action against defendants, the State Board of Pardons & Paroles of Georgia (Board) and several of its employees, asserting that the release of a certain investigatory report violated his common law and constitutional rights to privacy. The DeKalb County Superior Court (Georgia), dismissed the claims against the employees and subsequently dismissed the entire action. The former employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The former employee sought damages under the Georgia Tort Claims Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 50-21-20 et seq., and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, after the Board released to a television station, pursuant to the Public Records Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 50-18-70 et seq., an investigatory report that he had sexually harassed a co-worker while employed by the Board. On appeal, the court held that dismissal was proper because the public had a legitimate interest in a public employee's alleged improper activities in the workplace that outweighed the former employee's interest in non-disclosure. The report was a public record within the meaning of Ga. Code Ann. § 50-18-70, and there was no evidence that the report was protected by a court order under Ga. Code Ann. § 50-18-70(a). Dismissal of the invasion of privacy claim under the Georgia Tort Claims Act was proper because the Board was required under the Public Records Act to release the information. The trial court did not err in dismissing the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim because the former employee was not deprived of any right or privilege secured by the U.S. Constitution or federal law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the former employee's complaint.

Harris v. State

1468 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Schmidt v. Feldman


A98A0544.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


230 Ga. App. 500; 497 S.E.2d 23; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 201; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 773



February 9, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied May 29, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 593.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice. Clayton State Court. Before Judge Benefield.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, patient and patient's husband, challenged the decision of the Clayton State Court (Georgia), which dismissed their medical malpractice complaint against defendants, doctor and medical group, for failure to attach a properly notarized expert affidavit. Plaintiffs had attached to their complaint the expert affidavit of a doctor, which was signed in Michigan, although a Georgia notary had notarized it.


OVERVIEW: In response to defendants' motion to dismiss, plaintiffs submitted the affidavit of the notary. The notary testified that he had forwarded the affidavit to the expert in Michigan, spoke with the expert by telephone, reviewed the affidavit with him, and had the expert swear to the truth of its contents. The affidavit was notarized on the date that the expert signed it. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing plaintiffs' case. The court held that in order to make an affidavit, there must be present the officer, the affiant, and the paper, and there must be something done that amounted to the administration of an oath. There must be some solemnity, not mere telephone talk. Long-distance swearing was not permissible. Thus, in the absence of a valid jurat, the expert's affidavit had no validity. Plaintiffs' constitutional argument was not properly before the court for review, because the constitutional argument was to be addressed by the state supreme court, which had not found a reason to do so, and had transferred the appeal to the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which dismissed plaintiffs' medical malpractice complaint against defendants for failure to attach a properly notarized expert affidavit.

 

1469 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Baum v. Moore


A97A2042.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


230 Ga. App. 255; 496 S.E.2d 307; 1998 Ga. App. LEXIS 99; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 404



January 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Adoption. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Stark.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandparents challenged the decision of the Gwinnett Superior Court (Georgia), which denied their motion to intervene in the petition filed by appellee adoptive parents. The grandparents, who also filed a petition for adoption, argued that they had a right to intervene in the potential adoption of their grandchildren pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 19-7-1 (b.1).


OVERVIEW: Parents consented to give temporary custody of their children to the maternal grandparents. The juvenile court returned custody to the parents and gave the grandparents visitation rights. Less than one year later, the parents voluntarily surrendered their parental rights after an unrelated couple filed a petition to adopt the children. The grandparents' motion to intervene was denied and the couple's petition to adopt the grandchildren was granted. On appeal, the court considered whether Ga. Code Ann. § 19-7-1 (b.1) allowed the grandparents to intervene as of right. The court examined the statute in light of other state laws about grandparent rights and concluded that grandparents could object to an adoption when a child had no legal living parent, or when the parent had lost parental rights and the adoption petition had been filed by one of the child's blood relatives. Section 19-7-1(b.1) addressed only how parental power could be lost; it did not create a new right to intervene in an adoption proceeding. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court held that the grandparents could not intervene as of right in the adoption proceedings for their grandchildren. The court affirmed.

 

1470 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Harris v. State


A97A1236.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


229 Ga. App. 705; 494 S.E.2d 738; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1493; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 42



December 5, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Armed robbery. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Castellani.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of armed robbery and denied his motion for a new trial; defendant contended that the trial court erred in refusing to have the sheriff serve his subpoenas and in admitting evidence of similar transactions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, while incarcerated for other crimes, was indicted for armed robbery. Defendant chose to proceed pro se. Subsequently, defendant requested the superior court to arrange for the sheriff to serve various subpoenas, and he filed a motion to suppress evidence of similar transactions. The superior court denied the request to have the subpoenas served and denied the motion to suppress. The superior court ruled that the anticipated testimony was not material to defendant's case and that the prosecution would call the witnesses anyway; no subpoenas were thus necessary. Thereafter, defendant was convicted of armed robbery. Defendant appealed. On review, the court affirmed the judgment. In regard to the evidence of the similar transactions, the court found neither error nor infirmity, which could possibly have deprived defendant of a fair trial. The court noted that such evidence was offered for the proper purpose of showing intent, common scheme and plan, and motive. In regard to the subpoenas, the court held that the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt rendered harmless any possible error the trial court might have committed in failing to issue the subpoenas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court, which convicted defendant of armed robbery.

 

1471 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Thompson v. State


A97A1839.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


229 Ga. App. 526; 494 S.E.2d 306; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1452; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4447



November 24, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied May 14, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 554.


PRIOR HISTORY: D.U.I., etc. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Purdom.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the DeKalb State Court (Georgia), which denied his plea in bar based upon double jeopardy, contending that the $ 200 restoration fee for his driver's license was punitive. His driver's license was suspended for one year after he was arrested for DUI and a subsequent breath test indicated he had an alcohol concentration of .10 or above.


OVERVIEW: In order to reinstate his driving privileges, appellant submitted proof of completion of a risk reduction program and paid the $ 200 restoration fee. On appeal from the denial of his plea in bar, he claimed that the restoration fee was punishment for the same conduct for which he was being criminally prosecuted. The court affirmed the order denying relief, holding that the fee was not punitive because it was not a fine and was not required to be paid, but was rather a voluntary payment. Neither a driver's license suspension hearing nor the actual suspension of a driver's license constituted a bar to criminal prosecution for DUI. Suspension of a driver's license was the revocation of a privilege voluntarily granted, a traditional attribute of a remedial action. The State had the authority to revoke appellant's driving privileges as a remedial measure, without implication of his Fifth Amendment rights. Therefore, according to the court, the State could revoke appellant's privileges subject to his ability to reinstate them upon certain conditions. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying appellant's plea in bar based upon double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied appellant's plea in bar based on double jeopardy.

 

1472 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



In the Interest of Y.E.


A97A1783.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


229 Ga. App. 506; 494 S.E.2d 297; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1446; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4448



November 20, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Delinquency. Troup Juvenile Court. Before Judge Key.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a hearing pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-33(a), the Troup Juvenile Court (Georgia) adjudicated defendant delinquent upon a finding that she committed two designated felony acts that, if committed by an adult, were aggravated assault and carrying a weapon on school property. Defendant appealed therefrom, arguing that the trial court failed to properly consider her needs and best interests as required by Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-37.


OVERVIEW: After defendant and a victim exchanged insults at school, defendant cut the victim's arm with a box cutter. After adjudicating defendant delinquent, the trial court ordered that she be place in restrictive custody for five years. On appeal, the court held that the trial court's failure to make written findings on each of the five elements set forth in Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-37(c) required reversal. Specifically, the trial court's order of commitment failed to include written findings on the needs and best interests of the juvenile. The omission was particularly troubling in light of the trial court's comments regarding the punitive nature of the designated felony statute. To the contrary, the court explained that the objective of the Juvenile Code was non-confinement, rehabilitation, and restoration to parental care wherever possible rather than punishment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and remanded the case with directions to consider defendant's needs and best interests in light of the Juvenile Code's objectives.

 

1473 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Lombard Corp. v. Collins


A97A0150.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


229 Ga. App. 654; 494 S.E.2d 538; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1437; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4420



November 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 4, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Granted May 5, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 529.


PRIOR HISTORY: Declaratory judgment, etc. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Flake.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation appealed from the Superior Court's (Georgia) order granting appellee's motion to dismiss and dismissing appellant's motion for summary judgment on the pleadings. Appellant brought suit for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief asserting the unconstitutionality of the Georgia intangible tax, Ga. Code Ann. § 48-6-20 et seq. after appellant was assessed an intangible tax.


OVERVIEW: While suit was pending, the intangible tax assessment at issue was paid, without the prior consent of the appellant or of the trial court, by a person who was not a party to the litigation. Thus, the payment of the taxes was made, by a third party interloper. After payment of the taxes by the interloper, the trial court held that the appellant's suit was moot and the motion to dismiss was granted. The court considered as a matter of first impression whether it violated the public policy of this state for a third party, who was not a party to a lawsuit, to pay the taxes of a party plaintiff without the prior consent of either the trial court or the party plaintiff, thereby causing the plaintiff's case to become moot. The court concluded that it violated the public policy of the state to allow a case to be mooted by the intervention of a third-party who was not a party to the litigation, under the circumstances attendant in this particular case. Accordingly, a legitimate exception existed to the usual rules of mootness under these existing circumstances, and the suit was not rendered moot by the payment of the tax assessment by the third party.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which granted appellee's motion to dismiss appellant's suit.

Banks v. State


A97A2049.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


229 Ga. App. 414; 493 S.E.2d 923; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1421; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4371



November 17, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Drug violation. Gwinnett State Court. Before Judge Mock.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Gwinett State Court (Georgia), which convicted him of a misdemeanor for possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a misdemeanor for possession of marijuana. Defendant claimed that the trial court lacked jurisdiction over the crime charged, and that it erred in denying his motion to suppress the marijuana seized during a late-night security check of his business. On appeal, the court disagreed, and affirmed his conviction. The court rejected the argument that he was actually charged with a felony, over which the trial court had no jurisdiction. The court did not find anything in Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(j), which conferred misdemeanor status on first offenders, to apply only where a court actually considered and denied defendant a conditional discharge. Next, the court found the trial court had properly denied defendant's motion to suppress. The court held that the police officers who were conducting a routine, nighttime investigation of the business on their patrol could enter the unlocked commercial premises to check for intruders. Finally, the court concluded that once they entered the building and observed the marijuana smoking device in plain view, they had probable cause to seize the device and search for additional contraband.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of a misdemeanor for possession of marijuana.

Fly v. State


A97A1288.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


229 Ga. App. 374; 494 S.E.2d 95; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1415; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4350



November 14, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied February 20, 1998. Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 329.


PRIOR HISTORY: Aggravated stalking. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Flake.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pro se defendant appealed a judgment of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of aggravated stalking.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sent the victim threatening letters, messages, and presents; accessed her computer and went through her trash; contacted her friends, family, and associates, including sending over 200 letters and other materials to her minister; and tapped her telephone. Defendant plead guilty to eavesdropping. After defendant repeatedly violated his probation by continuing to contact her, sometimes from jail, he was convicted of aggravated stalking. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the evidence showed that defendant committed unconsented-to contact with the victim for the purpose of harassing and intimidating her in violation of a condition of probation, which was an offense under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-91(a). The court found that § 16-5-91(a) did not violate due process or the First Amendment, and that a pro se defendant was not entitled to bail or a personal computer in jail in order to prepare for trial. If the noisy jail conditions violated defendant's right to representation, the error was harmless because of the overwhelming evidence against him. The court found that evidence of defendant's harassing conduct prior to the eavesdropping was admissible to show intent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of aggravated stalking.

Sherin v. Dep't of Human Res.


A97A1091.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


229 Ga. App. 621; 494 S.E.2d 518; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1363; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4091



November 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 3, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied March 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 401.


PRIOR HISTORY: Negligence. Rabun Superior Court. Before Judge Struble.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, foster parents and parents, sought review of the decision of the Rabun Superior Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, Department of Human Resources (department) and caseworker, in the foster parents and parents' action for negligence under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for violation of their federal substantive and procedural due process rights and breach of contract.


OVERVIEW: The department placed a 13-year old boy with the foster parents. The boy molested the foster parents' granddaughter and another child. The foster parents and the granddaughter's parents brought an action for breach of contract and negligence for violating their due process rights against the department and the caseworker and alleged that the caseworker failed to inform them that the boy was observed masturbating in front of others prior to placing him with the foster parents. The trial court dismissed their action. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision and held that the caseworker's failure to tell the foster parents about the boy's sexual misbehavior was not objectively unreasonable so as to deprive the caseworker of qualified immunity. The department was not aware of any prior sexual molestation of or by the boy, and there was no showing of deliberate indifference by the department that was required to sustain a § 1983 claim. Thus, summary judgment to the caseworker was appropriate. Also, the department did not waive its sovereign immunity, and there was no merit to the breach of contract argument. The trial court did not err in not ordering production of the boy's records.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which granted summary judgment to the department and the caseworker in the foster parents and the parents' action for negligence and breach of contract.

 

1477 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



White v. Kfc Nat'l Mgmt. Co.


A97A1852.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


229 Ga. App. 73; 493 S.E.2d 244; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1347; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4039



October 30, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 242.


PRIOR HISTORY: Negligence. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Thompson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff customer challenged the judgment of the Fulton State Court (Georgia), which granted defendant food chain's motion to dismiss the negligence action pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 9-2-61(a). The customer sought damages allegedly caused by eating rancid food.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the customer's negligence action for want of prosecution. The customer refiled and voluntarily dismissed her action against the food chain without prejudice because it was outside the statute of limitation period. The customer later again refiled the action and the trial court dismissed. The court affirmed the judgment. While Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-41(a) permitted the customer to dismiss her action twice without prejudice, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-2-61(a) controlled the refiling of the action, both within and outside the statute of limitation period. The court held that it was undisputed that both the trial court's dismissal and the customer's voluntary dismissal occurred outside of the statute of limitation period. The trial court was correct in granting the food chain's motion to dismiss based on the applicable statute of limitation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that granted the food chain's motion to dismiss the customer's negligence action. The court held that the customer failed to properly file her action within the applicable statute of limitations.

 

1478 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Bd. of Comm'Rs v. Farmer


A97A2240, A97A2241.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


228 Ga. App. 819; 493 S.E.2d 21; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1281; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 3854



October 15, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 42 USC § 1983. Effingham Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. A97A2241. Judgments affirmed in part and reversed in part in Case No. A97A2240.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county board of commissioners (board) and commissioners, sought review of the order of the Effingham Superior Court (Georgia), which granted partial summary judgment on a federal procedural due process claim brought under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, in favor of appellee county administrator. The administrator filed a cross-appeal of the grant of summary judgment on a slander claim and the board's lack of liability.


OVERVIEW: After the commissioners spontaneously terminated the county administrator, the administrator appealed to the board. The board reaffirmed the termination, and the administrator brought a procedural due process action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and a slander action. The lower superior granted the administrator partial summary judgment on the due process claim and granted the commissioners summary judgment on the slander claim. The court reversed the due process portion of the superior court's decision and held that a post-deprivation hearing satisfied due process when the board's action was a random, unauthorized act that was not the result of an established state procedure. The court held that the state courts provided the administrator with an adequate post-deprivation remedy. Moreover, the commissioners were protected by qualified immunity because at the time of the incident, no concrete law existed that would have compelled the commissioners to conclude that their actions violated federal law. Finally, the grant of summary judgment on the slander claim was proper because the commissioners' statements were merely an expression of opinion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the superior court's order granting summary judgment to the board and commissioners on the administrator's due process claims. The court affirmed the order in all other respects.

 

1479 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Billups v. State


A97A1201.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


228 Ga. App. 804; 493 S.E.2d 8; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1280; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 3877



October 14, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Double jeopardy. Clarke Superior Court. Before Judge Jones.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Clarke Superior Court (Georgia), which denied his plea of former jeopardy in the prosecution for aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with reckless conduct for firing at a house. The arresting officer also swore out warrants for aggravated assault based on the same shooting. Defendant was indicted on four counts of aggravated assault. Defendant pleaded guilty to reckless conduct and filed a motion to dismiss the aggravated assault indictments as double jeopardy. The trial court denied this motion. Defendant appealed. The court held that the trial court incorrectly interpreted Ga. Code Ann. § 16-1-7(b) to mean the prosecutor must have had knowledge of charges pending. The court also held that the trial court erred in refusing to impute to prosecutors a knowledge of the law. The court found that the trial court erred in ruling that single prosecutions were required only if a prosecutor knew of other "charges pending" as to the same conduct. The court held that the aggravated assault prosecution was therefore barred by Ga. Code Ann. §§ 16-1-7(b), 16-1-8 (b)(1). The court reversed the decision of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court which denied defendant's plea of former jeopardy in the prosecution for aggravated assault.

 

1480 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Siegrist v. Iwuagwa


A97A1338.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


229 Ga. App. 508; 494 S.E.2d 180; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1214; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 3605



September 26, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 21, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Denied October 13, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6534.


PRIOR HISTORY: Chiropractic treatment; massage. Cobb State Court. Before Judge Glover.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff chiropractor challenged the decision of the Cobb State Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant patient in the chiropractor's suit to collect payment for the rendering of services which were outside the scope of chiropractic treatment. The chiropractor claimed that he was entitled to payment from the patient for massages, which were not authorized chiropractic treatment under Ga. Code Ann. § 43-9-16.


OVERVIEW: The chiropractor provided treatment to the patient for injuries. After the patient's insurance refused to pay for the massage services, the patient likewise refused, and the chiropractor brought suit. On appeal, the court affirmed. First, the court held that § 43-9-16 limited the treatments that chiropractors could provide, and because massage was not a listed treatment, the chiropractor was not entitled to recover for the massages. The patient's guarantee to pay for chiropractic services could not include the guarantee to pay for any type of non-chiropractic service, including massage. Second, the court held that the contract between the parties was void under Ga. Code Ann. §13-8-1 because the massages were not authorized by law as chiropractic treatment. And finally, the court addressed the constitutional claims and held that the statute did not violate the chiropractor's equal protection rights because it was not arbitrary and capricious, it did not violate his due process rights because massage services did not fall within the scope of chiropractic practice, and it did not impair his right to contract because he had no vested right to perform massages and charge for them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the patient holding that the chiropractor could not recover for massage services because such services were not statutorily authorized as chiropractic treatment.
