Jackson v. Ga. Lottery Corp.


A97A2135.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


228 Ga. App. 239; 491 S.E.2d 408; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1054; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 3067



August 11, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsiderations Denied August 25, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied January 5, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 162.


PRIOR HISTORY: Lottery games. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Langham.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals sought review of the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee state lottery corporation's motion for summary judgment, in individuals' action that challenged the constitutionality of two of the state lottery corporation's lottery games, sought injunctive relief to prevent these games from being played, and requested damages in the amount of all proceeds from the two games.


OVERVIEW: State lottery commission operated two lottery games that individuals believed violated the state constitution. Individuals filed an action, attempting to file a class action for all other persons similarly situated, for injunctive relief and requested damages in the amount of all proceeds from the two games. The state lottery commission filed a summary judgment motion, and argued that it was protected by sovereign immunity and that the proceeds could not be forfeited from the educational funds to which they were directed. The trial court granted the motion for summary judgment, and the individuals appealed. On appeal, the court held that the state lottery commission was not a state "agency" entitled to the defense of sovereign immunity in this particular case, and that the fact that funds were directed to the state's educational fund was insufficient to support summary judgment. However, the court also held that because the two games challenged were constitutional, that the trial court's conclusion was nonetheless proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1482 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Preston v. Ga. Power Co.


A97A0776. A97A0777.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


227 Ga. App. 449; 489 S.E.2d 573; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 932



July 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied February 20, 1998. Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 299.


PRIOR HISTORY: Workers' compensation; High-voltage Safety Act. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Coursey.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed a negligence action against defendants, a chemical company and a power company. The DeKalb County Superior Court (Georgia) granted summary judgment holding that the workers' compensation tort bar of Ga. Code Ann. § 34-9-11 precluded an action against the chemical company and that under Ga. Code Ann. § 46-3-39 there was no proximate cause in the action against the power company. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: An employee of a temporary labor agency was injured when a pole he was using to clean out a railcar touched high voltage lines. He claimed that he was not a borrowed employee of the chemical company to which he was assigned because the agency retained the right to discharge him. He also asserted that the High-voltage Safety Act, Ga. Code Ann. §§ 46-3-30 to -40, which protected a power company from liability for work performed near high-voltage lines unless notice of the work was given to the company, was unconstitutional. The court held that the employee was a borrowed servant of the chemical company and that his sole remedy was workers' compensation because once he was assigned to work for a special master, the agency relinquished its control. Summary judgment for the power company was proper because it was protected under Ga. Code Ann. § 46-3-39(a) by the failure of the employee and chemical company to give the notice required by the Act. The claim that the Act was unreasonable, arbitrary, and capricious because it did not require the power company to identify which lines were high-voltage was irrelevant because the chemical company had actual notice of the high voltage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment.

 

1483 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Utica Mut. Ins. Co. v. Mitchell


A97A0781.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


227 Ga. App. 830; 490 S.E.2d 489; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 933



July 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 31, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied January 5, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 126.


PRIOR HISTORY: Guardianship. Union Superior Court. Before Judge Stone from Enotah Circuit.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of the decision from the Union Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee ward's motion, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-60(d), to set aside the dismissal by the probate court of her mother as guardian of the ward's property.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed a motion in the probate court to be dismissed as the guardian of the ward's property. The probate court granted the motion on the basis that the ward had been emancipated by marriage. The ward filed an action in the trial court to set aside the dismissal, based on the fact that no accounting and settlement had been made and that she had not received notice of the proceeding. The ward's motion was granted. The insurer, which had posted the surety bond in the course of the guardianship, challenged the decision. On appeal the court reversed, holding that the trial court was without jurisdiction, under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-60, to rule on the ward's motion. The ward could attack the probate court's judgment only on direct appeal because the judgment was not void on its face. While the ward had alleged procedural defects, they were not apparent on the face of the judgment. A judgment void on its face was limited to judgments that lacked either personal or subject matter jurisdiction. Because the ward was not entitled to personal service, notice by publication being expressly provided for by Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-4 (j), the probate court had jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, for lack of jurisdiction, the trial court's decision that granted the ward's motion to set aside a guardian's dismissal entered by the probate court.

 

1484 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



McDaniel v. State


A97A0847.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


227 Ga. App. 364; 489 S.E.2d 112; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 917; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 2793



July 15, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Search and seizure. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Simmons.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia), after the denial of his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the arresting officer lacked an articulable suspicion to make the initial stop of defendant. The court found that the defendant, who reacted to seeing the officer by turning off his headlights and speeding away, created a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity by his odd and evasive behavior. After he was released by the first officer, the court concluded, the subsequent stop of defendant's vehicle was lawful, even though based on a revoked dispatch to be-on-the-lookout where that revocation preceded the stop by but one hour and such revocation had not yet been communicated to the arresting officer. Specifically, the officer's momentary detention of defendant's vehicle was reasonable despite being based on another jurisdiction's recalled dispatch, where the recall of that dispatch one hour earlier was not seasonably communicated. Because the suppression of the evidence seized was properly denied, the conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The conviction of defendant was affirmed.

 

1485 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Walker v. Melton


A97A0786.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


227 Ga. App. 149; 489 S.E.2d 63; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 863; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 2525



July 8, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Denied January 8, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 74.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice. Coweta Superior Court. Before Judge Lee.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed a medical malpractice action against defendant medical providers. The Coweta Superior Court (Georgia) granted summary judgment to the providers based on the two-year statute of limitation of Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-71(a). The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient received x-rays of his spine after he was injured in a car accident. The providers read the x-rays and failed to recognize a fracture of a vertebra. As a result, the patient received no treatment. When the patient's back pain recurred, x-rays revealed the fracture damage, which by that time had worsened. The patient argued that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment to the providers because the statute of limitation began to run not when the providers misread the x-rays, but when he learned his vertebra was fractured. The court reversed the summary judgment order. The court stressed that the patient did not allege that the misdiagnosis caused his broken back. The complaint was based on the worsened compression of his spine. The evidence showed these injuries occurred sometime between the misdiagnosis and the correct diagnosis. Because the subsequent injury was difficult to date precisely, the statute of limitation ran from the date symptoms attributable to the new injury were manifest to the patient. The providers failed to show that the patient had any manifestations of the new injuries until less than two years before suit was filed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting summary judgment in favor of the providers in the patient's medical malpractice action, holding that the statute of limitation began to run not when the providers misread the x-rays, but when the symptoms became manifest to the patient.

 

1486 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Ga. Psc v. Alltel Ga. Communs. Corp.


A97A1141.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


227 Ga. App. 382; 489 S.E.2d 350; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 851; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 2516



July 3, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 16, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Granted February 5, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ga. LEXIS 222.


PRIOR HISTORY: Telephone rates. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Etheridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state public service commission (commission) sought review of the decision of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which reversed the commission's decision that changed appellee telephone companies' rates for intrastate switched access after the telephone companies filed a notice of alternative regulation with the commission pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 46-5-165.


OVERVIEW: The commission argued that the legislature intended to have provided that the rates of a local exchange company were deemed just and reasonable on the effective date specified by the local exchange company in its election notice, and it was on that date that the local exchange company became subject to alternative regulation. The telephone companies argued that on the date they filed their notice of election of alternative regulation the commission lost its jurisdiction to have determined the telephone companies' appropriate earning levels and to have adjusted their rates. The court reversed the judgment in favor of the telephone companies. The court held that the legislative intent of the Georgia Telecommunications & Competition Development Act of 1995, Ga. Code Ann. § 46-5-160 et seq., was to have protected consumers and authorized competition. The court determined that the commission retained its authority to have adjusted the rates of the telephone companies so that the rates remained reasonable and just. The court also decided that the regulatory plan in effect did not abrogate or otherwise limit the power of the commission to have adjusted the rates.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the telephone companies.

 

1487 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Vines


A97A0356.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


226 Ga. App. 779; 487 S.E.2d 521; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 767; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 2291



June 11, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Granted December 19, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ga. LEXIS 978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Child molestation. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge McGarity.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged a judgment from the Henry Superior Court (Georgia), which sustained defendant's demurrer that the allegation in an indictment was insufficient to indict defendant for child molestation under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-4(a) and dismissed the indictment.


OVERVIEW: The state indicted defendant for child molestation under § 16-6-4(a). The indictment alleged that he had performed an immoral and indecent act to a child under 16 years of age with intent to arouse and to satisfy his sexual desires by calling said child on the telephone and engaging in conversation about sexual acts, including fondling of private parts, intercourse, and oral sodomy. The trial court granted defendant's demurrer that the allegation was insufficient to sustain the indictment and dismissed the indictment. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and held that: (1) the allegation that defendant had initiated a conversation with the child about the various sexual acts with intent to arouse and to satisfy his sexual desires alleged an immoral or indecent "act;" (2) the sexually exploitative and psychologically damaging nature of the alleged act was not altered by the fact that it was communicated by telephone, and thus did not remove it from the scope of acts prohibited by § 16-6-4(a); and (3) the physical presence of the child was not required because the language of was § 16-6-4(a) sufficiently broad to apply to a conversation by telephone.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had sustained defendant's demurrer and dismissed his indictment for child molestation, in the state's challenge to the dismissal of the indictment.

 

1488 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Rowe v. Fleet Mortg. Corp.


A97A0461, A97A0943, A97A1073.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


226 Ga. App. 593; 487 S.E.2d 133; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 701; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 2181



May 29, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Dispossessory. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Leitch, pro hac vice (case no. A97A0461). Before Judge Leshaw, pro hac vice (case nos. A97A0943 and A97A1073).



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. A97A0461. Appeals voluntarily dismissed upon motion in Case Nos. A97A0943 and A97A1073.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tenant appealed judgments of the DeKalb State Court (Georgia), which twice issued plaintiff mortgage company a writ of possession and determined that defendant did not timely pay money into court pending his appeal of the trial court's issuance of the first writ of possession.


OVERVIEW: The mortgage company brought a dispossessory action, which alleged that the tenant was a tenant at sufferance due to foreclosure. The trial court issued a writ of possession. The tenant appealed and contended that the dispossessory should have been transferred to the superior court after the tenant timely answered. The court granted the tenant's motion for voluntary dismissal of his appeals of a second issuance of a writ of possession and his appeal of a trial court determination that the tenant had not timely paid money into court pending appeal, and affirmed the issuance of the first writ of possession. The court held that there was no automatic transfer of a dispossessory action from the state court to the superior court, upon the tenant's timely answer, because the statute that once provided so had been superceded by subsequent legislative enactment. The tenant had also contended that proper notice of the foreclosure was not given and that Ga. Code Ann. § 44-14-162.2 was unconstitutional. The court found that the tenant had not shown any trial court error and that the issues were not presented to the trial court, so the court had nothing for decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order in the first writ of possession action and granted defendant's motions to voluntarily dismiss his appeals of the trial court's issuance of the second writ of possession and the trial court's determination that defendant did not timely pay money into court pending his appeal of the trial court's issuance of the first writ of possession.

Wright v. Barnett Mortg. Co.


A97A0609.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


226 Ga. App. 94; 485 S.E.2d 583; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 524; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1762



April 4, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wrongful foreclosure. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wyatt Cummings Moore.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagor sought review of the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted defendant mortgagee's motion for summary judgment in the mortgagor's wrongful foreclosure action.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor filed an action against the mortgagee alleging that the mortgagee wrongfully foreclosed on a security interest in a parcel of real property owned by the mortgagor. The mortgagor contended that she never received notice of the foreclosure sale. The mortgagee contended that it sent notice of the foreclosure by certified mail to the mortgagor's last known address. The trial court granted the mortgagee's motion for summary judgment, and the mortgagor sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that the mortgagor's contention that the notice of foreclosure was defective because it failed to provide a reinstatement balance was without merit because the mortgagor failed to demonstrate how she was prejudiced by the alleged omission. The court held that the mortgagor's undisputed failure to provide the mortgagee was written notice of a new address defeated the mortgagor's claim that she was not properly notified of the sale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted the mortgagee's motion for summary judgment of the mortgagor's wrongful foreclosure action.

 

1490 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Parian Lodge v. Dekalb County


A97A0480.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


225 Ga. App. 853; 485 S.E.2d 545; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 502; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1759



April 1, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied September 4, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ga. LEXIS 776.


PRIOR HISTORY: Ad valorem tax refund. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Castellani.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed the order of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which granted defendant county's motion to dismiss the taxpayer's claims for a refund of ad valorem real property taxes paid on certain property for the 1990 tax year and for inverse condemnation.


OVERVIEW: The county reassessed the property's fair market value in 1990 without the owners filing an appeal or protest. The taxpayer, as mortgagee and security holder, then foreclosed on the property in question and paid the taxes due without protest. In 1991, the county lowered the fair market value. In 1993, the taxpayer sought a refund or the 1990-year. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the taxpayer's complaint. The court found, inter alia, that (1) the refund procedure delineated in Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-380 was limited to the correction of errors of fact or law that had resulted in erroneous or illegal taxation; (2) the taxpayer's claim based on mere dissatisfaction with an assessment, or on an assertion that the assessors did not take into account matters that the taxpayer believed should have been considered, did not assert that an assessment was erroneous or illegal within the meaning of § 48-5-380; and (3) the taxpayer's claim for a refund of taxes was based not on any inaccuracy in the factual record or any illegality in the procedure used to reach an assessment, but on a disagreement with the amount of the assessment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which dismissed the taxpayer's complaint for a refund of ad valorem real property taxes.

 

1491 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Skidmore v. State


A97A0724.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


226 Ga. App. 130; 485 S.E.2d 540; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 492; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1697



March 28, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 9, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Denied September 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ga. LEXIS 830.


PRIOR HISTORY: Armed robbery. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Mallis.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed from the rulings of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which tried defendant for armed robbery as an adult pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-5 (b)(2)(A)(vii). A jury convicted defendant, and the trial court sentenced him to 10 years in prison. The trial court refused to sever defendant's trial from that of his co-defendant and admitted defendant's custodial statements.


OVERVIEW: The trial court instructed the jury to consider the guilt or innocence of each defendant separately, and the jury acquitted the co-defendant. On appeal, the court deemed that the acquittal was evidence that the number of defendants was not so great as to cause confusion of the evidence and the law. The court found that the co-defendant's statement was properly admitted with a cautionary instruction and held that antagonistic defenses did not mandate the severance of co-defendants. The court held that any violation of the juvenile arrest procedures outlined in Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-19(a) did not render defendant's custodial statements inadmissible, but rather, that the issue was whether defendant made the statements after freely, knowingly, and voluntarily waiving his Miranda rights. The court also ruled that it had no authority to decide a constitutional challenge to the facial validity of the juvenile transfer statute, but it noted that the possibility of a life sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment and that a defendant had the burden to show purposeful discrimination in an equal protection challenge, not mere statistical disparities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of armed robbery as an adult.

 

1492 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Osborne Bonding & Sur. Co. ex rel. Castaneda v. State


A97A0059.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


225 Ga. App. 896; 485 S.E.2d 235; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 446; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1575



March 18, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 3, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied September 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ga. LEXIS 826.


PRIOR HISTORY: Bond reduction. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Benefield.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surety challenged the judgment of the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia), which held that the surety was not entitled to a reduction of bond amount which it had posted for an accused. The trial court determined that the surety had presented no evidence that it played any role in returning the accused to authorities. The surety did not pay the judgment and relied on 1992 Ga. Laws p. 2933, §§ 4(d)(1) and (d)(3) on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The surety posted bond for the accused, who failed to appear for arraignment. Subsequently, the authorities apprehended the accused, and the surety and the State presented a consent order under which the surety would have been allowed to pay only five percent of the bond amount. The trial court gave the surety time to present evidence, which it did not do. On appeal, the court held that 1992 Ga. Laws p. 2933, § 4(d)(1) was not applicable. The court determined that pursuant to 1992 Ga. Laws p. 2933, § 4(d)(3) the surety, as the debtor and the party seeking the reduction of the debt under the statute, had the burden of producing evidence that it located the accused. The court noted that the surety would have earned a reduction of the bond amount by fulfilling one of the conditions set forth in the statute. The court concluded that the State's participation in the proposed consent order did not conclusively establish that one of the statutory conditions was met. Further, the court indicated that the surety was given adequate opportunity to present the prescribed evidence, and it failed to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's holding that the surety was not entitled to a reduction of the bond amount.

Dekalb County v. Genuine Parts Co.


A97A0392, A97A0400, A97A0499.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


225 Ga. App. 376; 484 S.E.2d 57; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 404; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1357



March 11, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Denied June 27, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ga. LEXIS 669 and 1997 Ga. LEXIS 667.


PRIOR HISTORY: Taxation. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Castellani.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. A97A0499. Judgments reversed in Case Nos. A97A0392 and A97A0400.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the decision of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee trucking companies partial summary judgment in a taxation action. The trucking companies claimed they were entitled to refunds because the vehicles acquired tax situs in states other than Georgia and were not subject to the unapportioned value of the vehicles assessed by and paid to the county.


OVERVIEW: The county appealed two separate rulings that were consolidated for appeal. On appeal, the court reversed one decision and affirmed another decision of the trial court. The court found that the trial court erred in finding the first trucking company's claim for a refund fell within on of the exceptions allowed by Gwinnett County. The court also found that Georgia law provided under Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-311 which challenged the unapportioned assessment of the ad valorem tax, the law also provided other avenues of review available to an aggrieved taxpayer or trucking company that challenged the validity of a tax prior to remittance of taxes but because the trucking company failed to pursue any of those remedies, the trial court erred in allowing the first trucking company to proceed under § 48-5-311 for a refund of a portion of the ad valorem taxes they paid on their trucks. The court also concluded that the second trucking company's motion for partial summary judgment was properly denied based on the findings of the first trucking company.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the second trucking company's motion for partial summary judgment. The court reversed the trial court's decision that concerned the first trucking company and found that the trucking company had failed to pursue other avenues of review of the ad valorem tax and was not entitled to bring them under the state statute which governed the unapportioned assessment of the ad valorem tax.

 

1494 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Allen v. Hub Cap Heaven


A96A2051. A96A2052.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


225 Ga. App. 533; 484 S.E.2d 259; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 300; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1274; 1997-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P71,761



March 5, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 18, 1997. Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hassett, Cohen, Beitchman & Goldstein, Lee S. Goldstein, for Allen et al.

Wilson, Brock & Irby, Richard W. Wilson, Jr., James S. Teague, Jr., for Hubcap Masters International, Inc.

Drew, Eckl & Farnham, Peter B. Barlow, J. William Haley, Alston & Bird, G. Conley Ingram, Jay D. Bennett, Timothy G. Werner, for Hub Cap Heaven, Inc.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part in Case No. A96A2052. Judgment reversed in Case No. A96A2051.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, franchisees and competing company, appealed the judgment of a Georgia trial court, which granted an injunction with no geographic limits prohibiting the franchisees and the competing company from franchising, operating, or advising others about the operation of stores selling hubcaps, wheels, and related automotive accessories. The company also appealed the order denying its request for written findings of fact and conclusions of law.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court examined the grounds for the injunction and found none valid. The court held that the information franchisor claimed it needed to protect did not qualify as trade secrets. Thus, the Trade Secrets Act did not support the grant of the interlocutory injunction. For instance, the franchisor did claim the franchisee misappropriated a tangible supplier list, and the franchisee's personal knowledge of the franchisor's suppliers was not a trade secret. Also, the injunction could not be upheld as a remedy for breach of a confidential relationship because no such relationship existed where the franchise contract expressly provided for an independent contractor relationship between franchisor and its franchisees. The court held that one party was not under any duty to represent or advance the other's interests. The court further held that the injunction could not be based on the noncompetition clause of the franchise agreement because it was overbroad and void. The court also held that the franchisor's fraud claim failed because it did not show damages resulted from a false representation made by the franchisees and competing company.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of the injunction against the franchisees and competing company and affirmed the order denying the company's request for written findings of fact and conclusions of law.

 

1495 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Thompson v. Long


A96A1997.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


225 Ga. App. 719; 484 S.E.2d 666; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 253; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1018



February 25, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 26, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied September 5, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ga. LEXIS 764. Certiorari Denied March 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1498.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice; statute of repose. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Lovett, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient brought a medical malpractice action against defendant doctor alleging negligence in her prenatal care that resulted in the death of her unborn child. The Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) dismissed the patient's complaint. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued that the five-year statute of repose was unconstitutional in that it arbitrarily distinguished medical malpractice claimants from all other personal injury claimants and subjected medical malpractice claimants to abrogation of their claims, that her refiled complaint should relate back to the original complaint, and that her complaint included claims of simple negligence resulting in personal injuries that are not barred by the statute of repose. The court concluded that the patient's complaint was properly dismissed as barred by the statute of repose. The court found that the statute of repose Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-71(b) was constitutional and that the refiled complaint did not relate back to the original complaint. The patient did not assert any claims of simple negligence against the doctor. Thus, the patient's medical malpractice claims were barred by the five-year statute of repose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that dismissed the patient's complaint.

 

1496 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Glisson v. Hosp. Auth.


A96A2128.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


224 Ga. App. 649; 481 S.E.2d 612; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 174; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 629



February 14, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice. Lowndes Superior Court. Before Judge Horkan.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a former patient, sought review of an order entered in the Lowndes Superior Court (Georgia), which granted the motion to dismiss the former patient's amended complaint filed by appellees, a hospital and associated individuals, in a medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: After contacting an attorney eight days prior to the running of the statute of limitations, the former patient filed a medical malpractice action without the expert's affidavit required by Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1(a). After the statute ran, the hospital and associated individuals filed a motion to dismiss on grounds that the complaint did not specifically plead pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1(b) that, because of time constraints, an affidavit could not be prepared and filed at the time the original complaint was filed. The trial court dismissed the former patient's amended complaint that added allegations that that she was unable to obtain the affidavit because of time constraints. Applying a rule of liberal construction and concluding that the provisions of Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1 were intended to be procedural, the court held that the trial court erred in dismissing the amended complaint because the body of the complaint was properly amended, under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-15, to include the language of Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1 (b) and because the former patient filed an expert's affidavit within the extended filing time within Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1 (b).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the former patient's amended complaint in a medical malpractice action against the hospital and associated individuals.
