Dutton v. State


A96A2124.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


225 Ga. App. 67; 483 S.E.2d 305; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 190; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 651



February 14, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 4, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Denied May 30, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ga. LEXIS 571.


PRIOR HISTORY: Delusional compulsion defense. Polk Superior Court. Before Judge Cummings.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Polk Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of simple battery, misdemeanor obstruction of an officer, burglary, aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, and criminal trespass.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with simple battery, misdemeanor obstruction of an officer, burglary, aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, and criminal trespass. The trial court convicted defendant. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court improperly applied the third element of the delusional compulsion defense. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that: (1) the weight of authority supported the trial court's construction of the justification criterion of the compulsion defense; (2) it was an established practice in Georgia courts to construe the justification criterion as requiring legal justification for defendant's acts and to evaluate the evidence in light of the justification statutes; and (3) it was proper for the trial court to use the general law of self-defense and Ga. Code Ann. § 16-3-20(6) to determine whether defendant had met the justification criterion of the delusional compulsion defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of simple battery, misdemeanor obstruction of an officer, burglary, aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, and criminal trespass.

 

1498 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Lombard Corp. v. Collins


A97A0150.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


224 Ga. App. 282; 480 S.E.2d 47; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 43; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 129



January 16, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certified question to the Supreme Court of Georgia.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a decision of the superior court (Georgia), which dismissed the taxpayer's action to dispute a tax assessment against appellee tax officials.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer sought to challenge the constitutionality of Georgia's intangible tax, Ga. Code Ann. § 48-6-20 et seq. However, a third party interloper paid the tax without the taxpayer or the trial court's consent. The trial court dismissed the taxpayer's action for lack of jurisdiction because the action had become moot. On appeal, the taxpayer argued that the action was not moot because the taxpayer's court costs had not been paid. The court was unable to determine from existing authority the answer to the question of whether the taxpayer's constitutional right was violated by the mooting of the action by reason of the payment of the taxes in question by a third party. Accordingly, the court certified the question along with related questions to the Georgia Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: The question of whether the taxpayer's constitutional right was violated by the mooting of the action by reason of the payment of the taxes in question by a third party was certified to the Georgia Supreme Court. Certain related questions were also certified.

 

1499 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Williams v. State


A96A1734.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


224 Ga. App. 368; 481 S.E.2d 535; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 37; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 161



January 15, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 28, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. As Amended. Certiorari Denied May 2, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ga. LEXIS 482.


PRIOR HISTORY: D.U.I. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the DeKalb State Court (Georgia), which entered a conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding. After being administered several field sobriety tests, defendant was arrested for DUI. Defendant subsequently submitted to a State-administered breath test on an Intoxilyzer 5000, producing results of .090 and .089. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court improperly admitted the results of his breath test and improperly denied his motion for new trial. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that the trial court properly admitted the certificate of inspection showing that the Intoxilyzer 5000 was in good working order in December 1994 because (1) Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-392 (f) did not mandate that the breathalyzer's certificate of inspection be prepared on the day of inspection, and (2) defendant failed to cite any authority that mandated an inspection of the instrument immediately after his test. The court also held that the trial court did not err in charging the jury on the presumptions of intoxication at various blood-alcohol levels established by Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-392(b) because it was not necessary for the State to show defendant's blood-alcohol level at the time he was initially stopped.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

1500 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Lewis v. Uselton


A96A1783.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


224 Ga. App. 428; 480 S.E.2d 856; 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 30; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 131



January 14, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 31, 1997. Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Denied May 2, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Ga. LEXIS 484.


PRIOR HISTORY: Legal malpractice. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Workman.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in part and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of the judgment of the State Court of DeKalb County (Georgia), which entered judgment for appellee clients for damages on their counterclaim for legal malpractice.


OVERVIEW: The clients discharged the attorney after he settled the clients' personal injury lawsuit against a county with the county's insurance carrier in violation of the clients' specific instructions. The clients repudiated the settlement, and the attorney filed a complaint against the clients for unpaid attorney fees. The clients filed a counterclaim for legal malpractice. A jury: (1) determined that the county was liable to the clients and fixed the clients' special and general damages, which was later reduced by a personal injury protection set-off; and (2) after the trial court granted the clients' motion for directed verdict on the legal malpractice claim, awarded the clients their attorney fees and litigation expenses, but did not award punitive damages to the clients. The court held that the trial court did not err when it entered judgment against the attorney for an amount that was greater than the amount the attorney contended was the maximum the judgment could have been, but the court held that the amount of damages computed by the trial court was calculated incorrectly. The court held that the jury verdict had to be reduced to insurance policy limits before any set-offs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, except that it reversed and remanded with directions that the trial court had to properly recalculate the amount of the judgment for the clients.

 

1501 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Westbury Square Townhouses Ass'n v. Bryan


A96A2258.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


223 Ga. App. 885; 479 S.E.2d 190; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 1322; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 4381



December 9, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Nonprofit corporations; inspection of rewards. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Joyner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nonprofit corporation sought review of an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) directing it to allow appellee member to inspect and copy certain corporate records, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 14-3-1604, and to pay the member costs and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: When the nonprofit corporation did not respond to the member's request inspection and copying of certain corporate records, the member filed an application for an order allowing inspection and copying of the records and for costs and attorney fees under § 14-3-1604. The superior court granted the member's request without notifying the nonprofit corporation of the application. On appeal, the court vacated the order. The court held that the proceedings violated the nonprofit corporations' due process rights to notice. Due process required a procedure that provided notice to the nonprofit corporation, and § 14-3-1604 did not specify a procedure to be used. Thus, the court suggested that the following procedure be used for obtaining corporate records: (1) The member was to file an application with the superior court for an order requiring access and awarding costs and attorney fees; (2) the application was to be served on the nonprofit corporation pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-4; and (3) the superior court was to expedite a hearing on the matter, and the hearing may be set by rule nisi. The nonprofit corporation did not have the right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the superior court's order directing the nonprofit corporation to allow the member to inspect and copy certain corporate records and to pay costs and attorney fees. The court remanded the case for a new hearing complying with due process notice requirements.

 

1502 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Ga. Bd. of Dentistry v. Pence


A96A1390, A96A1391.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


223 Ga. App. 603; 478 S.E.2d 437; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 1249; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 4159



November 19, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Dentistry license; suspension. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Cook.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. A96A1391. Judgment reversed in Case No. A96A1390.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Georgia Board of Dentistry appealed the decision of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which reversed the board's determination against defendant dentist in an administrative disciplinary proceeding. The dentist cross-appealed, alleging that the trial court refused to rule on certain claims.


OVERVIEW: After patient complaints, the board of dentistry initiated disciplinary proceedings against a dentist. A hearing officer recommended suspension, probation, and a fine, and the board adopted the findings but increased the sanctions against the dentist. Pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 50-13-19, the trial court reviewed the board's determination and reversed on the grounds of due process violations. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court and affirmed the board's determination. It held that the fact that the board was both the accuser and judge did not deprive the dentist of due process of law, especially since she had the opportunity to seek judicial review. The court also found that each member of the board testified unequivocally that he or she did not consider any information in deliberations that was not a part of the hearing record as developed before the hearing officer. The board was not required to meet additional requirements of specifying factual data supporting its reasons for imposing harsher sanctions on the dentist. The court found the dentist's assertions in her cross-appeal to be either waived or without merit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court dismissing the decision of the board of dentistry, but affirmed on the dentist's cross-appeal.

 

1503 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Grantham v. Grantham


A96A2054.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


224 Ga. App. 1; 479 S.E.2d 370; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 1215; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 4056



November 7, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 11, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Child custody. Coffee Superior Court. Before Judge Holton.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and case remanded for proper proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order from the Coffee Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee grandmother custody of a child.


OVERVIEW: The mother appealed a decision of the trial court granting permanent custody of a child to the grandmother. On appeal, the court vacated and remanded the judgment. The court held that there was no evidence in a hearing either of the mother's unfitness or the best interests of the child. Whether the case was adjudged under the "clear and convincing evidence of unfitness" standard which had been the law in cases involving a custody challenge by a third party or under the new law creating a "best interests of the child" standard for third-party challengers to custody, there was no evidence warranting the actions of the trial court awarding custody of this child to the grandmother. The court also found that no valid judgment could have been rendered on the unsworn statements made in the hearing.


OUTCOME: An order of the lower court granting child custody to the grandmother in a case involving the mother was vacated and remanded.

 

1504 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Sledge v. State


A96A2444.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


223 Ga. App. 488; 477 S.E.2d 898; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 1209; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 4016



November 6, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Drug violation. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Karpf.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of selling cocaine in violation of the Georgia Controlled Substances Act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold cocaine to a confidential informant who was a convicted felon. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held: (1) defendant was not entitled to a mistrial when the informant implied that defendant had been involved in previous drug buys because the evidence explained the circumstances leading to defendant's arrest; (2) the State was not required to use a laboratory operated by the Division of Forensic Sciences of the Georgia Bureau of Investigation; (3) the trial court did not err when it allowed the State to play an audiotape of the drug transaction even though the State had not provided the tape to defendant 10 days prior to trial as required by Ga. Code Ann. § 17-16-1 et seq. because defendant was unable to establish any prejudice; (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it allowed the jury to rehear the audiotape after their deliberations had began; and (5) issues of credibility were for the jury to determine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of selling cocaine.

 

1505 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Watson v. Mayor of Savannah


A96A1274.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


223 Ga. App. 399; 477 S.E.2d 667; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 1171; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 3914



October 30, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 42 USC § 1983. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Brannen.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim appealed an order of the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia) that granted summary judgment to defendant city on the victim's claim for injuries received in a dispute with an off-duty policeman.


OVERVIEW: The policeman, moonlighting as a security guard at a nightclub, went to a neighboring club to see if his fellow officers, also moonlighting, needed help. When the victim greeted him with an offensive term, the officer grabbed him around his throat and swept his feet out from under him. The victim filed a complaint against the officer for assault and battery, which was amended to add a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim against the officer and the city. The city brought a motion for summary judgment contending that the officer was not acting under color of law and there was insufficient evidence that the officer was acting in conformity with any city policy at the time of the altercation. The trial court granted the motion, and the court affirmed. The court held that, pretermitting the issue of whether or not the trial court correctly found that the officer was acting under color of law, there was no evidence sufficient to show that the off-duty altercation was the result of an impermissible or corrupt policy which was intentional and deliberate. Even if it could be argued that the city failed to properly investigate the charges against the officer, it did not sustain a claim under § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that granted summary judgment to the city on the victim's claim for injuries received in a dispute with an off-duty policeman.

 

1506 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Dep't of Human Res. v. Phillips


A96A1449.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


223 Ga. App. 520; 478 S.E.2d 598; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 1158; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 3797



October 23, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration dismissed November 13, 1996. Certified Question To The Supreme Court Of Georgia.



DISPOSITION: Question certified to the Supreme Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Georgia Department of Human Resources (state) challenged a judgment from the trial court (Georgia), which awarded monetary damages to plaintiff mother for her daughter's life and for pain and suffering in a wrongful death and personal injury action. The daughter was a mental patient in a state hospital. The state contended that the judgment exceeded the statutory cap in Ga. Code Ann. § 50-21-29(b) (1992) of the Georgia Tort Claims Act.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the application of Ga. Code Ann. § 50-21-29(b) (1992), the part of the Georgia Tort Claims Act limiting damages recoverable against the state, would abridge the mother's state constitutional rights against retroactivity as provided in Ga. Const. art. I, § 1(X). The court acknowledged that the Georgia Supreme Court had exclusive appellate jurisdiction of the issue and that the case could not be transferred because the state as the appealing party did not contend that the limitation was contrary to the constitution, but that the trial court erred in not reducing the judgment to conform to it. The court opined that it could have presumed constitutionality, reversed the judgment, and remanded with instructions to reduce the judgment, but that would have merely decided constitutionality sub silentio, prompting a petition for certiorari. The court held that the more direct and proper approach was to seek instruction and not delay the appellate process, resolving the issue definitively before other errors were addressed. The court held that the issue was timely because until the verdict exceeded the statutory cap, no ruling was required. The question was certified.


OUTCOME: The court certified a question to the Supreme Court of Georgia, seeking instruction on whether the statutory caps limiting money damages recoverable by the mother under the Georgia Tort Claims Act in her daughter's wrongful death and personal injury action against the state were constitutional.

 

1507 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. D'Auria


A95A2655, A95A2656.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


222 Ga. App. 615; 475 S.E.2d 678; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 951



August 28, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Double jeopardy. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Case No. A95A2655 is remanded. Case No. A95A2656 is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision from the DeKalb State Court (Georgia), which granted defendant's plea in bar-double jeopardy based upon prosecutorial misconduct motion. Defendant sought review f the denial of his plea in bar-statute of limitations motion and his demurrer based on the unconstitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-22.1.


OVERVIEW: When it was discovered that the state withheld important information about a witness against defendant who was accused of sexual battery, the trial court ordered a new trial. Prior to the new trial the court granted defendant's plea in bar-double jeopardy based upon prosecutorial misconduct motion, but denied his plea-in bar-statute of limitation motion and his demurrer alleging the unconstitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-22. The state appealed the grant of the plea in bar and defendant appealed the denial of the other plea in bar and of his demurrer. The court determined the prosecutorial misconduct was an improper basis for granting the double jeopardy plea in bar without some evidence that the intent of the state was to cause a retrial by its improper conduct. Additionally, the court determined that neither it nor the trial court had the jurisdiction to determine the constitutional issue presented by defendant and that issue would not be ripe unless and until the state prevailed in the remanded double jeopardy issue in the trial court. The order of the trial court on the issue of double jeopardy was reversed and remanded and the constitutional issue was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the double jeopardy issue and dismissed the constitutionality issue.

 

1508 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Cody v. State


A96A1120. A96A1121.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


222 Ga. App. 468; 474 S.E.2d 669; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 875; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 3013



August 12, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Drug violation. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Jackson.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and codefendant sought review of the decision of the Gwinnett Superior Court (Georgia), which entered a jury verdict convicting them of trafficking in cocaine, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-31.


OVERVIEW: An informant arranged a meeting between defendant, codefendant, and an undercover detective. The informant said that he would accompany defendant and codefendant to the meeting and that they would arrive in a black Mercedes automobile. Thereafter, defendant purchased cocaine from the detective. While the drug buy was in progress, codefendant remained in the black Mercedes. A jury found defendant and codefendant guilty of trafficking in cocaine, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-31. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that codefendant's motion for a directed verdict of acquittal was properly denied because, while a finding of constructive possession had to be based on more than codefendant's spatial proximity to the cocaine, there was sufficient evidence that codefendant participated with defendant in the purchase of cocaine. Further, codefendant's motion challenging the life sentence provisions of Ga. Code Ann. §16-13-30(d) was properly denied because his constitutionality claim lacked evidence of purposeful racial discrimination or selective enforcement against codefendant. Finally, the evidence did not demand a finding that defendant was entrapped.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of defendant and codefendant for trafficking in cocaine.

 

1509 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Rabern v. State


A96A0135.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


221 Ga. App. 874; 473 S.E.2d 547; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 738; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 2739



June 26, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Forfeiture. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant real property owner sought review of a judgment from the Henry Superior Court (Georgia), which was rendered in favor of appellee state in an in rem forfeiture proceeding that was filed by the state pursuant to the forfeiture statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-49.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a complaint against the real property owner, instituting in rem forfeiture proceedings pursuant to the forfeiture statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-49. The proceedings were instituted after an April 1994 search of the real property produced 450 small marijuana plants and other related items. The trial court issued a judgment in the state's favor, and the real property owner appealed. On appeal, the court vacated the trial court's judgment and remanded for further determinations on the Eighth Amendment issue presented. The trial court properly ruled that the forfeiture statute was constitutional. The trial court also properly admitted into evidence certain hearsay testimony for determining probable cause and for explaining the conduct of the police officers. Further, the trial court properly ordered the property be forfeited to the state because an actual sale was not required for supporting forfeiture under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-49(e). However, the trial court erred in requiring forfeiture of the entire home and the entire tract of land to the state because such fine may have been excessive in violation of the Eighth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's judgment that was rendered in favor of the state on its in rem forfeiture complaint that was filed against the real property owner. It remanded for further determinations on the Eighth Amendment issue presented.

 

1510 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Melton v. State


A96A0900.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


221 Ga. App. 778; 472 S.E.2d 547; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 644; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 2581



June 19, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Kidnapping with bodily injury. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge White.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which conducted a resentencing hearing and sentenced defendant to life in prison. In his sole enumeration of error, defendant contended that he was sentenced to an unconstitutional, invalid, and excessive sentence that violated his constitutional guarantee against cruel and unusual punishment. Defendant had been convicted of kidnapping with bodily injury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to life as a recidivist following his conviction for kidnapping with bodily injury. On appeal of that decision, the court expressed concern over the use of the recidivist statute and remanded the action to determine the validity of defendant's sentence. On remand, the trial court conducted a resentencing hearing and sentenced defendant to life in prison. The court affirmed that decision. It was not disputed that under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-40(b), the only sentences authorized for a conviction of kidnapping with bodily injury were life imprisonment or death. However, defendant contended that the statute was unconstitutional. He attacked the statute because it robbed the trial court of any discretion to sentence him to a lighter sentence regardless of the severity of the injury. The court had previously considered and rejected that argument in other cases. Accordingly, that enumeration was without merit. Although defendant also argued that the evidence was insufficient to convict him of kidnapping with bodily injury, that issue was previously resolved against him by the court in the prior appeal. Moreover, that issue was not properly before the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which conducted a resentencing hearing and sentenced defendant to life in prison for his kidnapping with bodily injury conviction.

 

1511 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Braden v. Bell


A96A0659.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


222 Ga. App. 144; 473 S.E.2d 523; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 621; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 2500



June 14, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 9, 1996. Certiorari Applied for. Certiorari Denied October 18, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ga. LEXIS 1077.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice's statute of repose. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Langham.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant decedent's widow sought review of the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted defendants, hospital and physicians', motions for judgment on the pleadings of the widow's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The widow's complaint was filed on June 1, 1995, alleging that defendants committed medical malpractice in March 1984 by failing to diagnose that the decedent had a malignant carcinoma of the testes. The decedent died on June 3, 1993. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the complaint was barred by Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-71, which barred a medical malpractice action from being brought more than five years from the negligent act or omission. The complaint alleged that the negligent diagnosis occurred in March 1984, however, the complaint was not filed until 1995. Therefore, the action was barred under § 9-3-71.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings of the widow's medical malpractice action.

 

1512 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Dowdy v. Earthwise Rest. Mgmt.


A96A0021.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


221 Ga. App. 220; 471 S.E.2d 42; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 452; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 1940



May 2, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Workers' compensation. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Carnes.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of an order from the Fulton State Court (Georgia), which dismissed her complaint for premises liability against appellee third-party tortfeasors, because it was time-barred under Ga. Code Ann. § 34-9-11.1(c).


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that § 34-9-11.1(c) provided that an employee suing a third-party tortfeasor had to institute an action within one year of the injury or her rights were automatically assigned to the employer or the employer's insurer. Upon review, the court observed that shortly after the trial court's order, § 34-9-11.1(c) was amended, and required an employee to bring its third-party action within the applicable statute of limitations, which was two years under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-33. The language that automatically assigned an employee's claim was not found in the new legislation. The court noted that Ga. Code Ann. § 34-9-11.1(e) provided that the amended provisions were to apply retroactively to injuries occurring on or after July 1, 1992. The employee's injury occurred on August 12, 1992. Because the statute was given retroactive effect, the court found that the automatic assignment language did not apply to the employee's action, and she brought it within the applicable statute of limitations. The court stated that the tortfeasors had no vested right in the assignment of her claim under Ga. Code Ann. § 34-9-11.1(c). The court reversed the dismissal of her complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the employee's action against the tortfeasors.

 

1513 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Thedieck v. Thedieck


A95A2608, A95A2609.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


220 Ga. App. 764; 470 S.E.2d 265; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 334; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 1518



March 15, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Contempt. Thomas Superior Court. Before Judge Lott, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in part, reversed in part, vacated in part and cases remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted respondent wife's application for a discretionary appeal of the decision of the Thomas Superior Court (Georgia), which held her in contempt for violating the visitation provisions of a child custody order. Petitioner husband had filed for contempt charges alleging that the wife had willfully deprived him of visits with the child. The trial court ordered the wife jailed if she did not made the child available for visitation.


OVERVIEW: The parties were divorced. The trial court also ordered that the wife could purge herself of the contempt by paying attorney fees and costs. The wife contended on appeal that the adjudication was criminal, not civil contempt, that an award of attorney fees was not part of any prior order, thus she could not be held in contempt for failure to pay fees which were not due yet, that the incarceration sanction was excessive, and that the evidence to support the adjudication was insufficient. The court found that to the extent that the trial court's order conditioned the wife's avoidance of, or release from, incarceration upon payment of attorney fees, it was erroneous. Thus, that portion of the trial court's order was reversed. However, the court found that though the manner of imposing incarceration for not paying the fees was improper, the actual award of attorney fees to the husband was authorized. However, in making that award, the trial court failed to properly consider the husband's financial circumstances and the order was vacated with respect to the amount of attorney fees and the case was remanded for a more detailed consideration of the parties' financial circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, in part, reversed, in part, and vacated, in part, and the case was remanded with direction.

 

1514 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Allsouth Stevedoring Co. v. Wilson


A95A2379. A95A2541.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


220 Ga. App. 205; 469 S.E.2d 348; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 144; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 686; 1996 AMC 1874



February 14, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied May 3, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ga. LEXIS 570.


PRIOR HISTORY: Workers' compensation. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Karpf.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, employer and former employer, challenged the decision of the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia), affirming the award of compensation to appellee claimant. They disputed the claim for benefits under the Georgia Workers Compensation Act (Act), Ga. Code Ann. § 34-9-1 et seq., claiming the Longshoremen's & Harbor Workers' Compensation Act (LHWCA), 33 U.S.C.S. § 901 et seq., had exclusive jurisdiction and disclaimed responsibility.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was injured while an employee of the former employer and received LHWCA compensation. While he was on leave, appellants' merger agreement ended and he returned to work as an employee of the employer. The claimant continued to experience back pain and began experiencing muscle cramps in his leg. He suffered a cramp while at work that rendered him unable to get off a ladder. He applied for benefits under the LHWCA and the state act. The administrative law judge granted him benefits under the state act and found that his claim constituted a change in condition, which decision was affirmed by the appellate division and the superior court. The court also affirmed, finding that while the claimant's injury was clearly compensable under the LHWCA because it occurred on navigable waters, it was also covered under the state act as neither federal nor Georgia law precluded such coverage. In addition, the claim constituted a change in condition, as his duties at work were the same, he began having the muscle cramps after the initial injury, they gradually worsened, and the claimant had no other traumatic incident or injury that caused him to stop work.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was concurrent jurisdiction under the LHWCA and the state act and that the claim constituted a change in condition, not a new injury. It the affirmed the award of benefits to the claimant under the state act, holding the former employer responsible for the award, and reliving the employer of responsibility.

 

1515 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Banks v. Ga. Power Co.


A95A2039.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


220 Ga. App. 84; 469 S.E.2d 218; 1996 Ga. App. LEXIS 51; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 389



January 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 6, 1996. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied May 3, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ga. LEXIS 576.


PRIOR HISTORY: Condemnation. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Story.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of the judgment from the Hall Superior Court (Georgia), which entered judgment of a taking in favor of appellee power company, resolved the non-value issues against the landowner, and found that the issues of value needed to be tried to a jury.


OVERVIEW: The power company instituted a special master proceeding to condemn a portion of a tract of the landowner's property as an easement for a right-of-way in order to construct, operate, and maintain a high-voltage electric power line. The landowner appealed to the superior court that entered a judgment of taking, and on appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court concluded that: (1) the power company had statutory authority to utilize a special master proceeding for the condemnation; (2) the power company established that a quick taking, as provided for in the special master proceeding, was necessary due to recent blackouts; (3) the court had no authority to determine the constitutional challenges to the condemnation statutes because the court received the case on a transfer order, which stated that the superior court had not made any constitutional rulings; (4) the power company had to have a right to enter the easement in order to utilize the easement as allowed by law; and (5) the appeal to the superior court was a de novo proceeding and an appeal by either party entitled both parties to a de novo determination of the issue of value or damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of a taking in favor of the power company against the landowner.

 

1516 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



In re I. B.


A95A1729.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


219 Ga. App. 268; 464 S.E.2d 865; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 1027; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 3819



December 1, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Moot issue; constitutional challenge. Fulton Juvenile Court. Before Judge Jones.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father sought review of the judgment from the Fulton Juvenile Court (Georgia), which declared petitioner's challenge of the constitutionality of the statute establishing the child abuse registry, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 49-5-184 (c), to be moot and not subject to an exception. The issues were whether the trial court had jurisdiction and whether petitioner was entitled to a ruling on the constitutionality issue.


OVERVIEW: Following the judgment that held that petitioner father's challenge to the constitutionality of the child abuse registry, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 49-5-184 (c) was moot and not subject to an exception was appealed by petitioner. Petitioner argued that the question was not moot because there was a reasonable expectation that his name would again be placed on the registry. The court affirmed, holding that speculation did not save the constitutional issue from being moot by the expungement. Additionally, the court reasoned that expungement left no existing facts or rights. The court held that neither could the trial court merely advise petitioner of the legal aspects of possible future consequences of possible future action on petitioner's part. Additionally, the court found that the trial court had no discretion to rule on the question of the statute's constitutionality. The court concluded that the issue was not saved from mootness, even applying a broad view of nonmootness.


OUTCOME: The judgment that declared petitioner father's challenge of the constitutionality of the statute establishing the child abuse registry as being moot was affirmed. The court found that petitioner's name had been expunged and as such left no existing facts or rights at stake. The court reasoned that it had no authority to render an advisory opinion regarding what petitioner feared could arise at a future date.

 

1517 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Collins v. At&T


A95A1347.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


219 Ga. App. 196; 464 S.E.2d 642; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 1009; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 3836



November 29, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied April 1, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ga. LEXIS 671.


PRIOR HISTORY: Taxation. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Langham.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax commissioner reapportioned appellee taxpayers' income and deductions after an audit asserting that the taxpayers used the wrong method of apportionment. The Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) held that the taxpayers were entitled to choose their own method of apportionment. The tax commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers utilized the unitary method of apportioning their income when filing their tax returns pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 48-7-31(d)(3). Under that method, each return determined the taxpayer's taxable income by taking the combined net income of the taxpayer and the other affiliated companies and apportioning that total income based on the ratio of the particular taxpayer's property, payroll, and gross receipts in the state to the property, payroll and gross receipts everywhere for the affiliates. The state revenue department audited the taxpayers' state income tax returns, determined each taxpayer's tax liability based only on the particular taxpayer's income and deductions, and apportioned income using a different apportionment method. The lower court held that the taxpayers were entitled to choose their own method of apportionment. On appeal by the tax commissioner, the court affirmed the lower court's decision. Because Ga. Code Ann. § 48-7-31(d)(3) did not specify the method of apportionment to be used by taxpayers, they were free to choose their own method of apportionment, including the unitary method of apportionment that they had selected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which held that the taxpayers were entitled to use their chosen method of apportionment.

 

1518 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Tidwell v. State


A95A2234.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


219 Ga. App. 233; 464 S.E.2d 834; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 1004; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 3558



November 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 30, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Child molestation. Lamar Superior Court. Before Judge Craig.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Lamar Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of two counts of child molestation involving the same victim, enumerating 13 errors. The appeal was transferred by the Georgia Supreme Court when it determined that the constitutional issues raised involved the application of well-settled principles and the appeal brought no new issues within its jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and convicted after school authorities notified the State about a possible child abuse case involving the 10-year-old female victim. The jury heard numerous witnesses but there was no physical evidence of molestation. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that: (1) Georgia's Child Hearsay Statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 24-3-16, was constitutional; (2) the trial court properly determined that the victim's out-of-court statements had sufficient indicia of reliability; (3) defendant's prior sodomy conviction was admissible because it was sufficiently similar to the offenses charged; (4) the trial court did not err in permitting the victim's mother to testify about the victim's intelligence level and knowledge of right and wrong; (5) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for mistrial after the victim's mother testified as to defendant's intoxication because the trial court issued a curative instruction and defendant did not request further instructions or renew his motion for a mistrial; and (6) the trial court did not err in excluding testimony related to the victim's sexual contacts with other persons.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

1519 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Keith v. State


A95A1445.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


218 Ga. App. 729; 463 S.E.2d 51; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 860; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 3173



October 13, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Demand for jury trial. Clayton State Court. Before Judge Arnold.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Clayton State Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of the misdemeanor offense of permitting another to unlawfully operate a vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of permitting another to unlawfully operate her vehicle. Defendant sought review of her conviction, contending that the trial court erred by requiring her to be tried without her attorney present and by conducting her trial without a jury. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to determine if defendant had waived her right to a jury trial. The court held that defendant had a right to counsel because imprisonment was a possible sentence for the crime of which she was charged and that the burden of proof that defendant knowingly and waived her right to counsel was upon the State. The court held that the record was insufficient to support the finding that defendant had waived her right to counsel. The court also held that when a defendant proceeded pro se, defendant's failure to request a jury trial was not sufficient to prove a waiver of defendant's right to a jury trial. The court held that the State had the burden to prove defendant had waived her right to a jury trial and that the record was not sufficient to determine if she waived her right.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for permitting another to unlawfully operate her vehicle and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to determine if defendant had waived her right to a jury trial.

 

1520 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Gwinnett County v. King


A95A1381.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


218 Ga. App. 800; 463 S.E.2d 511; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 891; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 3146



October 4, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 25, 1995. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied January 26, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ga. LEXIS 287.


PRIOR HISTORY: Improper confinement, etc. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Oxendine.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county, warden of county correctional institute and diversion center, and classification officer at the correctional institute and diversion center sought review of an order of the Gwinnett Superior Court (Georgia) that denied their motions for summary judgment in appellee inmate's action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for alleged improper confinement and various tort claims under state law.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced to 12 months confinement, but the sentence allowed that upon 90 days work release, the remainder could have been served on probation. His participation in the program was terminated, following a disciplinary proceeding, after he reported to work drunk. He was placed in the county correctional institute to serve his full sentence in accordance with the trial court's order. The inmate's action against appellants, brought pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, alleged improper confinement, the denial of credit for time served, and improper termination from the program. The court reversed the denial of appellants' motions for summary judgment. Given the terms of the sentence imposed, a supplemental order of the trial court, and the inmate's agreement to participate under terms that authorized no good-time credit for participation in the program, the inmate's right to good-time credit was not established and the defense of qualified immunity defeated the claims against the warden and officer. Further, the inmate identified no county policy which was responsible for any of the alleged deprivations, and therefore, he could not prevail on his claim against the county.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed the trial court's denial of appellants' motions for summary judgment and remanded the case with directions.

 

1521 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Allstate Ins. v. Duncan


A95A1286, A95A1287.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


218 Ga. App. 552; 462 S.E.2d 638; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 820; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2935



September 19, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Dismissed January 5, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ga. LEXIS 199.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action on policy. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Cook.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Consolidated appeals from decisions of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) holding that a Georgia court has jurisdiction over a John Doe uninsured motorist accident in Missouri.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a Georgia resident, was injured in an auto accident caused by an unknown uninsured motorist (John Doe) in Missouri, and was insured by defendant under a Missouri policy that included uninsured motorist coverage. Plaintiff sued John Doe in Georgia and defendant unsuccessfully moved to dismiss on jurisdictional grounds. The reviewing court held that Ga. Code Ann. § 33-7-11(d)(1) addressed residency in cases where a trial court was unable to exercise in personam jurisdiction over an unknown nonresident uninsured motorist, and the action should proceed as if it were a John Doe action. The court further held that defendant's assertion that the exercise of jurisdiction would be unconstitutional if the John Doe did not have sufficient minimum contacts with Georgia did not violate his due process rights because any judgment against John Doe would not be an in personam judgment.


OUTCOME: Decisions reversed because a Georgia statute that bestows jurisdiction over out-of-state uninsured motorists was applicable.

 

1522 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Smith v. City of Lagrange


A95A1158.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


218 Ga. App. 394; 461 S.E.2d 550; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 746; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2704



August 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 24, 1995. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied November 9, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ga. LEXIS 1192.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action on contract, etc. Troup Superior Court. Before Judge Keeble.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retired employees sought review of the decision of the Troup Superior Court (Georgia), which granted the summary judgment motion of defendant employer in an action alleging a violation of the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and Georgia Constitutions, for breach of employment contract, for breach of fiduciary duty, and for negligence and fraud in the administration of a retirement benefit plan.


OVERVIEW: The employer, a city, offered a retirement benefit plan. The city's mayor and council proposed two early retirement programs. The first incentive program allowed certain employees to retire and receive a monthly contribution toward their post-retirement health insurance premium until Medicare eligibility. The second incentive program allowed certain employees to retire and receive free health insurance until Medicare eligibility. Thereafter, the employees filed an action against the city for, inter alia, a violation of their equal protection rights and for breach of fiduciary duty. The trial court granted the employer summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that because one employee retired prior to the adoption of either program, the administration of the program did not affect his rights. Further, because the other employees retired prior to the administration of the second program, its administration did not affect their rights. Thus, the employees did not have standing to bring an equal protection challenge. Moreover, the employer's lack of knowledge and inability to predict city council's conduct precluded the employees' claim for breach of any duty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision granting the employer's summary judgment motion in the action alleging a violation of the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and Georgia Constitutions, for breach of employment contract, for breach of fiduciary duty, and for negligence and fraud in the administration of the employer's retirement benefit plan.

 

1523 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Bergmann v. McCullough


A95A1300. A95A1301.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


218 Ga. App. 353; 461 S.E.2d 544; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 718; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2632



August 2, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 16, 1995. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied November 9, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ga. LEXIS 1195.


PRIOR HISTORY: Adoption. Candler Superior Court. Before Judge McMillan.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. A95A1300. Appeal dismissed in Case No. A95A1301.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a natural father and paternal grandmother, challenged the judgment of the Candler Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee step-father's petition to adopt a minor child and granted the grandmother limited visitation of the minor child under Ga. Code Ann. § 19-8-19, upon her motion to intervene in the adoption proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The minor child was born out of wedlock shortly after the natural father was incarcerated for two 15-year sentences in a correctional institution in Wisconsin. The mother and step-father were married in Indiana and moved with the minor child to Georgia. An Indiana trial court adjudged the natural father to be the minor child's natural father at his behest. Approximately two months later, the step-father commenced the underlying adoption proceeding. An Indiana court granted the petition for grandparent visitation rights. The trial court granted the petition to adopt and the petition for grandparent visitation rights, and the natural father and grandmother appealed. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Indiana's court did not make a custody determination, and the visitation determination was made after the child had lived in Georgia for over six months. Thus, the Parental Kidnapping Prevention Act, 28 U.S.C.S. § 1738A, did not apply, and Georgia could properly exercise jurisdiction. There was clear and convincing evidence that supported the order of adoption, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion. The visitation issue was moot, and the court dismissed it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1524 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Saleem v. Snow


A95A0117.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


217 Ga. App. 883; 460 S.E.2d 104; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 628; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2547



July 14, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Armed robbery, etc. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Jenrette.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner filed an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the Georgia Tort Claims Act against defendants parole board and corrections department employees in the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia). The trial court denied the convicted criminal's motion for partial summary judgment, granted summary judgment to the state employees and denied as moot several other motions filed by the prisoner. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that: (1) the prisoner's claims concerning disciplinary problems were time-barred; (2) the corrections employee was entitled to qualified immunity on the federal claims for damages; (3) the trial court correctly applied the doctrine of legislative immunity; (4) no reasonable person would have believed that a state official's reliance on unvacated criminal convictions violated clearly established federal law; (5) the trial court correctly ruled that the Open Meetings Act did not apply to parole deliberations; (6) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting the defendants to withdraw admissions; (7) because the trial court had already resolved the case, denial of the prisoner's motion to amend was not an abuse of discretion; (8) the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying the prisoner's motion for appointment of counsel; (9) the trial court did not err in failing to extend discovery; (10) the trial court properly denied the prisoner's request for public funds to cover transcription costs; and (11) the trial court correctly refused to order the clerk to certify the transcript the prisoner prepared from memory for appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1525 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Miller v. Ga. Ports Auth.


A94A1448.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


217 Ga. App. 876; 460 S.E.2d 100; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 629; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2554



July 14, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Granted October 20, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ga. LEXIS 1104.


PRIOR HISTORY: Motion to dismiss. Chatham State Court. Before Judge Morse.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a longshoreman and his wife, appealed a judgment of the Chatham State Court (Georgia), which granted the motion of defendant Georgia Ports Authority in the personal injury and loss of consortium action brought by the longshoreman and his wife after the longshoreman was injured on the job. The trial court granted the Authority's motion to dismiss due to failure to comply with the provisions of the Georgia Tort Claims Act.


OVERVIEW: The longshoreman was injured at one of the Authority's terminals and he and his wife instituted an action claiming personal injury and loss of consortium. The Authority sought to dismiss on the basis that the Georgia Tort Claims Act had not been complied with and the trial court granted the motion. On an appeal by the longshoreman and his wife, the court affirmed, holding that the Act applied to the Authority. The court held that, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 50-21-22(5), the Act applied to, inter alia, "authorities" of the State of Georgia. When the Act was enacted, the Authority was already in existence and by its very name was an "authority" of Georgia. Absent evidence to the contrary, no change was intended in the Authority's status as to sovereign immunity and the Act therefore applied. The contention that the Act's notice requirements could not be applied to the present action retroactively was briefed and transferred to the State's high court, which transferred the case back to the court without explanation. Such a transfer was a final determination that no constitutional question was in fact properly raised, or if so raised, was not meritorious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the action by the longshoreman and his wife against the Authority.

 

1526 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Pratt & Whitney Can. v. Sanders


A95A0393.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


218 Ga. App. 1; 460 S.E.2d 94; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 635; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2462



July 14, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied December 1, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ga. LEXIS 1225.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Langford.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant aircraft engine manufacturer sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia) which denied appellant's motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction and insufficient service of process, denied appellant's motions for a new trial and a judgment notwithstanding the verdict, and entered judgment for appellee estate representatives. Appellee had brought a products liability action against appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellee estate representatives brought a products liability action against appellant aircraft engine manufacturer in the superior court. Appellee's action was related to a plane crash in which appellee's decedent was a passenger. The superior court denied appellant's motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction and insufficient service of process, denied appellant's motions for a new trial and a judgment notwithstanding the verdict, and entered judgment in favor of appellee. The court reversed the superior court's judgment. The court held that the superior court erred in denying appellant's motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction under the long arm statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-10-91, because appellee was not a Georgia resident, the plane crash did not occur in Georgia, appellant was not a Georgia corporation, and there were not sufficient minimum contacts between appellant and Georgia under § 9-10-91 to have provided the superior court with a basis for asserting jurisdiction over appellant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's entry of judgment in favor of appellee estate representatives and the superior court's denial of appellant aircraft engine manufacturer's motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction. The court held that under the long arm statute there were not sufficient minimum contacts between appellant and Georgia to have provided the superior court with a basis for asserting jurisdiction over appellant.

 

1527 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Hoesch Am. v. Dai Yang Metal Co.


A95A0689.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


217 Ga. App. 845; 459 S.E.2d 187; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 619



July 13, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on contract. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hancock.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), in which the court granted of motions of appellee, Korean corporation, to open the default judgment against it and to dismiss the complaint appellant had filed.


OVERVIEW: Appellee Korean corporation negotiated contract in Korea for purchase of steel. Appellant American corporation alleged that some of the steel it received was defective and filed a breach of contract action against appellee in Georgia. Appellee was served with process in Korea, but never answered or entered an appearance. Appellant received a default judgment against appellee. The trial court granted appellee's motions to open default judgment and dismiss complaint. The court affirmed the trial court, finding that appellee had not waived defense of lack of personal jurisdiction when appellee failed to answer the complaint. The court stated that a foreign corporation that was not transacting business within Georgia could not be forced to come into Georgia to defend against a claim or to contest jurisdiction. The court found that appellee had not transacted business within Georgia and did not have the minimum contacts with Georgia to give trial court jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed trial court, finding that appellee had not waived the defense of lack of personal jurisdiction when appellee failed to answer the complaint.

 

1528 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Murray County Sch. Dist. v. Adams


A95A0523.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


218 Ga. App. 220; 461 S.E.2d 228; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 703; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2089



June 21, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 28, 1995. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied November 17, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ga. LEXIS 1186.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action on contract. Murray Superior Court. Before Judge Boyett.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board sought review of a decision from the Murray Superior Court (Georgia) granting partial summary judgment to appellee teachers on the issue of liability in the teachers' class action suit challenging the board's decision to terminate the employer matching portion of a previously established annuity retirement savings plan for its employees. The teachers claimed the board's action violated Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. X (1983).


OVERVIEW: As an incentive to attract quality employees, the board offered a retirement savings plan to the school district's employees that fully matched participating employees' contributions of two percent of their salary and match 50 percent of additional contributions. When the board terminated the latter contribution provision from the plan, the employees filed suit claiming that termination of benefits was an unconstitutional impairment of contract in violation of Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. X (1983). The board appealed after the trial court granted the employees' motion for partial summary judgment on the issue of liability. The court held that the plan was a part of the employees' contracts, which provided for future amendment or termination of the plan at the board's discretion. Where the employment contracts provided that the terms of the plan could be modified or changed in the future, the participating employees never acquired a property right in the benefits. Because no property rights had vested, the modification did not violate the employees' constitutional rights. The judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: Partial summary judgment on the issue of liability granted in favor of the employees in their suit challenging the board's decision to terminate a portion of the employees' retirement savings benefits under the board's retirement plan was reversed.

 

1529 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Harvey v. State


A95A0357.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


217 Ga. App. 776; 459 S.E.2d 433; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 601; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2107



June 20, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 11, 1995. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Granted December 5, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ga. LEXIS 1246.


PRIOR HISTORY: Motion to suppress. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Eldridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) that denied his motion to suppress evidence after he was indicted for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: A police officer was dispatched to a public housing project to investigate suspicious activity involving a described individual. The officer saw a man matching the description talking with two the men. Defendant was one of the three men. After the men provided identification, the officer called in their names to his dispatcher. A computer check revealed that there was an outstanding bench warrant for defendant. Defendant was arrested pursuant to the bench warrant and searched incident to his arrest. The officer found cocaine in defendant's possession. Defendant was indicted for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. Later, it was determined that the bench warrant had been recalled four days before defendant's arrest. Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence. The trial court denied the motion, holding that a good faith exception applied. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed the denial of the motion to suppress. Although the court concluded that there was no good faith exception in Georgia, the search producing the evidence was still proper incident to a lawful arrest because the officer had probable cause at the time to make the arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence.

Action for a Clean Env't v. State


A95A0602.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA
