PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Jenrette.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff environmental groups sought review of an order of the Fulton Superior Court, which granted the motion of defendant, the State of Georgia, to dismiss their action in which they sought to have Ga. Code Ann. § 2-16-1, et seq. declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Ga. Code Ann. § 2-16-1, et seq. provided a cause of action to any producer, processor, marketer, or seller of agricultural or aquacultural product injured by disparaging remarks about their products. The State asserted that it had no legal interest adverse to the environmental groups and thus they had failed to establish the existence of a justiciable controversy. The court agreed, ruling that the trial court correctly dismissed the environmental groups' declaratory judgment action for failure to state a claim. The court reasoned that there was no party to the action who sought to uphold the constitutionality of the statute under attack. The court also held that the environmental groups' challenge to the statute giving rise to a cause of action for disparagement of perishable food products was not ripe for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision dismissing the environmental groups' action.

 

1531 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Kelly v. City of Atlanta


A95A0991.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


217 Ga. App. 365; 457 S.E.2d 675; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 415; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 1624



May 2, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Bonner, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon transfer from the Supreme Court of Georgia (supreme court), plaintiff taxpayer challenged the dismissal of his petition against defendants, City of Atlanta (city), Atlanta School District and its board members (school district), and Tax Commissioner of Fulton County (commissioner), to enjoin them from imposing a revenue sharing agreement allocating illegal local option sales taxes and collecting unconstitutional ad valorem taxes.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court transferred the action because the trial court made no ruling on the constitutional issues raised by the taxpayer. At the time of the trial court's hearing on defendants' motion to dismiss, substantially all of the challenged ad valorem taxes had been levied, collected, and disbursed by the city. The trial court denied the taxpayer's petition, finding that the taxpayer's relief was limited to the post-deprivation remedies of the tax refund statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-380, because the controversy that was the subject to the taxpayer's declaratory action was no longer under defendants' control. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the taxpayer's constitutional challenges lacked merit because the supreme court had exclusive jurisdiction to decide constitutional issues and its transfer of the taxpayer's appeal was tantamount to a ruling that eliminated and resolved the equitable and injunctive issues raised by the taxpayer. The court held that the trial court had properly dismissed the taxpayer's declaratory judgment action because the levied taxes at issue had been substantially collected and disbursed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in dismissing the taxpayer's declaratory judgment action against the city, school district, and commissioner to declare levied property taxes unconstitutional.

 

1532 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Envtl. Waste Reductions v. Legal Envtl. Assistance Found.


A94A2495. A94A2496.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


216 Ga. App. 699; 455 S.E.2d 393; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 246; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 1230



March 16, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Solid waste management permit. Quitman Superior Court. Before Judge Stone.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, applicant and the director of the Georgia Department of Natural Resources, sought discretionary review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Quitman County (Georgia), which reversed the decision of an administrative law judge that granted the applicant issuance of a permit to build and operate a biomedical waste disposal facility.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought a permit from the department to build and operate a biomedical waste disposal facility under Georgia's Comprehensive Solid Waste Management Act (Act). The director found the application met the requirements of the Act and issued the permit. Appellees, residents and a legal foundation, challenged issuance of the permit and appealed to the department. An administrative law judge (ALJ) affirmed the issuance after a hearing. The foundation appealed the decision to the trial court, which reversed the administrative decision. The court reversed, and held that: (1) the record amply supported the ALJ's finding that the need for the facility was shown; (2) the trial court erred in its failure to give the department's interpretation of the statute the deference to which it was entitled because the interpretation was reasonably and legally correct; and (3) the record supported the department's final decision and the trial court failed to give proper weight and deference to the director's and the ALJ's interpretation of planning requirements in the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and reinstated the decision of the administrative law judge that affirmed the issuance of the permit.

 

1533 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Blue Ridge Mt. Fisheries v. Dep't of Natural Res.


A94A2003.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


217 Ga. App. 89; 456 S.E.2d 651; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 350; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 1701



March 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsiderations Denied March 30, 1995. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied December 1, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ga. LEXIS 1238.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Flake.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, fishery and its owner (fishery), sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of DeKalb County (Georgia), which granted the motion of defendants, Department of Natural Resources and its officials (department), for summary judgment on the fishery's state tort claims and claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for deprivation of constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: Following a seizure of white sturgeon that were held by the fishery for breeding and caviar production, and the owner's arrest for possession of exotic fish without a wild animal license, the fishery filed a civil action against the department under Ga. Code Ann. § 27-5-8(b) to recover the sturgeon. The trial court declared the seizure was illegal and found that to the extent Ga. Code Ann. § 27-5-5(b)(6) criminalized the possession of exotic fish it was unconstitutionally vague and that sturgeon were not exotic fish. The criminal charges were then dismissed. The fishery then instituted an action that asserted state tort claims and claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against the department for deprivation of constitutional rights. The department filed a motion for summary judgment and the fishery filed a motion for partial summary judgment. The trial court granted the department's motion and denied the fishery's motion. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part and held that: (1) the department officials were not entitled to qualified immunity from the fishery's claims under § 1983; and (2) summary judgment was error on the unlawful seizure claim but not the unlawful arrest claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's decision that granted the department and its employees summary judgment.

 

1534 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Griffith v. Brooks


A94A2776.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


216 Ga. App. 401; 454 S.E.2d 602; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 158; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 778



February 23, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Termination of parental rights. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Oxendine.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant biological father challenged the order of the Gwinnett Superior Court (Georgia), which upon retrial terminated his parental rights and granted the adoption petition of appellees, the mother and stepfather.


OVERVIEW: The mother and father were married when the child was born. The mother left the father four months later and married the stepfather, who voluntarily supported the child. The father ceased paying child support before the child was two years old and was later incarcerated. An earlier trial terminated the father's parental rights, but that decision was reversed and remanded on appeal. Upon retrial, the superior court found that the father had failed to support the child or establish a familial bond or communicate with the child after seven years, and therefore, it terminated the father's parental rights and granted the adoption petition. The father appealed and the court affirmed. The court rejected the father's assertion that he had paid support except when incarcerated because the evidence showed he was six months in arrears at the time of his incarceration. The court found that clear and convincing evidence supported the superior court's determination under Ga. Code Ann. § 19-8-10 that the father's failure to pay support or communicate with the child was without justifiable cause. The court found that the father's allegations of error were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the superior court, which terminated the father's parental rights and granted the adoption petition of the mother and stepfather.

 

1535 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Corey v. State


A94A2088.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


216 Ga. App. 180; 454 S.E.2d 154; 1995 Ga. App. LEXIS 78; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 436



January 31, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Armed robbery. Bartow Superior Court. Before Judge Howell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Bartow Superior Court (Georgia), which sentenced him to life imprisonment for armed robbery. Defendant contended that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to modify his sentence imposed under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-8-41(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-8-41(b), under which he was sentenced, was unconstitutionally vague because it provided two maximum sentences, one of life imprisonment and another of 20 years. The court indicated that it disagreed with defendant's argument because, although § 16-8-41(b) allowed the sentencing judge broad discretion, it did not provide two different maximum sentences and was not unconstitutionally vague. The court noted that although the courts of the state had consistently held that the maximum penalty upon conviction for armed robbery was life imprisonment, a court also was empowered to impose a determinable sentence of any period of time between 5 and 20 years. The court concluded that since Ga. Code Ann. § 16-8-41 (b) was clear in its provision for a maximum sentence of life imprisonment, and the sentence of life imprisonment imposed by the trial court was within that limit, there was no error in the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against defendant who was convicted of armed robbery and sentenced to life imprisonment.

 

1536 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Banks


A94A1411.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


215 Ga. App. 828; 452 S.E.2d 533; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 1390; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 4133



December 2, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 20, 1994. Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Condemnation. Carroll Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged an order of the Carroll Superior Court (Georgia), which held that defendant claimant, rather than the driver, owned a car that was seized during a drug raid and denied the State's petition for civil forfeiture pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 16-13-49.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that the claimant, rather than the driver, owned a car that was seized during a drug raid and denied the State's petition for civil forfeiture under § 16-13-49. The court affirmed that judgment on appeal. The court concluded that the claimant's ownership interest, as against the State, was complete when the driver voluntarily transferred possession of the vehicle for valuable consideration and the claimant obtained from the transferor the duly transferred certificate of title thereto several months before the drug raid. The court also held that the claimant's failure to register it so as to authorize its use and operation on the public highways did not defeat his legal ownership of the car, noting that the Motor Vehicle Certificate of Title Act, O.C.G.A. § 40-3-1 et seq., was a recording statute that was designed to perfect and to give notice of security interests. The court further found that the claimant proved that the driver's sale of the car was a valid transaction that had economic substance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a denial of the State's petition for civil forfeiture of the claimant's car, which was being operated by the driver, that was seized during a drug raid.

 

1537 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Barrett


A94A1910, A94A1911.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


215 Ga. App. 401; 451 S.E.2d 82; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 1262; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3778



November 17, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 2, 1994. Certiorari Denied February 24, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ga. LEXIS 493.


PRIOR HISTORY: Theft by taking, etc. Habersham Superior Court. Before Judge Struble.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in Case No. A94A1910; judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part in Case No. A94A1911.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the orders of the Habersham Superior Court (Georgia), which dismissed charges of felony theft and forgery on the basis of double jeopardy, and dismissed other charges on the basis of the statute of limitations. Defendant, a former mayor, had completed probation on a sentence received under a plea agreement that waived any procedural defenses and allowed the state to recharge him if he ran for public office again.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been charged with crimes arising from his office and agreed that in return for first offender treatment, he would never run for office again. The state recharged him when he completed his probation and ran for office. On appeal, the court held that the restriction was unenforceable after the expiration of defendant's probation, so that it was only relevant as a triggering event. The court held that the trial court properly dismissed the identical offenses as barred by double jeopardy because defendant had already been tried, convicted, and served his sentence, and any general waiver in the plea agreement was ineffective as to double jeopardy. On the other charges, the court held that the statutes of limitation were not jurisdictional, so the passage of time did not automatically bar the charges. The court held that a statute of limitations could be waived by defendant and applied the same test used for waiver of a jury trial: whether the waiver was made both intelligently and knowingly. The court found that the state had met its burden because both defense counsel and defendant had executed the plea agreement that waived the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court insofar as it held that prosecution of the identical offenses was barred by double jeopardy. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court insofar as it held that the prosecution of some offenses was barred by the statute of limitations.

 

1538 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Gilstrap v. State


A94A2469.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


215 Ga. App. 180; 450 S.E.2d 436; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 1159; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3629



October 31, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 10, 1994. Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Child molestation. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Story.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for three counts of child molestation by the Hall Superior Court (Georgia).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the trial court's refusal to allow his expert to testify regarding results of tests administered to defendant and render an opinion as to whether defendant's responses fit the profile of a pedophile. The court held the trial court's refusal was correct because the jury could have determined the credibility and truthfulness of all the witnesses. Defendant challenged certain rulings made by the trial court. Defendant argued that testimony regarding an incident with the victim's grandfather would have shown that the child had knowledge that sex acts could occur between adults and children. The court held that the evidence could not be considered exculpatory and that the trial court had not abused its discretion in refusing to grant a continuance. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in refusing to declare the rape shield statute unconstitutional. The court concluded that any challenge to the rape shield evidence was rendered moot by defendant's acquittal on the charge of rape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1539 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Hollis v. State


A94A1188


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


215 Ga. App. 35; 450 S.E.2d 247; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 1139; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3546



October 24, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Hollis v. Smith, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 11221 (11th Cir. Ga., June 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Child molestation, etc. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Castellani.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) for child molestation, aggravated child molestation, sodomy, contributing to the unruliness of a minor, and exhibiting harmful materials to minors. He also appealed the trial court's denial of his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant relied on an insanity defense at trial. The trial court denied his motion to amend the verdict to reflect the evidence of guilty but mentally ill. It did not err because altering the verdict would change the jury's verdict. Defendant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel when he failed to show that evidence would have been excluded at trial on any proper ground but for the failure of counsel to file a timely motion to suppress. The trial court properly admitted documentary evidence that showed defendant's state of mind and his lustful disposition toward children generally. Defendant failed to show that the trial court's ruling that the witness could only testify to any change she had seen in defendant's character during the period at issue infringed upon his ability to defend against any specific allegation made by the State. According to Ga. Code Ann. § 16-12-102(1) it was immaterial whether a defense expert considered the materials to be harmful to minors. The trial court improperly made reference to the appellate court but they did not lessen the sense of the jury's responsibility. Defendant failed to object to the comments. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1540 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Westmoreland v. State


A94A2010


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


215 Ga. App. 21; 449 S.E.2d 640; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 1147; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3535



October 21, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Drug violation. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Ison.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia) for sale of cocaine and his sentence of life imprisonment pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-31(b), (d).


OVERVIEW: After an undercover agent bought cocaine, he gave a description of the seller that matched defendant and later identified defendant from a photograph. Defendant's first trial on the charge of selling cocaine ended in a mistrial. At his second trial on the same charges, the trial court entered judgment convicting him. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) evidence of defendant's two prior selling cocaine offenses was admissible similar transaction evidence because the State submitted proper purposes for admitting the evidence, proving identity and modus operandi, and the trial court specifically admitted the evidence on the issue of identity; (2) the trial court did not fail to limit the purpose for which evidence of similar transactions could have been used by the jury; (3) the court was not able to consider defendant's challenge to Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30 as constituting cruel and unusual punishment because he raised the challenge for the first time on appeal, and the state supreme court had declared that the statute was not unconstitutional; and (4) the evidence was sufficient to persuade a rational trier of fact of defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for sale of cocaine and his life sentence.

Smith v. State


A94A1599


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


214 Ga. App. 631; 448 S.E.2d 906; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 992; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 2969



August 26, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 13, 1994. Certiorari Applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Kidnapping, etc. Wayne Superior Court. Before Judge Killian, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Wayne Superior Court, which convicted one defendant of kidnapping, possession of a firearm during the commission of a crime, and aggravated sodomy. The other defendant was convicted of rape, kidnapping, robbery, and possession of a firearm during the commission of a crime.


OVERVIEW: Three men were charged with kidnapping, sexual assaults, robbery, and possession of a firearm during the commission of a crime. One of the defendants, who died before trial, forced his way into the victim's car and drove her to a wooded area. Defendants followed in a truck. Both defendants admitted the deceased threw the victim on the hood of her car and raped her. Defendants also admitted they had been drinking, and one admitted kissing the victim and fondling her breasts and genitals. The other defendant admitted getting in the truck and trying to calm the victim; he admitted fondling her breasts and genitals and turning her on her knees, and he admitted that his penis pressed against her rectum. Both were convicted as charged. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgments of the trial court. The court had no jurisdiction over claims that the statutes were unconstitutional. The charges were brought in the correct county because the venue was determined from the second kidnapping that occurred in the wooded area. Defendants abandoned a number of enumerations for failure to give any argument or cite any legal authority concerning them pursuant to Ga. Ct. App. R. 15(c)(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Evans v. State

214 Ga. App. 844; 449 S.E.2d 302; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 1076; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 2913

PRIOR HISTORY: Forfeiture. Cherokee Superior Court. Before Judge Roach.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from the decision rendered by the Cherokee Superior Court (Georgia), which ordered the forfeiture of their property when it was determined that the property was used to grow marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendants appealed the forfeiture judgment rendered against them and in favor of the state. After a bench trial, the superior court determined that defendants' property was used to facilitate a violation of the Georgia Controlled Substances Act in the manufacture and growing of marijuana. 1543 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Mitchell v. State


A94A0506


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


214 Ga. App. 69; 447 S.E.2d 140; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 771; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 2666



July 15, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Armed robbery. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Long.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed without prejudice and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) convicting him of armed robbery. The appeal presented the question of how the court should have handled defendant's appeal when defendant's attorney had failed to file a brief and enumerations of error despite having been ordered to do so.


OVERVIEW: A majority of the court did not think that the appeal should have simply been dismissed without requiring the trial court to look into whether defendant should have been given another opportunity to appeal. The court struck the appeal from the docket of the court without prejudice to defendant's right to file a direct appeal from his conviction and ordered the trial court to conduct a hearing at which defendant's counsel would have been required to show cause why he should not have been held in contempt of court for failure to prosecute defendant's appeal. The court ordered that the trial court report its findings to the court with regard to defense counsel's failure to prosecute the appeal and that the trial court inquire into defendant's need for appellate counsel and ordered the trial court to take such action as appropriate. The trial court had the burden of looking into the situation even if defendant did not act, to determine why defendant's counsel did not perform and whether defendant needed new counsel.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal without prejudice and remanded the case to the trial court with direction.

In the Interest of T.A.W.


A94A0789


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


214 Ga. App. 1; 447 S.E.2d 136; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 804; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 2663



July 14, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Delinquency. Douglas Juvenile Court. Before Judge Messinger.



DISPOSITION: Case transferred to the Supreme Court of Georgia.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of an order from the Douglas Juvenile Court (Georgia), which denied his motion for a new trial after he was adjudicated delinquent and in need of treatment and rehabilitation.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was adjudicated delinquent and filed a motion for new trial. The juvenile court denied the motion, determining that it lacked the authority to consider the motion's merits under the case law, although it noted that a state constitutional provision gave juvenile courts the authority to grant new trials. On appeal, the court held that it had no jurisdiction to construe Ga. Const. art. VI, § I, para. IV, to determine whether the provision authorized any court of record to grant a new trial. The court held that, under Ga. Const. art. VI, § VI, para. II(1), the exclusive jurisdiction to construe the state constitution rested with the state supreme court. The court ordered the case to be transferred to the supreme court.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the case to the Georgia supreme court for construction of the state constitution.

Taeger Enters. v. Herdlein Techs.


A94A0500, A94A0501


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


213 Ga. App. 740; 445 S.E.2d 848; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 726



July 1, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on contract, etc. Columbia Superior Court. Before Judge Pickett.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Florida corporation commenced suit against defendants, a corporate trade name and president of the corporation, in contract and tort for unpaid labor and services provided. The Columbia Superior Court (Georgia) dismissed the complaint against defendants for lack of personal jurisdiction, and plaintiff sought review.


OVERVIEW: After it was left unpaid for labor and services provided, plaintiff Florida corporation commenced suit in contract and tort against defendants, a corporate trade name and president of the corporation, in Georgia. Defendants moved to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction, which the trial court granted. Plaintiff sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the affidavits made out a prima facie case that the Georgia court lacked personal jurisdiction under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-12 because (1) the torts were committed without the territorial limits of Georgia; (2) and the fact that the corporation and the president of the trade name shared an office in Georgia was not sufficient to confer jurisdiction over the corporation because there was no evidence that the corporation derived revenue in Georgia; (3) the two visits to the site were too attenuated to confer jurisdiction; and (4) there was no evidence that either the corporation or the president of the corporation transacted business in Georgia under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-10-91(1), or solicited business under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-10-91(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal plaintiff Florida corporation's complaint against defendants, a corporate trade name and president of the corporation, based in contract and tort for unpaid labor services provided on grounds of lack personal jurisdiction.

 

1546 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



GM Corp. v. Moseley


A94A0826, A94A0827


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


213 Ga. App. 875; 447 S.E.2d 302; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 797; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 1994; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,996



June 13, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsiderations Denied July 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Thompson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in Case No. A94A0826; judgment dismissed as moot in part, affirmed in part in Case No. A94A0827.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff heirs filed a wrongful death action against defendant auto manufacturer. The jury found in favor of the heirs and awarded actual and punitive damages. The Fulton State Court (Georgia) entered a judgment on the verdict. Both parties filed motions for new trial, which were denied. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was killed when another vehicle struck his truck, causing the gas tank to explode. At trial, the manufacturer's motion in limine regarding other gas tank explosions was granted, but the heirs' counsel repeatedly refereed to other accidents, even though no evidence of the other accidents was introduced. The court held that the repeated violations of the motion in limine was reversible error. The court held that the manufacturer did not waive error by not objecting every time at trial because error was preserved by the granting of the motion in limine. The court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to exclude testimony of a former employee of the manufacturer because he did not testify regarding privileged matters. The court held that it was error to permit the introduction of a deposition from a prior case because the cases were unrelated. The court held that evidence of subsequent remedial measures would be admissible if it tended to prove some fact at issue. The court held there was evidence to support the punitive damages and that they were not unreasonable. The court held that the jury instructions on punitive damages were erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

1547 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Harper v. State


A94A0848


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


213 Ga. App. 611; 445 S.E.2d 300; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 672; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 2090



June 1, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 23, 1994. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied September 29, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ga. LEXIS 1028.
Reconsideration denied by, 06/23/1994
Writ of certiorari denied Harper v. State, 1994 Ga. LEXIS 1028 (Ga., Sept. 29, 1994)
Subsequent appeal at Harper v. State, 2004 Ga. App. LEXIS 1430 (Ga. Ct. App., Nov. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Drug violation. Floyd Superior Court. Before Judge Matthews.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Floyd Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted and sentenced him for selling cocaine, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(b), and selling cocaine within 1000 feet of a public housing project, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-32.5(b).


OVERVIEW: Following a single transaction, defendant was convicted and sentenced for selling cocaine and selling cocaine within 1000 feet of a public housing project. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in not declaring Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-32.5 unconstitutional because the statute was violative of due process and equal protection rights where it treated drug sales in the vicinity of public housing projects differently than sales in other residential areas. The court rejected the argument because it was presented for the first time in his motion for a new trial; therefore, the court held that it was without jurisdiction. Defendant argued that it was error to convict him of violating both Ga. Code Ann. §§ 16-13-30 and § 16-13-32.5.2 because there was no merger of the crimes. The court disagreed concluding that the legislature intended to increase the punishment for selling drugs near public housing projects and recreational facilities. The court concluded that the added element of specific location properly increased the total punishment, using the vehicle of an additional crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for selling cocaine and selling cocaine within 1000 feet of a public housing project.

 

1548 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Dorsey v. State


A93A1933


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


212 Ga. App. 830; 442 S.E.2d 922; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 410; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 1476



April 5, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Carrying a concealed weapon. Clarke State Court. Before Judge Lawrence.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Clarke State Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of carrying a dangerous weapon in a concealed manner, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-126 (a) and sentenced defendant to 12 months on probation.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose when the police searched defendant and found a scalpel in defendant's wallet in defendant's pocket. Defendant argued on appeal that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-126 (a), applicable to the offense of carrying a concealed weapon, was void for vagueness as applied to the facts of the case because the "scalpel" was not a knife designed for the purpose of offense and defense. He asserted that the language of the statute referring to any other dangerous or deadly weapon or instrument of like character had to be construed as being limited by the words: "designed for the purpose of offense and defense." The court held on appeal that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of the case. Reading the statute as a whole, the phrase "designed for the purpose of offense and defense" did not limit the phrase "any other dangerous or deadly weapon or instrument of like character," which was a "catch all." The court concluded that the fact that a scalpel was not designed for purposes of offense and defense did not mean that it could not be concealed as a dangerous or deadly weapon or instrument under certain circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for carrying a concealed weapon.

 

1549 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Gibby v. State


A94A0297.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


213 Ga. App. 20; 443 S.E.2d 852; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 473; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 1474



April 1, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 18, 1994. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied July 7, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ga. LEXIS 848.


PRIOR HISTORY: Child molestation, etc. Spalding Superior Court. Before Judge Miller.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Spalding Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of child molestation, statutory rape, rape, incest, criminal attempt to commit aggravated sodomy, and aggravated child molestation and denied his motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of multiple sex crimes. The court affirmed the convictions and held that the evidence was sufficient to enable rational jurors to find defendant guilty on all counts beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that (1) the Child Hearsay Statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 24-3-16, did not violate the Sixth Amendment; (2) testimony about what the mother said to the victim was not hearsay because it was not offered to show the truth of matters asserted; (3) defendant's direction about what he wanted the girls to do was an integral part of his offenses and was admissible as part of the res gestae; (4) because the victims were available, the trial court did not err in failing to determine the victims' competency prior to allowing the hearsay testimony; (5) defendant failed to show that any of the withheld information was material and exculpatory, and his general assertion that something in the volumes of material would have cast doubt on the reliability of the victims' statements was not enough; (7) the prosecutor's remark that in child molestation cases the only witnesses are the victims was not improper; and (8) the jury was properly instructed on good character evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant.

 

1550 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Logan v. State


A93A1800.


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


212 Ga. App. 734; 442 S.E.2d 883; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 398; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 1487



March 18, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 1, 1994. Certiorari Applied for. Petition for Certiorari Denied July 1, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ga. LEXIS 843.


PRIOR HISTORY: Rape, etc. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Girardeau.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Hall Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of rape, aggravated sodomy, kidnapping with bodily injury, aggravated assault, and simple battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape, aggravated sodomy, kidnapping with bodily injury, aggravated assault, and simple battery. The trial court denied his motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and vacated in part. The court vacated defendant's rape conviction because it was the "rape" that was the basis for the "bodily injury" portion of the kidnapping with bodily injury offense. The court determined that these two offenses merged. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment. The court ruled that defendant's proposed testimony concerning alleged statements made by the victim to defendant concerning her past prostitution, relationships with black men, and fear of getting pregnant were properly excluded under the Rape Shield Statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 24-2-3, which superseded any statement that would have been otherwise admissible as res gestae. Defendant's testimony was not admissible under the exception to the Rape Shield Statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 24-2-3(c), because the proposed testimony did not substantially support the conclusion that defendant reasonably believed the victim consented or that justice mandated the admission of such testimony.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's rape conviction, holding that it merged into the kidnapping with bodily injury conviction, but otherwise affirmed the remainder of the judgment.

 

1551 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Klein v. Williams


A93A2067


COURT OF APPEALS OF GEORGIA


212 Ga. App. 39; 441 S.E.2d 270; 1994 Ga. App. LEXIS 135; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 677; 1994-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P70,571



February 11, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Non-competition covenant. Pickens Superior Court. Before Judge Milam.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from an order of the Pickens Superior Court (Georgia), which issued permanent injunction prohibiting appellant from competing with appellee in the local liquor store industry after a jury found that a non-competition covenant was part of the purchase agreement when appellee bought a liquor store from appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellee filed a complaint against appellant seeking an injunction to prohibit appellant from breaching an agreement not to compete that was allegedly part of sale of appellant's liquor store to appellee. After a special jury found that the agreement existed, the trial court issued an order permanently enjoining appellant from entering into the local liquor store business, so long as appellee owned and operated the liquor store appellee purchased from appellant. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's issuance of the injunction, and held that clear and convincing evidence showed that the competition restriction was the least burdensome restriction necessary to protect appellee's interest because appellee's liquor store was the only such store in a small community. The area protected and activity prohibited were not overbroad.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the permanent injunction barring appellant from competing with appellee and held that the restriction was reasonable and not overbroad because it only restricted appellant entering the local liquor store industry so long as appellee owned and operated the liquor store purchased from appellant.

 

1552 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Scarber v. State


No. A93A1585


Court of Appeals of Georgia


211 Ga. App. 260; 439 S.E.2d 83; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 1481; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 4568



December 3, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Theft by conversion. Bartow Superior Court. Before Judge Howell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted of felony theft by conversion and convicted of misdemeanor theft by conversion under Ga. Code Ann. 16-8-4 in the Bartow Superior Court (Georgia). Defendant's motion for new trial was denied and he appealed, contending that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The alleged victim asserted that defendant agreed to sell several pieces of antique furniture for her and that she was to receive a sum from the sale. After defendant took the furniture to his shop, the victim did not hear from him for some unspecified time. According to the victim, defendant assured her that he would pay her the money, but when she visited his shop he was never there. The victim also testified that she spoke with defendant's employees, but a hearsay objection as to what they told her was sustained. No other witnesses testified for the prosecution. The court reversed defendant's fraudulent conversion conviction on the ground that the evidence was insufficient. Because the victim's testimony did not establish fraudulent intent as required by § 16-8-4, the conviction ran afoul of the constitutional prohibition against imprisonment for debt. The prosecution failed to establish what happened to the furniture and that defendant knowingly and with fraudulent intent appropriated it for his own use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment convicting defendant of misdemeanor theft by conversion.

 

1553 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Glover v. Colbert


No. A93A1640


Court of Appeals of Georgia


210 Ga. App. 666; 437 S.E.2d 363; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 1274



October 27, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Bonner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant victim sought discretionary review of the judgment of the State Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which entered a judgment for damages against appellee tortfeasor after it deducted an amount pursuant to former Ga. Code Ann. § 33-34-9(b) (repealed) as a result of the victim's receipt of medical-expense personal injury protection (PIP) benefits under the Motor Vehicle Reparations Act (Act), § 33-34-1 et seq. (repealed).


OVERVIEW: The victim filed suit against the tortfeasor for damages sustained in a vehicular collision. At trial, a jury returned a verdict in favor of the victim for damages. The trial court entered a judgment after deducting an amount pursuant to former § 33-34-9(b) as a result of the victim's receipt of medical-expense PIP benefits under the Act. The court affirmed and held that the subsequent repeal of the Act did not apply because the tortfeasor had a statutory right that a plaintiff could not recover damages against a tortfeasor for which minimum, mandatory no-fault compensation was available, and which became fixed at the time of the collision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of the reduced award to the victim.

 

1554 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Ballenger v. State


No. A93A1575


Court of Appeals of Georgia


210 Ga. App. 627; 436 S.E.2d 793; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 1295; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 3852



October 21, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Obstruction of officer. Cherokee Superior Court. Before Judge Mills.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision from the Cherokee Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of interference with government property, obstruction of an officer, habitual violator, driving under the influence of alcohol, and operating a vehicle with a foreign license. Defendant objected to a special condition imposed upon the probated portion of his sentence requiring him to wear a fluorescent pink plastic bracelet stating "DUI convict."


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to charges of interference with government property, obstruction of an officer, habitual violator, driving under the influence of alcohol and operating a vehicle with a foreign license. The trial court imposed a five-year sentence upon defendant, including a special condition on the probated portion of the sentence requiring him to wear a pink bracelet imprinted with the words "DUI convict." Defendant contended that the trial court lacked authority to impose the special condition. In affirming on appeal, the court held that: (1) because the trial court had broad discretion to determine the terms and conditions of probation, its requirement that defendant wear the prescribed pink bracelet was permissible even though not expressly authorized by statute; (2) the requirement that defendant wear the pink bracelet did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment where it might have a rehabilitative effect and would forewarn people who might otherwise ride with him; and (3) where the conditions of probation would lapse upon the expiration of the probationary period, the special condition was not for an indeterminate period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which imposed as a special condition upon the probated period of defendant's sentence that he wear a fluorescent pink plastic bracelet stating "DUI convict."

 

1555 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Zechmann v. Thigpen


No. A93A0886


Court of Appeals of Georgia


210 Ga. App. 726; 437 S.E.2d 475; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 1335; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 3741



October 14, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 3, 1993. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied January 21, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ga. LEXIS 159.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice. Ware Superior Court. Before Judge Newton.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant optometrist appealed the decision from the Ware Superior Court (Georgia), which denied the optometrist's motion for summary judgment in the professional malpractice suit brought by plaintiffs, parents and injured child, for an alleged misdiagnosis of an eye abnormality. The optometrist alleged that the suit was untimely pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-73(c)(2).


OVERVIEW: The optometrist treated the injured child for amblyopia. The optometrist did not inform the parents and injured child that she had an optic nerve disease even though the optometrist wrote that fact on the injured child's chart. Approximately four years after the last treatment, it was discovered that the injured child suffered from Coats' disease. The evidence was that the child had the disease when she was treated. The appellate court reversed. Section 9-3-73(c)(2) applied to the optometrist. The two-year medical malpractice limitations period, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-30-71, applied to more than just the practice of medicine. However, when an injury occurred subsequent to treatment, the limitations period commenced on the date the injury was discovered, which was four years after the treatment. Thus, the suit would have been timely if not for Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-73(c)(2). The time for repose was not computed from the time the injury arose but rather from the time of the negligent act. Under § 9-3-73(c)(2), the injured child's claim was barred since she had essentially five years to file suit from the misdiagnosis. There was no evidence of fraud to toll the limitations period.


OUTCOME: The denial of summary judgment to the optometrist was reversed, and he was entitled to judgment as a matter of law. Under the Georgia repose statute for minors, the suit was untimely. The statute applied to optometrists. There was no evidence of fraud, which would have tolled the statute.

 

1556 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Bell v. City of Albany


Nos. A93A1638, A93A1639


Court of Appeals of Georgia


210 Ga. App. 371; 436 S.E.2d 87; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 1180; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 3470



September 23, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. Dougherty Superior Court. Before Judge Gray.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. A93A1638, and reversed in Case No. A93A1639.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestee appealed the judgment of the Dougherty Superior Court (Georgia), which granted defendant city's motion for summary judgment on the arrestee's state and federal claims surrounding the arrestee's arrest. Defendant, a police officer, cross-appealed the denial of his motion for summary judgment in the arrestee's action against the officer for actions taken in the officer's official capacity during the arrest.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee alleged that the trial court erred in concluding that there was no evidence of a city policy or custom that caused the arrestee's injury. The officer contended that he was entitled to qualified immunity on the arrestee's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims. The court held that there was no evidence of any official city policy or custom of using excessive force, nor was there any evidence that the city endorsed a policy or custom of handling intoxicated arrestees in a manner that resulted in injury. Furthermore, the court held that there was no evidence of other incidences suggesting any widespread informal policy or practice constituting a custom or usage with the force of law. The court also held that there was insufficient evidence to create any factual issue in support of any claim of inadequate training. The court held that the force the officer used was not such that would have been clear to a reasonable police officer that using such force would violate the arrestee's Fourth Amendment rights not to be subjected to an unreasonable use of force during his arrest. Therefore, the court held that the officer used was entitled to the protection of qualified immunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the city and reversed the trial court's denial of the officer's summary judgment motion.

 

1557 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Stevens v. State


No. A93A1657


Court of Appeals of Georgia


210 Ga. App. 355; 436 S.E.2d 82; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 1188; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 3499



September 22, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Drug violation, etc. Glynn Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Glynn Superior Court (Georgia) convicted defendant of the sale of cocaine. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several claims. The court rejected each claim and affirmed the conviction. The court found that defendant waved and whistled at an unmarked police car and asked the driver what he wanted. When the driver told defendant that he wanted crack cocaine, defendant replied that he had to get his man. Defendant and his co-defendant then approached the car, and defendant stood to the side as his co-defendant sold the drug. The court held that this evidence was sufficient to show that defendant was a party to the sale of cocaine. The court also rejected defendant's claim that the trial court erred in denying his motion for a severance. The court found that defendant failed to show prejudice from this ruling and that a common trial was warranted because the criminal conduct involved the same place of occurrence, the same undercover agents, and the same transaction. In addition, the court rejected defendant's claim that the sentencing provision of Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7 was unconstitutional. The court held that defendant did not have standing to contest the validity of § 17-10-7 until he had a right of parole, and the statute was asserted against him as a bar.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1558 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Wayne County v. Herrin


Nos. A93A1178, A93A1179


Court of Appeals of Georgia


210 Ga. App. 747; 437 S.E.2d 793; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 1336; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 3323



September 10, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 3, 1993. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied January 28, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ga. LEXIS 265. Petition for Certiorari Denied January 28, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Ga. LEXIS 238.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action on employment. Wayne Superior Court. Before Judge Taylor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with direction in Case No. A93A1178. Judgment affirmed in Case No. A93A1179.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff board and defendant sheriff both appealed from the judgment of the Wayne Superior Court (Georgia), which held that the board had properly adopted a county personnel system pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 36-1-21, but that the sheriff could refuse to reappoint employees in the sheriff's office pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 15-16-23.


OVERVIEW: The board had recently enacted a county personnel system and one of the last acts of the outgoing officeholder was to request that the employees of the sheriff's office be covered by the system. The first thing the sheriff did upon taking office was to notify the employees that he was not reappointing them to their positions and to appoint new deputies. The sheriff argued that the personnel system had not been validly adopted because § 36-1-21 required action by ordinance or resolution and the board had acted by motion to adopt the system. The court held that the term resolution included action by motion. The court held that the enactment of § 36-1-21 did not repeal § 15-16-23 by implication and reconciled the two by holding that once positions in a sheriff's office had been made subject to the personnel system, the sheriff's authority to appoint deputies pursuant to § 15-16-23 was limited to vacancies created by the removal of employees in the manner provided under the personnel system or vacancies created when employees resigned or retired. Thus, the sheriff had no authority to discharge or fail to reappoint the employees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment holding that the county personnel system was properly adopted but reversed its holding that the sheriff could discharge or refuse to reappoint employees in the sheriff's office covered by the system.

Hopkins v. State


No. A93A0836


Court of Appeals of Georgia


209 Ga. App. 376; 434 S.E.2d 74; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 893; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 2586



June 24, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 9, 1993. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied September 20, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ga. LEXIS 897.


PRIOR HISTORY: Cruelty to children, etc. Douglas Superior Court. Before Judge Emerson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Douglas Superior Court (Georgia), which ruled in favor of the State and convicted defendant of cruelty to children.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of cruelty to children he appealed. On appeal the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to find defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court stated that the jury, as the trier of fact, was properly left to determine what was cruel or excessive physical or mental pain. The court found that defendant's due process rights were not violated when he was not permitted to cross-examine a witness for the State. The court noted that the witness's testimony pertained to the nature of her relationship with defendant and was completely irrelevant to the issue of whether defendant was guilty of cruelty to children. The court held that the trial court did not commit reversible error by allowing the State to inject defendant's character into evidence. The court stated that the testimony was elicited as background evidence regarding the child's primary caregivers, and that any error in allowing the testimony was harmless. The court noted that because defendant did not argue the constitutionality of the statutory definition of reasonable punishment in the trial court the issue was not preserved on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Bieling v. Battle


No. A93A0693


Court of Appeals of Georgia


209 Ga. App. 874; 434 S.E.2d 719; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 1021; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 2567



June 24, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 30, 1993. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied October 29, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ga. LEXIS 1056.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Thompson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, physician and medical group, sought review of the judgment of the Fulton State Court (Georgia), which denied defendants' motion for summary judgment as to plaintiff former patient's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The former patient was diagnosed with AIDS allegedly due to an unnecessary blood transfusion during her hysterectomy. The former patient brought a medical malpractice action against defendants. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment, which the trial court denied. The court granted interlocutory review, and reversed the denial of summary judgment. The court held that the statute of repose, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-71(b), governed the action. The court found that because the former patient brought her action more than five years after the date of the alleged negligent act, the statute of ultimate repose barred it. Therefore, the court held that defendants were entitled to summary judgment as a matter of law. The court also held that defendants were entitled to summary judgment because it was undisputed that the former patient's contraction of AIDS was not the natural or foreseeable proximate result of a blood transfusion known within the medical community at the time.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and granted summary judgment for defendants.

 

1561 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Nowak v. High


No. A93A0129


Court of Appeals of Georgia


209 Ga. App. 536; 433 S.E.2d 602; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 931; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 2217



June 8, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 16, 1993. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied October 12, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ga. LEXIS 956.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Etheridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) granting the motion of appellee physician to dismiss her medical malpractice action on the grounds that the affidavit of a registered nurse was, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1, insufficient evidence regarding the medical standard of care applicable to administering the drug Phenergan.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed a complaint alleging that the physician negligently injected the drug into the patient's lower hip area, which caused her injuries because the drug should have been injected into the upper hip area. She contested the judgment of dismissal rendered by the trial court, which the court reversed. The court held that the affidavit supporting the patient's complaint constituted sufficient proof to satisfy § 9-11-9.1 that the methods of treatment for injecting the drug, by nurses and doctors, were the same. The court found sufficient proof of the nurse's overlapping expertise to establish that she was competent to provide the affidavit stating the standards of care regarding the giving of Phenergan injections in both the nursing profession and in the medical profession. The court reached that conclusion based on the statutory definition of the practice of nursing encompassing the giving of injections, the averments in the affidavit, and the patient's allegations of negligence. The court accepted the affidavit's conclusion that the physician's performance fell beneath the medical profession's standard of care by injecting the drug in the wrong place on the patient's leg.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment challenged by the patient, which incorrectly granted the physician's motion for dismissal of this medical malpractice lawsuit on the basis that the registered nurse's affidavit was, under the statute, sufficient evidence concerning the medical standard of care governing the drug's application..

 

1562 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Moore v. Mellars


No. A92A2179


Court of Appeals of Georgia


208 Ga. App. 69; 430 S.E.2d 179; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 415; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 1439



March 19, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. Cobb State Court. Before Judge Nix.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injury victim sought review of the decision from the Cobb State Court (Georgia), which rendered a jury verdict in favor of appellee driver in the victim's action for damages arising out of an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: The victim was injured when she was involved in an automobile accident with the driver. She filed an action to recover for her damages and the jury returned a verdict in favor of the driver. The victim challenged the verdict and maintained that it was error to allow the issue of collateral source funds into evidence. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the victim had raised the issue on direct examination and therefore limited cross-examination on the issue was proper. Even though the collateral source statute, authorizing the admission of evidence of collateral source payments, had been declared unconstitutional the rules in effect prior to the enactment of the statute still governed. Because the victim broached the issue of insurance payment on direct examination when she averred that she stopped going to a physician because insurance had stopped paying, defense counsel was entitled to cross-examine her on the point.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the verdict in favor of the driver in the victim's personal injury action.

McDonald v. Simmons


No. A92A2307


Court of Appeals of Georgia


207 Ga. App. 692; 428 S.E.2d 690; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 274; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 1063



March 9, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. Jeff Davis Superior Court. Before Judge Tuten.

1564 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Sumlin v. State


No. A92A2415


Court of Appeals of Georgia


207 Ga. App. 408; 427 S.E.2d 868; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 182; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 718



February 19, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Armed robbery. Bartow Superior Court. Before Judge Pope.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Bartow Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contested his conviction and argued that the armed robbery statute was unconstitutional and that the trial court erred in refusing to give a certain jury instruction. The court determined that although a constitutional issue was raised by the appeal, the court, and not the supreme court, had jurisdiction over the appeal because the constitutional issue had not been raised in the trial court and thus was not open for review. The court also found that the trial court did not err in failing to issue defendant's requested instruction to the effect that victim's testimony would be sufficient to authorize a finding of robbery by intimidation because such a charge was argumentative and incomplete. Robbery by intimidation was a lesser included offense in the offense of armed robbery. The victim's testimony authorized a finding of either armed robbery or robbery by intimidation. The trial court properly instructed the jury on both armed robbery and robbery by intimidation. It was not incumbent upon the trial court to specifically point out particular evidence in behalf of defendant that the jury should specially consider.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction by the trial court.

 

1565 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Barrett v. State


No. A92A2222


Court of Appeals of Georgia


207 Ga. App. 370; 427 S.E.2d 845; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 186; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 726



February 16, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Theft by conversion. Jackson State Court. Before Judge Motes.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Jackson State Court (Georgia), which, after a bench trial, convicted him of theft by conversion pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 16-8-4.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the state presented evidence that defendant failed to return rented equipment from a video rental store on a Friday. Defendant testified that he rented the equipment to use with a neighbor and that the neighbor said he would return the same. Defendant further testified that he has not seen the neighbor since and was not aware the equipment had not been returned until he was served with the criminal warrant. The whereabouts of the equipment was not established. In reversing defendant's conviction for theft by conversion, the court held that the evidence was insufficient to establish that defendant knowingly converted the equipment to his own use with fraudulent intent, an essential element of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-8-4. In so ruling, the court stated that fraudulent intent could not be inferred from defendant's failure to return the equipment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of theft by conversion.

 

1566 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Macon Tel. Publ'g Co. v. Tatum


Nos. A92A1702, A92A1703


Court of Appeals of Georgia


208 Ga. App. 111; 430 S.E.2d 18; 1993 Ga. App. LEXIS 409; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 620; 21 Media L. Rep. 1116



February 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 24, 1993. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Granted May 10, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ga. LEXIS 606.


PRIOR HISTORY: Invasion of privacy. Bibb State Court. Before Judge Phillips.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant daily newspaper sought review of a jury verdict by the Bibb State Court (Georgia), of invasion of privacy. The jury found against the newspaper on the two counts, one for each article published, arising out of a cause of action filed by appellee sexual assault victim, pursuant to the Georgia Rape Shield Statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-23, which made illegal the publication of the name of a sexual assault victim.


OVERVIEW: The police testified at trial that they made it clear to the newspaper's reporters that they were treating the incident as a sexual assault. The police further testified that they were reluctant to give out the name of the sexual assault victim and finally did so only with the understanding that her name would not be published without her permission and that publication otherwise would violate the state's Rape Shield Statute. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment, concluding that imposition of liability for invasion of privacy for publishing the name of a sexual assault victim was not precluded by existing case law. The court ruled that while crime was a matter of legitimate public interest, the victim's privacy interest in protecting her identity outweighed any legitimate public interest. The court ruled that since the constitutionality of the Rape Shield Statute was not ruled upon by the trial court, it could be raised on appeal and, in any event, the state supreme court had sole jurisdiction on a question of the constitutionality of a statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against the newspaper on two counts of invasion of privacy of the sexual assault victim.

 

1567 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Jones v. Lamon


No. A92A1315


Court of Appeals of Georgia


206 Ga. App. 842; 426 S.E.2d 657; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1814; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 67



December 4, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 17, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice, etc. Colquitt Superior Court. Before Judge Lilly.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a patient and her husband, appealed an order of the Superior Court, Colquitt County (Georgia), which granted summary judgment to defendants, hospital, physician, and hospital authority, in a suit for medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: A patient was prescribed the anticoagulant drug Coumadin after surgery. Two weeks later, on August 26, 1989, she began to have nausea and other symptoms and was admitted to the hospital. Tests confirmed that she was hemorrhaging, which the patient and her husband later claimed was caused by the physician's and hospital's failure to monitor her properly while she was taking the drug. The patient and her husband filed suit for medical malpractice and loss of consortium. The trial court granted summary judgment for the hospital, physician, and hospital authority. On appeal, the court held that Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-71(a) provided that malpractice actions had to be brought within two years after the date on which an injury arose from a negligent or wrongful act or omission. The patient's cause of action accrued when her symptoms began on Aug. 26, and her initial subjective belief that her symptoms came from some cause unrelated to negligence did not change the running of the statute. The court also held that the statute of limitations applicable to the claim for loss of consortium was four years, as set forth in Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-33, so the husband's cause of action was viable.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed as to the patient's cause of action for medical malpractice, but reversed as to her husband's cause of action for loss of consortium.
