Watkins v. State


No. A92A1280


Court of Appeals of Georgia


206 Ga. App. 575; 426 S.E.2d 26; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1701; 92 Fulton County D. Rep. 2913



November 17, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 3, 1992. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied February 25, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ga. LEXIS 278.


PRIOR HISTORY: Drug violation, etc. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Hull.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(b) and denied his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of violating Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(b) by possessing cocaine with intent to distribute and denied his new trial motion. The court affirmed that judgment on appeal, reasoning that the record did not support defendant's allegation that he deserved a new trial based on his attorney's alleged failure to prepare for his trial. The court also held that the circumstances of defendant's earlier conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute justified the attorney's decision to not object to its introduction as similar transaction evidence. The court further determined that charging the jury with the entirety of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(b) was not a reversible error because the entire indictment was read to the jury, which was instructed that defendant was only on trial only for the offense of possession with intent to distribute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and the denial of his motion for a new trial.

 

1569 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Strozier v. Clark


No. A92A1394


Court of Appeals of Georgia


206 Ga. App. 85; 424 S.E.2d 368; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1429; 92 Fulton County D. Rep. 2547



October 30, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages. Coffee Superior Court. Before Judge Newton.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured person challenged an order of the Coffee Superior Court (Georgia) that denied his Batson motion and rendered a judgment in favor of appellee tortfeasor in the injured person's action to recover for injuries sustained in an automobile collision.


OVERVIEW: Of the 24 prospective jurors, 5 were black. Of these 5, the tortfeasor used peremptory strikes against 4. After voir dire, the injured person made a Batson motion, and the trial court conducted a hearing wherein the tortfeasor's counsel offered explanations for the peremptory strikes against the 4 black prospective jurors. After the hearing, the trial court denied the Batson motion. In reversing, the court found that as to 3 of the 4 black potential jurors, counsel offered a racially neutral reason. As to the fourth, age was offered as a neutral explanation related to the case. However counsel went further and indicated that he was also skeptical of the prospective juror's denial on voir dire that she actually knew the injured person or the witnesses who would testify in the case. The court determined that an assumption that the prospective juror would act along racial lines and engage in misconduct constituted an impermissible assumption ultimately arising solely from the juror's race. Even though counsel gave one racially neutral explanation, the racially motivated explanation vitiated the legitimacy of the entire procedure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that denied the injured person's Batson motion and that rendered a judgment in favor of the tortfeasor in the injured person's action to recover for injuries sustained in an automobile collision.

 

1570 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Klinakis


No. A92A1030


Court of Appeals of Georgia


206 Ga. App. 318; 425 S.E.2d 665; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1669



October 29, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 18, 1992. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied April 8, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ga. LEXIS 330.


PRIOR HISTORY: Fighting words, etc. Clayton State Court. Before Judge Arnold.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision by the Clayton State Court (Georgia), which granted appellee union member's motion to dismiss the state's charge of use of fighting words under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-39 and simple assault under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-20.


OVERVIEW: After a meeting between labor unions, the union member was charged with use of fighting words and simple assault. The union member filed a plea in abatement as to the fighting words charge and demurred to the charge of simple assault. The trial court dismissed the charges. On appeal, the court reversed the dismissal. In stating that fighting words were not constitutionally protected, the court held that the state enacted Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-39 and Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-20 to curtail criminal activity before it escalated into or caused immediate acts of actual violence. The court stated that under the circumstances, the exercise of criminal jurisdiction posed no significant threat of interference with the policies and jurisdiction of the Railway Labor Act. The court held that the violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-39 was based on the utterance of fighting words while the simple assault violation was based on certain physical conduct. Therefore, the trial court erred in dismissing the simple assault charge as moot, and the existence of a labor dispute did not give any party to the controversy an unfettered right to violate an applicable criminal law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court dismissing the charge of use of fighting words and simple assault.

 

1571 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Dye v. State


No. A92A2115


Court of Appeals of Georgia


205 Ga. App. 781; 423 S.E.2d 713; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1383; 92 Fulton County D. Rep. 2428



October 9, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Rape, etc. Camden Superior Court. Before Judge Knox.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in Camden Superior Court (Georgia), defendant was convicted of statutory rape, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-3, and aggravated child molestation. Defendant appealed the judgment with respect to his statutory rape conviction, alleging that: 1) § 16-6-3 was unconstitutional; and 2) there was insufficient evidence to support the conviction.


OVERVIEW: During defendant's trial, the underage victim of the statutory rape testified to the sexual conduct she experienced. On appeal, the court first considered whether defendant's claim that § 16-6-3 was unconstitutional required it to transfer the action to the Supreme Court of Georgia, which was given exclusive jurisdiction by Ga. Const. art. VI, § 6, para. 2(1) to hear challenges to the constitutionality of legislation. Because defendant had neither sought nor obtained a ruling from the trial court on the statute's constitutionality, the court declared that the issue had not been preserved for appellate review. The court rejected defendant's claim that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction; in doing so, it recognized that § 16-6-3 declared that a statutory rape conviction could not be based solely on the unsupported testimony of the female. However, the female's testimony did not need to support every essential element of the crime. Because the child's testimony was corroborated by defendant's testimony, and would lead a reasonable trier of fact to rationally find defendant guilty of statutory rape, the evidence was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of aggravated child molestation and statutory rape.

 

1572 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Harmon v. State


No. A92A1282


Court of Appeals of Georgia


205 Ga. App. 685; 423 S.E.2d 302; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1294; 92 Fulton County D. Rep. 2259



October 2, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Ordinance violation. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Carnes.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from the judgment of Fulton State Court (Georgia), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted him of violating Fulton County, Ga., Ordinances § 33-5-10(b). Section 33-5-10(b) provided that no adult entertainment premises could be licensed to sell alcoholic beverages if it was located within 1,000 feet of the boundaries of any residential zoning district.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that, by its terms, the ordinance related solely to the county's issuance of a liquor license and provided that no such license was to be issued to adult entertainment premises located within certain geographic areas. Under this ordinance, appellant would not be entitled to a liquor license for his adult entertainment premises if he were seeking one from the county. However, appellant had a liquor license that predated § 33-5-10(b) and nothing under the terms of that ordinance prohibited him from featuring nude dancing at his bar and restaurant. The court also noted that Fulton County, Ga., Ordinances § 33-5-11(5) enumerated acts that no holder of a liquor license could allow to occur on the licensed premises. However, the language of that ordinance tracked the former Ga. Code Ann. § 3-3-41, which had been held unconstitutional. The county could not forgo an attempted prosecution of appellant under the possibly unconstitutional § 33-5-11 by urging that § 33-5-10(b) was itself a criminal provision that prohibited appellant, in his capacity as a holder of an existing liquor license, from featuring nude dancing at his bar and restaurant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

1573 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Reeves


Nos. A92A1143, A92A1237


Court of Appeals of Georgia


205 Ga. App. 656; 423 S.E.2d 32; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1280



September 21, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 1, 1992. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied January 14, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ga. LEXIS 76.


PRIOR HISTORY: Jurisdiction. Lincoln Superior Court. Before Judge Davis.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed and cases remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of South Carolina and its department of corrections appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Lincoln County (Georgia), challenging the court's jurisdiction under Georgia's Long-Arm Statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-10-91(3), in a tort action filed by plaintiff administrator and next friend of the decedent and a seriously injured individual, who were both attacked by an escaped South Carolina prison inmate.


OVERVIEW: The administrator of the decedent's estate and next fried filed two actions against the State of South Carolina and its department of corrections in the State of Georgia, alleging that certain negligent acts and omissions of employees of the department had enabled an inmate to escape into Georgia and fatally wound the decedent and seriously injure another individual. The trial court consolidated the cases and denied the state's and the department's motions for summary judgment, finding that the contacts requirement of the Georgia Long-Arm Statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-10-91 et seq., had been satisfied because the state and the department transacted business in Georgia, at a minimum in the form of tourism solicitation and received revenue from taxpayers who lived in Georgia, but worked or owned property in South Carolina. The court reversed and remanded with directions to dismiss the actions for lack of personal jurisdiction. Sufficient contacts did not exist between Georgia and South Carolina within the meaning of § 9-10-91(3) to authorize personal jurisdiction. To say otherwise would have resulted in an unconstitutionally broad construction of Georgia's Long-Arm Statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that denied the State of South Carolina and its department of correction's motions for summary judgment, and remanded the case with directions to enter orders that dismissed the administrator's complaints against the state and the department for lack of personal jurisdiction.

 

1574 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Wright v. Crawford Long Hosp.


No. A92A0964


Court of Appeals of Georgia


205 Ga. App. 653; 423 S.E.2d 12; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1279; 92 Fulton County D. Rep. 1883



September 8, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 1, 1992. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Denied September 8, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ga. LEXIS 952.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Fryer.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a decision from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted judgment for appellees, hospital and physicians, and dismissed the patient's medical malpractice claim for noncompliance with Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1.


OVERVIEW: A patient filed a medical malpractice action against a hospital and several physicians claiming damages for injuries sustained when an introducer wire was left in her body during a catheterization procedure. The court affirmed the superior court's judgment dismissing the patient's suit and concluded that the patient had failed to comply with Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1(a). The surgeon who removed the wire testified that the wire removed was not the kind used to thread a catheterization line, and that she did not recognize the type of wire and was unable to identify a procedure in which such a wire would be used. As such, the surgeon's testimony failed to specify at least one negligent act or omission committed by the hospital or physicians as required under § 9-11-9.1(a). The court concluded that the patient could not amend the action to add a different medical expert's affidavit because she failed to allege in her original complaint that she was unable to obtain an affidavit because of time constraints as required under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1(b). Also, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1(e) did not apply since the doctor's affidavit was dated after the patient's suit was filed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment dismissing the patient's medical malpractice suit against a hospital and several physicians.

 

1575 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Dep't of Human Res. v. Ammons


No. A92A0839


Court of Appeals of Georgia


206 Ga. App. 805; 426 S.E.2d 901; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1790



September 8, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 17, 1992. Certiorari Applied For. Petition for Certiorari Granted April 15, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ga. LEXIS 576.


PRIOR HISTORY: Recovery of benefits. Whitfield Superior Court. Before Judge Temples.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Georgia Department of Human Resources (DHR) sought review of an order of the Whitfield Superior Court (Georgia), which denied its claim, brought pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. §§ 19-11-1 et seq., for recovery of public assistance benefits paid on behalf of a child from appellee, the child's father. The trial court denied the claim because the father's parental rights had been terminated several years previously.


OVERVIEW: The father's parental rights were terminated, with his consent, in an action brought by the child's mother. Subsequently, DHR provided public assistance benefits to the child, and then sought to recover the amount of those benefits from the father. On appeal, the court affirmed because the father's obligation to support the child was extinguished by the termination order, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-80. The parent-child relationship remained intact, but the obligation and right of support, which was otherwise predicated on that relationship, was terminated. The termination order was not void because Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-81(b)(1) specifically authorized a termination of parental rights upon the written consent of a parent. Nor was the order void because the child was not represented by a guardian. The statute in effect at the time that the father's rights were terminated, Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-55, did not specifically require the appointment of a guardian in every case. Moreover, even if the child had not been represented by a guardian, the termination order would not be void and subject to DHR's collateral attack.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied DHR's claim for recovery of public assistance benefits paid on behalf of a child from the child's father, whose parental rights had previously terminated.

 

1576 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Cincinnati Ins. Co. v. Reybitz


Nos. A92A0103, A92A0104


Court of Appeals of Georgia


205 Ga. App. 174; 421 S.E.2d 767; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1046; 92 Fulton County D. Rep. 1440



July 16, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 27, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action on policy. Cobb State Court. Before Judge Adams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bicyclist brought an action against defendants, insureds and insurer, seeking to recover damages, personal injury protection benefits pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 33-34-7(a)(3), statutory penalties, and penalties for bad faith failure to pay insurance proceeds. The Cobb State Court (Georgia) denied the insureds and insurer's motion to bifurcate the claims. The jury found in favor of the bicyclist. The insureds and the insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The bicyclist was injured when one of the insured's struck him with her car while the bicyclist was riding on a public street. The insureds and insurer contended that the trial court erred by denying their motion to bifurcate the trial. Specifically, the insureds contended that the jury's consideration of the claims against the insurer allowed evidence in the trial of the negligence claims that the insureds possessed liability coverage. The appellate court held that the trial court abused its discretion by denying the motion to bifurcate. The court found that there was no express statutory provision in the Georgia Motor Vehicle Accident Reparations Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 33-34-1 et seq., authorizing the joinder of the claims. The admission of evidence of insurance coverage was inherently prejudicial, and prejudice was one of the statutory grounds for severance under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-42(b). Given the prejudicial nature of the evidence, the joinder was not justified on the grounds of judicial economy. Ga. Code Ann. § 51-12-1(b), which allowed evidence of collateral sources, was previously held unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the bicyclist.

 

1577 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Atlanta v. Atl. Realty Co.


Nos. A92A0581, A92A0582


Court of Appeals of Georgia


205 Ga. App. 1; 421 S.E.2d 113; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 1052



July 13, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action on contract. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Jenrette.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in Case No. A92A0581 is affirmed; judgment in Case No. A92A0582 is affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which entered a judgment on the jury verdict in favor of appellee property owner and denied its motion for a directed verdict and a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city challenged the trial court's order, which entered a judgment on the jury verdict in favor of appellee property owner and denied its motion for a directed verdict and a new trial. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in denying appellant's motions for directed verdict, j.n.o.v., and for a new trial because appellee failed to provide appellant with the ante litem notice required under Ga. Code Ann. § 36-33-5. The court affirmed the order. The court found that the uncontroverted evidence appeared in the record that appellee contacted the Assistant City Attorney in charge of the claims division for appellant, regarding the building damage. The assistant city attorney told appellee to send the ante litem notice to him at his office address and appellee complied with the request. Consequently, appellant waived its claim that the subject ante litem notice did not comply with Ga. Code Ann. § 36-33-5 because it was sent to a city claims investigator, rather than the City Attorney or the Mayor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which entered a judgment on the jury verdict in favor of appellee property owner and denied appellant city's motion for a directed verdict and a new trial. The court found that where the assistant city attorney instructed appellee to send the ante litem notice to his office appellant waived its claim that the notice did not comply with the statute.

 

1578 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Sanders v. State


No. A91A1886


Court of Appeals of Georgia


204 Ga. App. 37; 419 S.E.2d 24; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 667; 92 Fulton County D. Rep. 256



April 3, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Armed robbery, etc. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Jenrette.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of armed robbery and aggravated assault. He contended, in part, that the trial court violated his right pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 15-12-133 to question jurors about any inclination or bias respecting the action, counsel or the parties when it prohibited his counsel from questioning prospective jurors about possible bias against defense counsel.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose from an incident in which he robbed a woman and stole her car. While fleeing in the car, he ran into a policeman who was reporting for duty. He was eventually apprehended, after drawing a rifle on the officer. On appeal, the court affirmed. Although defense counsel should have been allowed to ask prospective jurors about potential bias toward criminal defense attorneys, in light of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt, the State met its burden of showing that it was highly probable the limitation on voir dire was harmless error. The victim's testimony that defendant had a gun wrapped in a coat, which he pointed at her while taking her keys and pocketbook was sufficient to infer the presence of a weapon, even when the victim did not actually see the gun. The trial court properly instructed the jury on flight because defendant's case was tried before the Georgia Supreme Court's decision holding that from that point forward no trial court should charge a jury on flight. Considering the totality of the circumstances, any suggestiveness in a photographic lineup did not give rise to a substantial likelihood of mistaken identification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for armed robbery and aggravated assault.

Tootle v. State

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Tattnall Superior Court (Georgia), which found defendant guilty of operating a motor vehicle after having been declared a habitual violator. Defendant was found not guilty of driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol and drugs.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of operating a motor vehicle after having been declared a habitual violator and not guilty of driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol and drugs. The court concluded that the evidence authorized the jury's finding that defendant was guilty, beyond a reasonable doubt, of operating a motor vehicle in the state after having been declared a habitual violator in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-58.

Spires v. Kim


No. A91A1471


Court of Appeals of Georgia


203 Ga. App. 302; 416 S.E.2d 780; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 507; 103-48 Fulton County D. Rep. 14B



February 20, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 11, 1992. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Medical malpractice. Laurens Superior Court. Before Judge Towson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of the judgment of the Laurens Superior Court (Georgia), which granted appellee obstetrician's motion to dismiss their "wrongful birth" and wrongful life" claims based on their child's birth with a congenital defect.


OVERVIEW: The parents alleged that they were deprived of the opportunity to abort the child by the obstetrician's negligent failure to conduct an additional sonogram and failure to disclose that an additional sonogram had been recommended by other healthcare professionals. The court affirmed the dismissal of the parents' claims based on precedent from the Georgia Supreme Court which held that "wrongful life" claims implicitly and "wrongful birth" claims explicitly could not be recognized in Georgia absent a clear mandate for such recognition by the legislature. The court declined to transfer the matter directly to the supreme court based on the parents' contention that the holding was violative of their constitutional right to due process. The parents did not raise an issue of constitutional construction and the supreme court decision was not a state "law" that would give the supreme court jurisdiction over a constitutional challenge to its continued viability. The parents could seek a writ of certiorari for supreme court review of their claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the parents' wrongful birth and wrongful life claims.

 

1581 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Stinson v. State


No. A91A2123


Court of Appeals of Georgia


203 Ga. App. 225; 416 S.E.2d 765; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 475; 103-46 Fulton County D. Rep. 22



February 19, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 6, 1992. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: D.U.I. Putnam State Court. Before Judge Rice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Putnam State Court (Georgia), which convicted him of operating a vehicle while having a blood alcohol concentration of 0.12 grams or more and operating a vehicle with a defective headlight.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions holding that independent testing of the machine could not establish that defendant's results were inaccurate since the original testing conditions, including defendant's physical state, could not have been duplicated. The court held that defendant was not denied the right to introduce evidence the machine may have malfunctioned by the court's refusal to allow him to test the machine. As to the admission of the breath test results, the court held that the admissibility of breathalyzer test results was controlled solely by Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-392, and in this case, the officer who administered the tests was authorized by the State of Georgia to perform chemical analyses utilizing the Intoximeter Breath Analyzer 3000 machine. Finally, the court held that as to the issue of the admissibility of the test results, the test results were not excludable because the examiner failed to wait 20 minutes between defendant's arrest and the first test and then again by not waiting 20 minutes between the first and second test. The court held that the record revealed that at least 45 minutes had elapsed between the traffic stop and the first test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for operating a vehicle while having a blood alcohol concentration of 0.12 grams or more and operating a vehicle with a defective headlight.

 

1582 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Giles v. Locust Grove


No. A91A1751


Court of Appeals of Georgia


203 Ga. App. 164; 416 S.E.2d 758; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 458; 103-45 Fulton County D. Rep. 22



February 18, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 4, 1992. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: D.U.I., etc. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge Craig.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Henry Superior Court (Georgia), which denied defendant's demand for a de novo trial by jury after defendant was found guilty in a municipal court of speeding, driving under the influence, and driving without proof of insurance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried and convicted in a municipal court for speeding, driving under the influence, and driving without proof of insurance. He appealed to the trial court and demanded a de novo trial by jury. The trial court denied his demand and found him guilty as charged. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that (1) the municipal court had jurisdiction over defendant's misdemeanor traffic charges; (2) defendant's right to appeal was governed by Ga. Code Ann. § 40-13-28 and the standard of review for defendant's appeal was not de novo but instead based on a review of the record; (3) the appeal procedures of § 40-13-28 took precedence over a city charter provision that specified that appeals from the municipal court to the trial court would be de novo; (4) even though no transcript or summary of the evidence was contained in the record transmitted to the trial court by the municipal court, defendant failed to request a transcript of the record, and the trial court was required to presume that the evidence supported the convictions; and (5) defendant waived his right to a jury because he proceeded to trial without objecting to being tried without a jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding defendant guilty of speeding, driving under the influence, and driving without proof of insurance.

 

1583 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Pruitt v. State


No. A91A2008


Court of Appeals of Georgia


203 Ga. App. 125; 416 S.E.2d 524; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 386; 103-43 Fulton County D. Rep. 23



February 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 2, 1992. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Motion in limine. Clarke State Court. Before Judge Lawrence.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Clarke State Court (Georgia), which denied his motion in limine to exclude the results of an Intoximeter 3000 test. Defendant had entered a plea of guilty to driving under the influence of alcohol to the extent that it was less safe for him to drive, driving with a blood alcohol concentration in excess of 0.12 grams, and failure to stop at a stop sign.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped after his car failed to stop at a stop sign. After failing a field sobriety test, a portable Alcosensor test was administered and defendant was arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol and running a stop sign. The implied consent warning was read to him and he was transported to the jail. An Intoximeter 3000 test was then performed, and one of the officer's assisted defendant in telephoning the only facility in the county that performed independent chemical analysis. However, defendant did not have sufficient funds for the test. At trial, defendant entered a plea of guilty to driving under the influence of alcohol, driving with a blood alcohol concentration in excess of 0.12 grams, and failure to stop at a stop sign. The trial court denied defendant's motion in limine to exclude the results of an Intoximeter 3000 test. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the officer made a reasonable effort to accommodate defendant's efforts to obtain an independent test. Also, the test results were admissible under Ga. Code Ann. § 392 because defendant was properly advised of his right to an independent test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion in limine to exclude the results of an Intoximeter 3000 test in defendant's trial for driving under the influence of alcohol, driving with a blood alcohol concentration in excess of 0.12 grams, and failure to stop at a stop sign.

 

1584 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



McLelland v. State


No. A91A2168


Court of Appeals of Georgia


203 Ga. App. 93; 416 S.E.2d 340; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 397; 103-43 Fulton County D. Rep. 22



February 14, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 26, 1992. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Child molestation. Grady Superior Court. Before Judge Chason.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Grady Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of child molestation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of child molestation, and the court, having found no error by the trial court, affirmed the conviction. The court held that the trial court properly ruled that the status of the witness as lay or expert would go, not to admissibility of her testimony, but to its credibility pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 24-9-65 and Ga. Code Ann. § 24-9-67. The court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to admit his victim's medical records in evidence because the only statement contained therein that defendant wished to introduce was inadmissible hearsay, thus inclusion of the entire hospital record was unnecessary. The court held that the trial court did not err in giving the jury an Allen charge and did not err in denying a mistrial on the ground that the jury was deadlocked. The court held that there was no evidence of a deadlock and a motion for mistrial based on the length of a jury's deliberation was within the sound discretion of the trial court. The court held that the trial court was bound by the jury's feeling that it was hopelessly deadlocked.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's child molestation conviction.

 

1585 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Armour v. Davidson


No. A91A2015


Court of Appeals of Georgia


203 Ga. App. 12; 416 S.E.2d 92; 1992 Ga. App. LEXIS 243; 103-22 Fulton County D. Rep. 11B



January 24, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 20, 1992. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages. Fayette Superior Court. Before Judge English.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a judgment from the Fayette Superior Court (Georgia), which granted a motion by defendants, city and its employee, for summary judgment dismissing plaintiff's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 civil rights action against defendants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was arrested without a warrant after an altercation with a city employee. He commenced a civil rights action, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, against defendants. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment dismissing plaintiff's § 1983 civil rights action. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing plaintiff's complaint. The court held the trial court correctly granted summary judgment to the city on the basis of sovereign immunity. The court held that plaintiff failed to allege a series of incidents of unconstitutional conduct suggesting the existence of a widespread practice that constituted a custom or usage approved by the city. The allegations in plaintiff's affidavit only alleged proof of a single incident of errant behavior, which did not constitute a sufficient basis for imposing liability on the city. Thus, the city was not liable for the negligent acts of a police officer, under Ga. Code Ann. § 36-33-3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment granting defendants' motion for summary judgment dismissing the injured party's § 1983 civil rights complaint.

 

1586 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Beasley v. State


No. A91A1446


Court of Appeals of Georgia


202 Ga. App. 349; 414 S.E.2d 663; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 1773



November 27, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 19, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Drug violation. Evans Superior Court. Before Judge Findley.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Evans Superior Court (Georgia), which denied his motion for a new trial following his conviction for selling cocaine.


OVERVIEW: On the same date defendant was indicted, a separate indictment was returned charging that defendant committed the offense of possessing cocaine with intent to distribute. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion for a new trial. The court rejected defendant's argument that a conviction of a second or subsequent offense within the contemplation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(d), mandating the imposition of a life sentence upon conviction of a second or subsequent offense for possessing cocaine with intent to distribute, was violative of the Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution. The court found no constitutional requirement that a defendant receive the benefit of rehabilitation before a life sentence for repeated conduct might be imposed. The Supreme Court of Georgia had rejected a similar constitutional attack on § 16-13-30. Defendant failed to elicit a ruling from the trial court on the statute's constitutionality; thus, it was not before the court for appellate review. Further, the court found that defendant opened the door to testimony of an undercover agent to relate the content of statements made to her by an informant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying defendant's motion for a new trial after his conviction for selling cocaine.

 

1587 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Padgett v. Klaus


No. A91A1042


Court of Appeals of Georgia


201 Ga. App. 399; 411 S.E.2d 126; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 1343



October 3, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Medical malpractice. Cobb State Court. Before Judge McDuff.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed the order of the Cobb State Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment to defendant physician in the patient's medical malpractice action, on the ground that the applicable period of limitation was not tolled by the alleged fraudulent acts of the physician and therefore the complaint was barred.


OVERVIEW: The patient had her leg broken in a car accident. When the cast was removed her leg was shorter than the other and the condition was only correctable by surgery. At the time of the accident and treatment the patient was a minor. The patient filed a medical malpractice action against the physician five years after the treatment. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the physician. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. The court found that the patient's attorney learned from the physician that the patient's short leg could only be corrected by surgery. The patient's physical symptoms were obvious when she was still being treated by the physician. The statute of limitation was not tolled by the physician's alleged fraud because the record contained nothing to suggest the patient was prevented from learning of the alleged negligence. Because the limitation period was not tolled by fraud, the two-year period of limitation which commenced running once the patient reached majority had expired long before she brought the action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

1588 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Rucks v. State


No. A91A1037


Court of Appeals of Georgia


201 Ga. App. 142; 410 S.E.2d 206; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 1267



September 6, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Drug violation. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Cauthorn.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a pro se appeal from the judgment of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of a second offense of the sale of cocaine under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30 and sentenced him to life imprisonment. Defendant claimed that the mandatory life sentence under the recidivist portion of the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(d) was not unconstitutional merely because a prosecutor had the same discretion whether or not to proceed under it as he had in any other criminal case. The court held that a prosecutor could selectively enforce any statute so long as he did not do based on race, religion, gender, or any other basis that violated Equal Protection principles. The court also held that the legislature had broad discretion to define crime and to determine the appropriate punishment. The court found that the drug problem was so serious that it provided a rational basis for the legislature to impose a mandatory life sentence for repeated drug sales. The court noted that Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. II (1983) and the Equal Protection Clause of the federal constitution were coextensive, so the state constitution did not require a different result. The court also ruled that the mandatory life sentence did not violate the Eighth Amendment prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. The court held that there was no statutory prerequisite as to a conviction that antedated the offense for which the accused was sentenced under § 16-13-30(d).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of second offense sale of cocaine and affirmed the mandatory life sentence.

 

1589 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Johnson v. State


No. A91A1090


Court of Appeals of Georgia


201 Ga. App. 88; 410 S.E.2d 189; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 1193



September 3, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Obstruction of officer. Hall State Court. Before Judge Gosselin.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the rulings of the Hall State Court (Georgia), which entered judgments of conviction and sentences on jury verdicts that defendant was guilty of public drunkenness and obstruction of a law enforcement officer. The charge of obstructing a law enforcement officer was predicated upon resistance to arrest for disorderly conduct under a statute subsequently declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The disorderly conduct statute was declared unconstitutional between the arrest and the trial. On appeal, the court held that an arrest was not unlawful within the common law right to resist, if the arrest was authorized by statute, although the statute was later declared unconstitutional. The court ruled that the validity of the arrest depended on the law as it existed at the time of the arrest and not as it was later declared. The court noted that it would not have been proper for the law enforcement police officer to take it upon himself to pass upon the validity of a statute and that it was the duty of the officer to enforce the law until repealed or held invalid by a court; and likewise, it was not the right of an individual to resist arrest on the basis of a contention that the law he allegedly was violating was unconstitutional or invalid for some other reason. On the public drunkenness charge, the court held that a strong smell of alcohol, demeanor, mannerisms, and an attitude indicative of intoxication were sufficient to support a conviction and that it was for the jury to judge the credibility of defendant's explanation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of public drunkenness and obstruction of a law enforcement officer.

 

1590 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Hall v. State


No. A91A0850


Court of Appeals of Georgia


201 Ga. App. 328; 411 S.E.2d 274; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 1337



September 3, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 27, 1991. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Obstruction of officer, etc. Clayton State Court. Before Judge Carbo.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Clayton State Court (Georgia), which convicted her of obstruction of a law enforcement officer, disorderly conduct, and driving with an expired license and improper taillights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to convict her of obstruction of a law enforcement agent and that her conviction for disorderly conduct had to be reversed. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions for obstruction of a law enforcement officer and for driving with an expired license and improper taillights but reversed her conviction for disorderly conduct. The court held that pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 40-8-7, and § 40-8-23 the evidence was clearly sufficient to show that the officer acted in the lawful discharge of his official duties when he stopped defendant's vehicle for the offense of driving an improperly equipped vehicle. A factfinder could have found that defendant's refusal to provide identification to the officer could have hindered the officer in the execution of the officer's duties. The court agreed with defendant that her conviction and sentence for the offense of disorderly conduct under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-39(3) had to be reversed because the statute that prohibited such conduct was declared unconstitutional prior to the judgment of conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for obstruction of a law enforcement officer and for driving with an expired license and improper taillights but reversed her conviction for disorderly conduct.

Harris v. State


No. A91A0490


Court of Appeals of Georgia


200 Ga. App. 841; 410 S.E.2d 123; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 1165



July 16, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 31, 1991. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Restitution. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Castellani.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) awarding restitution for auto theft in the amount of $ 2,296.30, on the grounds that a modification of his sentence by increasing the amount of restitution was invalid and an impermissible increase in his punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the trial court order that modified his sentence by increasing the amount of restitution originally set. Defendant was found guilty of stealing a car that was a rental car. The trial court originally set restitution at $ 600, but when the rental car company stated its damages the restitution amount was increased. Defendant claimed that the trial court's order was invalid because the attempted increase was ordered both after the term of court in which sentence initially was imposed and more than 60 days from the date sentence was imposed by the judge, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-1(a). Defendant also argued the order was invalid because it increased his punishment after he had commenced serving his sentence. The court affirmed the trial court order. The court found that the trial court had authority to modify the restitution order to include the rental company's damages. The court held that when error in determining the amount of damages was discovered, the proper procedure for correcting the error was to reopen the issue for further evidence and a new finding on the amount of damages, including the rental company's damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order that increased the amount of restitution that defendant was required to pay because the increase did not constitute an impermissible increase or enhancement of defendant's punishment.

Mays v. State


No. A91A0404


Court of Appeals of Georgia


200 Ga. App. 457; 408 S.E.2d 714; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 1058



July 1, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 15, 1991. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Drug violation. Bibb Superior Court. Before Judge Bell, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Bibb Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him for a second offense of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and sentenced him to life imprisonment pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(d).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to an offense that occurred on June 19, 2989. The offense was possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. He was sentenced to five years probation. On December 8, 1989, he was arrested on a charge of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and was found guilty. The trial court revoked defendant's probation, found him guilty of the June 19 offense, and in accordance with Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(d), regarding second offenses, imposed a sentence of life imprisonment for the June 19 offense. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by setting aside defendant's probation, adjudicating him guilty of the June 19 offense, and sentencing him accordingly because the evidence supporting defendant's conviction for the December 8 offense was sufficient to establish that defendant violated his probation. The evidence showed that defendant had possessed a plastic sandwich bag filled with crack cocaine and that defendant was carrying a beeper and large amounts of cash. The court held that defendant's conviction of the June 19 offense was a second conviction for a § 16-13-30(b) offense and that a life sentence was mandated by § 16-13-30(d).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant for a second offense of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and sentencing to life imprisonment.

Frost v. State


No. A91A0074


Court of Appeals of Georgia


200 Ga. App. 267; 407 S.E.2d 765; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 972



June 6, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 2, 1991. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Voluntary manslaughter. Washington Superior Court. Before Judge McMillan.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Washington Superior Court (Georgia), defendant was convicted of arson, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-7-60 (a), and of voluntary manslaughter, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-2 (a). Defendant shot her husband and then set fire to the trailer that they shared. She did not testify at trial, or call any witnesses. Through cross-examination, defendant attacked the credibility of the State witnesses, which included efforts to show inconsistencies.


OVERVIEW: The indictment charged defendant with "unlawfully" damaging by means of fire her husband's occupied dwelling house without the consent of her husband or of the lienholder. The court ruled that "unlawfully" in this instance meant as prohibited by Ga. Code Ann. § 16-7-60, encompassing both the intent to commit the proscribed act and the knowledge necessary to form that intent. Although the indictment did not recite the statutory section, the court found it obvious from her brief that defendant was unquestionably aware that she was charged with a violation of that section. The court found defendant's argument that the indictment did not apprise her of which of the two manners provided in Ga. Code Ann. § 16-2-1 was alleged not persuasive. The court found no violation of defendant's Miranda rights. Rejecting defendant's argument that the trailer was no one's home at the time of the fire, the court found that it was the marital home of the deceased and defendant. The court found no error in the trial court's quashing of defendant's subpoena to the State's crime laboratory personnel, or in the instructions given.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1594 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Hosp. Auth. v. Litterilla


Nos. A90A1553, A90A1814


Court of Appeals of Georgia


199 Ga. App. 345; 404 S.E.2d 796; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 490; 102-55 Fulton County D. Rep. 11B



March 8, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 28, 1991. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Governmental immunity. Fulton State Court. Before Judge Lambros.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated interlocutory appeal, defendant, county hospital authority (hospital), challenging the judgment of the Fulton State Court (Georgia), which found in favor of plaintiff injured parties. The hospital argued that the trial court erred in denying its motion for summary judgment because it was entitled to the defense of governmental immunity in the medical malpractice actions.


OVERVIEW: The injured parties filed medical malpractice actions against the hospital. The hospital filed motions for summary judgment in each action, and the motions were denied. The hospital filed interlocutory appeals. The court consolidated the appeals and reversed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the hospital was granted immunity from such tort actions under Ga. Const. art. VI, § V, para. I. The hospital was created and operated under the Hospital Authorities Law, Ga. Code Ann. § 31-7-71 et seq., under which the hospital was entitled to the defense of governmental immunity except to the extent there was an express statutory waiver of that immunity. The injured parties' claim that the hospital's reserve fund was a self insurance fund that would require such a waiver of the hospital's immunity was without merit, as was the claim that the malpractice actions could be construed as actions for breach of contract. The court noted that the power to "sue and be sued" meant only that a government entity had the status and capacity to enter the courts; it did not signify a waiver of sovereign immunity against suit.


OUTCOME: In the medical malpractice actions brought by the injured parties against the hospital, the court reversed the trial court's denial of the hospital's motion for summary judgment.

Harris v. State


No. A90A2300


Court of Appeals of Georgia


199 Ga. App. 457; 405 S.E.2d 501; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 515; 102-60 Fulton County D. Rep. 19B



March 8, 1991, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: D.U.I. Upson Superior Court. Before Judge English.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Upson Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of the offense of driving with an alcohol concentration of .12 grams or more, in violation of O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash the accusation on the ground that it was not prepared on a uniform traffic citation properly approved for use by the Commissioner of the Department of Public Safety and omitted required items. Defendant's class of license was omitted, and there was no space for commercial vehicle information. There was no notice that, pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 17-6-11, if defendant's license was surrendered in lieu of cash, a copy of the citation served as his temporary license. There was also testimony that the machine was periodically serviced.

Greenhill v. State


No. A90A1871


Court of Appeals of Georgia


199 Ga. App. 218; 404 S.E.2d 577; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 469; 102-37 Fulton County D. Rep. 16B



February 6, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied March 13, 1991. Rehearing dismissed March 22, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 450. Cert. applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Securities violations. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Hawkins, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Gwinnett Superior Court (Georgia), which entered his conviction for 13 counts of violation of the Georgia Securities Act of 1973.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for selling securities while neither he nor the security were registered, and for employing a device, scheme, or artifice to defraud in connection with the sale of securities in violation of Ga. Code Ann. §§ 10-5-3, 10-5-5, 10-5-12. Defendant contended, among other things, that the prosecution against him should have abated due to the repeal and reenactment of Ga. Code Ann. § 10-5-12. Affirming the conviction, the court held that: (1) the prosecution was not abated because there was a clear demonstration of legislative intent that prosecution of the conduct under the former law should not abate with the re-defining of the crime; (2) the burden of proving the applicability of exemptions under Ga. Code Ann. §§ 10-5-3, 10-5-5 was on defendant; (3) the indictment, proof, and jury instructions were sufficient on the issue of the willfulness of defendants actions; (4) defendant did not have a right to appointed counsel because he was not determined to be indigent; and (5) the prosecution was not barred by the statute of limitation because the four-year limitations period applicable to defendant's case did not include any period in which the crime was unknown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on 13 counts of violating the Georgia Securities Act of 1973.

Ranson v. State


No. A90A2118


Court of Appeals of Georgia


198 Ga. App. 659; 402 S.E.2d 740; 1991 Ga. App. LEXIS 258



February 5, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 22, 1991. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Attempted theft, etc. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Stark.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Gwinnett Superior Court (Georgia), in which he was convicted of attempted theft by taking of a motor vehicle, possession of tools for the commission of a crime, and giving a false name to a law enforcement officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury for attempting to steal a moving truck, and he appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the evidence was sufficient to authorize the jury to convict defendant on all three counts, and that: (1) the trial court properly denied defendant's motion for acquittal on the charge of possession of tools for the commission of crime since the position of the tools in the truck cab and a broken truck window indicated that the tools were used to break into the truck; (2) as the trial court's recharging of the jury on a certain issue was a correct statement of the law, there was no error in the trial court's denial of defendant's request to recharge on an incorrect principle of law or of defendant's request to be heard before the jury was recharged; (3) the introduction into evidence of a certified copy of defendant's prior conviction was sufficient to satisfy both the identity and similarity requirements for admission of independent crimes evidence; and (4) the sentence imposed was within the range authorized by Ga. Code Ann. § 16-4-6(b) and thus defendant's objections had to be addressed to the sentence review panel as provided in Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-6.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of attempted theft by taking of a motor vehicle, possession of tools for the commission of a crime, and giving a false name to a law enforcement officer.

OVERVIEW: Manufacturers of a watch brand filed a lawsuit in federal district court against defendant for selling counterfeit watches. Scott v. State


No. A90A1739


Court of Appeals of Georgia


198 Ga. App. 10; 400 S.E.2d 677; 1990 Ga. App. LEXIS 1537



December 5, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Child custody interference. Clayton State Court. Before Judge Benefield.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father sought review of the decision of the Clayton State Court (Georgia), which convicted the father of interfering with the custody of his minor daughter pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-45(b)(1)(A).


OVERVIEW: After the divorce, the father had visitation rights with the daughter. The father kept the child beyond the agreement because his truck broke down on two separate occasions. The trial court convicted the father of interfering with the custody of his minor daughter, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-45(b)(1)(A). On the father's appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court. The court determined that a defendant may not be held culpable under a criminal statute unless the act committed by the person clearly was in violation of the law, that the "any evidence rule" was unconstitutional in determining the question of the sufficiency of the evidence to support a conviction, that defendant was entitled to a reversal if upon the record no rational trier of fact could have found proof of guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, and that the undisputed evidence showed that defendant had retained the child beyond the authorized period only because of unavoidable vehicle breakdowns.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which had convicted the father.

 

1600 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Scroggins v. State


Nos. A90A1140, A90A1141, A90A1142, A90A1144, A90A1143


Court of Appeals of Georgia


198 Ga. App. 29; 401 S.E.2d 13; 1990 Ga. App. LEXIS 1555



November 5, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 6, 1990. Certiorari Applied For.


PRIOR HISTORY: Aggravated assault, etc. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge White.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cobb Superior Court (Georgia) entered judgments of conviction against the four defendants in a joint trial on various charges of affray and aggravated assault when one of the defendants, knowing that he was infected with acquired immunodeficiency syndrome (AIDS), bit a police officer. The defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendants were tried jointly on various charges arising out of biting a police officer during a domestic dispute. The defendants' motion to suppress the positive HIV test result was granted. The defendants were found guilty and sentence was imposed. On appeal, the defendants challenged the sufficiency of the evidence. The court found (1) that proof that the bite or saliva was a deadly weapon was irrelevant because the intent to commit a crime was the actionable conduct, (2) that the jury could infer malicious intent to murder because the defendant knew he had AIDS and his deliberate biting and injecting saliva into officer's bloodstream was wanton and reckless disregard for the transmission of AIDS, (3) that the defendant failed to show harm resulting from the denial of severance motions because there were no antagonistic defenses, confusion as to evidence and law was not created, and no evidence prejudicial to the misdemeanants was admitted against the aggravated assault defendant, and (5) that the defendant waived confidentiality in his medical records because he placed AIDS in issue by his conduct in committing an act linked to his having AIDS .


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction against the defendants for aggravated assault of a police officer.
